Zakat — Almsgiving

8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Meaning of 'Fi Sabil Allah' in Zakat
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'fi sabil Allah' as a Zakat recipient.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two competing Hanafi interpretations of 'fi sabil Allah' and identify the dalil that supports Imam Muhammad's view.

Core Idea
The term 'fi sabil Allah' in Zakat is disputed: Abu Yusuf sees a stranded mujahid; Muhammad sees a stranded pilgrim, each with textual proof.

In the Hanafi school, the eighth category of Zakat recipients is 'fi sabil Allah'. Its precise meaning has been a subject of debate between two giants of the school: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson unpacks their disagreement, the evidence each used, and the practical consequences for disbursing Zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term and its context
Recognize that 'fi sabil Allah' is one of the eight categories of Zakat recipients mentioned in Quran 9:60, and its interpretation is debated.
2
State Abu Yusuf's interpretation and his basis
Abu Yusuf argues it means a stranded mujahid, relying on the absolute (mutlaq) usage of the term.
He gives priority to the linguistic apparent meaning.
3
State Muhammad's interpretation and his basis
Muhammad argues it means a stranded hajj pilgrim, citing the hadith of a camel dedicated 'fi sabil Allah' that the Prophet instructed to be used for a pilgrim.
This is a dalil naqli that specifies the general term.
4
Compare the two views
Note the thamarah al-khilaf: Abu Yusuf would give to a mujahid in need; Muhammad would give to a pilgrim in need. Both agree the recipient must be needy at the time.
The dispute is about the specific type of traveler.
5
Recognize the broader Hanafi principle
The text states that Zakat is only for the poor (fuqara), so wealthy ghuzat are excluded. This is a common rule that both imams agree on.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللهِ مُنْقَطِعُ الْغُرَاةِ عِندَ أَبِى يُؤسف لأنَّهُ الْمُتَقَاهِمُ عِندَ الإطلاقِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ مُنقَطِعُ الْحَاجِّ لِمَا رُوِى أَنَّ رَجُلًا جَعَلَ بَعِيرًا لَهُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَأَمَرَهُ رَسُولُ اللهِ * أَنْ يَحْمِلُ عَلَيْهِ الْحَاجَ وَلَا يَصْرِفُ إِلَى أَغْنِيَاءِ الْغُرَاةِ عندنا لأنَّ الْمَصْرَفَ هُوَ الْفُقَرَاء
ترجمہ اور اللہ کی راہ میں ابو یوسف کے نزدیک وہ غازی جو مال سے منقطع ہوں، کیونکہ مطلق فی سبیل اللہ سے یہی مفہوم ہوتا ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک وہ حاجی لوگ جو اپنے مال سے منقطع ہوں ۔ کیونکہ روایت ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اپنا اونٹ فی سبیل اللہ کر دیا تھا۔ تو رسول اللہ نے اس کو حکم فرمایا کہ اس پر حاجیوں کو سوار کرے۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک مالدار غازیوں پر زکوۃ صرف نہ کی جائے گی کیونکہ زکوۃ کا مصرف فقراء ہی ہیں۔ تشریح مصارف زکوۃ کی چھٹی قسم فی سبیل اللہ ہے فی سبیل اللہ کی مراد میں اختلاف ہے چنانچہ امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ہے کہ فی سبیل اللہ سے مراد ایسے غازی ہیں جن کے گھر پر تو مال موجود ہے لیکن اس وقت سفر جہاد میں ان کے پاس مال نہیں ہے کیونکہ لفظ فی سبیل اللہ جب مطلق بولا جاتا ہے تو اس سے یہی معنی مفہوم ہوتے ہیں اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ فی سبیل اللہ سے مراد وہ حاجی ہے جس کے گھر پر تو مال موجود ہو مگر سفر حج میں اس کے پاس مال نہیں رہا اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اپنا اونٹ فی سبیل اللہ کر دیا تھا تو رسول اکرم نے
And in the cause of Allah: according to Abu Yusuf, the stranded ghuzat (mujahidun), because the absolute expression of fi sabil Allah gives this meaning. And according to Muhammad, the stranded hajj pilgrim, because it is narrated that a man dedicated his camel to the cause of Allah, and the Messenger of Allah commanded him to carry a hajj pilgrim on it. And according to us, Zakat is not given to wealthy ghuzat, because the recipient of Zakat is the poor. Explanation: The sixth category of Zakat expenditures is fi sabil Allah. There is disagreement on the intended meaning of fi sabil Allah. Imam Abu Yusuf said: fi sabil Allah means those ghazis (mujahidun) who have wealth at home but at the time of travel for jihad they do not have money with them, because when the word fi sabil Allah is used absolutely, this is the meaning understood. And Imam Muhammad said: fi sabil Allah refers to the hajj pilgrim who has wealth at home but has no money left during the hajj journey. The proof is that a man dedicated his camel to the cause of Allah, and the Messenger of Allah told him to let a hajj pilgrim ride on it.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the interpretation of 'fi sabil Allah' as a Zakat recipient. Abu Yusuf holds that it refers to a mujahid who is stranded without funds during jihad, even if he is wealthy at home. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it refers to a hajj pilgrim who runs out of funds during the pilgrimage, based on the hadith of the camel dedicated 'fi sabil Allah' and the Prophet's instruction to use it for a hajj pilgrim. Both views agree that the recipient must be in need at the time, and rich ghuzat are not eligible. The text also notes that the general Hanafi principle is that Zakat should go to the poor. The practical difference: according to Abu Yusuf, a stranded mujahid can receive Zakat; according to Muhammad, only a stranded pilgrim can. The mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated here.

Key Terms
فی سبیل اللہ (fī sabīl allāh): Literally 'in the cause of Allah'; as a Zakat recipient, interpreted by Hanafis as stranded mujahidun or stranded hajj pilgrims.
غازی (ghāzī): A warrior participating in jihad, especially one who is away from home and without funds.
حاجی (hājjī): A pilgrim performing Hajj, especially one who has run out of provisions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Imam Muhammad's interpretation of 'fi sabil Allah'?
A) The absolute usage of the term in the Quran.
B) The hadith of the camel dedicated to Allah's cause.
C) Qiyas on the category of travelers.
D) Consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The term 'fi sabil Allah' in Zakat is open to multiple valid interpretations within the Hanafi school, leading to a practical difference in who qualifies to receive Zakat.

Definition of Ghārim: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Defines ghārim and contrasts with Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ghārim and distinguish it from the Shafi'i definition, and explain the practical consequence of the difference.

Core Idea
The Hanafi ghārim is any debtor with insufficient wealth; the Shafi'i restricts it to reconciliation spenders, even if wealthy.

Among the eight categories of zakat recipients is al-ghārim, the debtor. However, the schools differ on who qualifies as a ghārim. This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi position as stated by al-Qudūrī and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view. Understanding this dispute clarifies when a debtor may legitimately receive zakat and when he may not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi definition
Read the first part of the passage: 'وَالْعَارِمُ مَنْ لَزِمَهُ دَيْنُ وَلَا يَمْلِكُ نِصَابًا فَاضِلًا عَنْ دَيْنِهِ'. Note that the condition is simply debt plus no surplus nisāb.
2
Identify the Shafi'i definition
Read the second part: 'وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ مَنْ تَحَمَّلَ غَرَامَةً فِي إِصْلَاحِ ذَاتِ الْبَيْنِ'. Note the restriction to reconciliation.
3
Examine the Hanafi response
The commentary explains that a reconciliation spender who becomes poor may receive zakat as faqīr, not as ghārim. So the Hanafi definition remains general.
Focus on the logical distinction: the reason for debt is irrelevant for the Hanafi school.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
A wealthy person who spends on reconciliation: according to Shafi'i, he may take zakat as ghārim; according to Hanafi, he may not, unless his wealth falls below nisāb.
This is the practical consequence of the definitional difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْعَارِمُ مَنْ لَزِمَهُ دَيْنُ وَلَا يَمْلِكُ نِصَابًا فَاضِلًا عَنْ دَيْنِهِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ مَنْ تَحَمَّلَ غَرَامَةً فِي إِصْلَاحِ ذَاتِ الْبَيْنِ وإطفاء النَّائِرَة بَيْنَ الْقَبِيلَتَينِ ترجمہ اور غارم وہ شخص ہے جس پر قرضہ لازم ہو اور اپنے قرضہ سے فاضل کسی نصاب کا مالک نہ ہو اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ غارم وہ ہے جس نے مسلمانوں کے درمیان باہمی پھوٹ کی اصلاح کی خاطر اور دو قبیلوں کے درمیان عداوت کی آگ کو بجھانے کے لئے مالی خسارہ برداشت کیا ہو۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری کے بیان کے مطابق مصارف زکوۃ کی پانچویں قسم غارم ہے غارم وہ شخص ہے جس کے ذمہ لوگوں کا قرضہ ہو ۔ اور قرضہ سے فاضل مقدار نصاب کا مالک نہ ہو ۔ مثلا ایک آدمی کے پاس ایک ہزار درہم ہوں اور وہ نوسو درہم کا مقروض ہو تو اس کو زکوۃ دینا جائز ہے کیونکہ نوسو درہم کے ساتھ قرض خواہوں کا حق متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ تو معدوم ہو گئے یعنی یہ نو سودرہم گویا اس کی ملک نہ رہے اور رہے ہو درہم تو وہ بقدر نصاب نہیں ہیں۔ اس لئے اس کے واسطے زکوۃ کا مال لینا جائز ہوگا ۔ امام شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ غارم وہ شخص ہے جس نے دو متحارب مسلم گروہوں کے درمیان صلح کرانے اور دشمنی کی آگ بجھانے کی خاطر کچھ مالی خسارہ برداشت کیا تو شخص اگر چہ مالدار ہو لیکن اس مقصد کے لئے زکوۃ لے سکتا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک یہ شخص زکوۃ نہیں لے سکتا ۔ ہاں اگر اصلاح بین الناس پر خرچ کرنے کے بعد مقدار نصاب کا مالک نہر ہا ہو تو لے سکتا ہے مگر یہ لینا غارم کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ فقیر یعنی مقدار نصاب کا مالک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے۔
And al-ghārim is the one upon whom is a debt and he does not possess a surplus of nisāb beyond his debt. Al-Shāfi‘ī said: the one who bears a pecuniary loss in mending relations and extinguishing the fire [of enmity] between two tribes. Translation: And al-ghārim is the person on whom a debt is obligatory and he does not own any nisāb surplus to his debt. Imām Shāfi‘ī stated that al-ghārim is the one who has borne a financial loss for the sake of reconciling between Muslims and extinguishing the fire of enmity between two tribes. Commentary: According to the statement of Ṣāḥib al-Qudūrī, the fifth category of the recipients of zakāh is al-ghārim. Al-ghārim is the person who owes a debt to people and does not own the amount of nisāb in surplus of the debt. For example, a person has one thousand dirhams and is in debt for nine hundred dirhams, then giving him zakāh is permissible because due to the right of the creditors being attached to the nine hundred dirhams, they are rendered nonexistent, i.e., these nine hundred dirhams are as if not his property, and the remaining one hundred dirhams are not to the extent of nisāb. Therefore, it is permissible for him to take zakāh wealth. Imām Shāfi‘ī says that al-ghārim is the person who has borne some financial loss for the sake of reconciling two warring Muslim groups and extinguishing the fire of enmity, so even if such a person is wealthy, he can take zakāh for this purpose. According to us, this person cannot take zakāh. Yes, if after spending on reconciliation he does not own nisāb, then he may take it, but this taking is not due to being ghārim but due to being faqīr, i.e., not owning nisāb.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute over the definition of ghārim (the debtor) among the eight categories of zakat recipients. The Hanafi position, based on the matn of al-Qudūrī, defines ghārim as a person who owes a debt and whose wealth after deducting the debt is less than nisāb. The debt is considered to consume an equivalent amount of his property, making him effectively poor. Imām al-Shafi‘i defines ghārim as one who incurs a liability for the sake of reconciliation between conflicting parties, even if he is wealthy. The Hanafi response clarifies that if such a reconciliation-spender becomes poor after spending, he receives zakat as a faqīr, not as a ghārim. Thus, the Hanafi definition of ghārim is strictly a debtor whose remaining wealth is below nisāb, regardless of the reason for the debt. The practical difference: according to Shafi‘i, a wealthy person can still take zakat for reconciliation; according to Hanafi, he cannot unless he is also poor.

Key Terms
غارم (ghārim): A person who owes a debt and does not own nisāb surplus to the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which condition must a debtor (ghārim) meet to be eligible for zakat?
A) He must have incurred the debt for reconciliation between Muslims.
B) His wealth after deducting the debt must be less than nisāb.
C) He must be a traveler away from his wealth.
D) He must have no family to support him.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines ghārim as any debtor whose net worth falls below nisāb, while the Shafi'i school restricts it to those who incur debt for reconciliation.

The Meaning of 'Fī Sabīl Allāh' in Zakat Distribution
Defines 'fī sabīl Allāh' and disputes among Hanafi imams and with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on giving zakat to wealthy fighters under 'fī sabīl Allāh', explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Zakat's category 'fī sabīl Allāh' is restricted to the needy; wealthy fighters cannot receive it.

The Qur'an specifies eight categories of zakat recipients, among them 'fī sabīl Allāh' (in the path of Allah). This term has been interpreted differently by the Hanafi imams and between madhhabs. The passage from al-Hidayah presents the views of Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad on its precise meaning, and then contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imām al-Shāfi‘ī regarding the eligibility of wealthy fighters. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how usul principles and hadith interpretation generate differing fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Recognise the views of Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad (intra-Hanafi), and the Shafi'i position on the meaning of 'fī sabīl Allāh' and who qualifies.
Abū Yūsuf: fighters cut off from wealth; Muḥammad: pilgrims cut off; Shafi'i: includes wealthy fighters.
2
Understand the Hanafi restriction
The Hanafi school holds that all zakat recipients must be poor. This is the founding principle that governs the interpretation of 'fī sabīl Allāh'.
Zakat is from the rich to the poor; transfer must be to those in need.
3
Examine Abū Yūsuf's proof
Abū Yūsuf argues that 'fī sabīl Allāh' conventionally means jihad, so it refers to fighters who are stranded and in need.
Based on customary understanding when used absolutely.
4
Examine Muḥammad's proof
Muḥammad cites a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ instructed a man to use his dedicated camel for pilgrims, indicating that 'fī sabīl Allāh' includes hajj.
The practical application supports pilgrims cut off from their funds.
5
Analyze the Shafi'i hadith and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school relies on a hadith that lists the fighter as an exception to the prohibition of charity for the wealthy. The Hanafi response reinterprets 'ghani' as one capable of earning, not one possessing nisab.
Thus, the fighter exception applies only when the fighter is not truly wealthy (i.e., he is poor).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللهِ مُنْقَطِعُ الْغُزَاةِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُتَفَاهِمُ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ مُنْقَطِعُ الْحَاجِّ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ رَجُلًا جَعَلَ بَعِيرًا لَهُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَأَمَرَهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَنْ يَحْمِلَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَاجَّ وَلَا يَصْرِفُ إِلَى أَغْنِيَاءِ الْغُزَاةِ عِنْدَنَا لِأَنَّ الْمَصْرَفَ هُوَ الْفُقَرَاءُ تَرْجَمَةٌ وَاللَّهِ الَّذِي وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ مُنْقَطِعُ الْغُزَاةِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُتَفَاهِمُ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ مُنْقَطِعُ الْحَاجِّ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ رَجُلًا جَعَلَ بَعِيرًا لَهُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَأَمَرَهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَنْ يَحْمِلَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَاجَّ وَعِنْدَنَا لَا يَصْرِفُ إِلَى أَغْنِيَاءِ الْغُزَاةِ لِأَنَّ الْمَصْرَفَ هُوَ الْفُقَرَاءُ تَرْجَمَةٌ وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ مُنْقَطِعُ الْغُزَاةِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُتَفَاهِمُ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ مُنْقَطِعُ الْحَاجِّ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ رَجُلًا جَعَلَ بَعِيرًا لَهُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَأَمَرَهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَنْ يَحْمِلَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَاجَّ وَعِنْدَنَا لَا يَصْرِفُ إِلَى أَغْنِيَاءِ الْغُزَاةِ لِأَنَّ الْمَصْرَفَ هُوَ الْفُقَرَاءُ وَالْغَازِي إِنْ كَانَ غَنِيًّا فَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ الزَّكَاةُ عِنْدَنَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَحِلُّ لِلْغَازِي الزَّكَاةُ وَإِنْ كَانَ غَنِيًّا لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ لَا تَحِلُّ الصَّدَقَةُ لِغَنِيٍّ إِلَّا لِخَمْسَةٍ الْغَازِي وَالْعَامِلُ وَالْغَارِمُ وَرَجُلٌ اشْتَرَاهَا بِمَالِهِ وَرَجُلٌ تَصَدَّقَ بِهَا عَلَى الْمِسْكِينِ فَأَهْدَاهَا الْمِسْكِينُ إِلَيْهِ تَرْجَمَةٌ وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ مُنْقَطِعُ الْغُزَاةِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُتَفَاهِمُ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ مُنْقَطِعُ الْحَاجِّ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ رَجُلًا جَعَلَ بَعِيرًا لَهُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَأَمَرَهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَنْ يَحْمِلَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَاجَّ وَعِنْدَنَا لَا يَصْرِفُ إِلَى أَغْنِيَاءِ الْغُزَاةِ لِأَنَّ الْمَصْرَفَ هُوَ الْفُقَرَاءُ وَالْغَازِي إِنْ كَانَ غَنِيًّا فَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ الزَّكَاةُ عِنْدَنَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَحِلُّ لِلْغَازِي الزَّكَاةُ وَإِنْ كَانَ غَنِيًّا لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ لَا تَحِلُّ الصَّدَقَةُ لِغَنِيٍّ إِلَّا لِخَمْسَةٍ الْغَازِي وَالْعَامِلُ وَالْغَارِمُ وَرَجُلٌ اشْتَرَاهَا بِمَالِهِ وَرَجُلٌ تَصَدَّقَ بِهَا عَلَى الْمِسْكِينِ فَأَهْدَاهَا الْمِسْكِينُ إِلَيْهِ تَرْجَمَةٌ وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ مُنْقَطِعُ الْغُزَاةِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُتَفَاهِمُ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ مُنْقَطِعُ الْحَاجِّ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ رَجُلًا جَعَلَ بَعِيرًا لَهُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَأَمَرَهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَنْ يَحْمِلَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَاجَّ وَعِنْدَنَا لَا يَصْرِفُ إِلَى أَغْنِيَاءِ الْغُزَاةِ لِأَنَّ الْمَصْرَفَ هُوَ الْفُقَرَاءُ وَالْغَازِي إِنْ كَانَ غَنِيًّا فَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ الزَّكَاةُ عِنْدَنَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَحِلُّ لِلْغَازِي الزَّكَاةُ وَإِنْ كَانَ غَنِيًّا لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ لَا تَحِلُّ الصَّدَقَةُ لِغَنِيٍّ إِلَّا لِخَمْسَةٍ الْغَازِي وَالْعَامِلُ وَالْغَارِمُ وَرَجُلٌ اشْتَرَاهَا بِمَالِهِ وَرَجُلٌ تَصَدَّقَ بِهَا عَلَى الْمِسْكِينِ فَأَهْدَاهَا الْمِسْكِينُ إِلَيْهِ
And fī sabīl Allāh [is] the one cut off from the fighters according to Abū Yūsuf because it is the understood [meaning] when absolutely mentioned, and according to Muḥammad, the one cut off from the pilgrims due to the narration that a man dedicated his camel fī sabīl Allāh and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ ordered him to carry the pilgrim on it. And we do not spend [zakāh] on wealthy fighters because the recipients [must be] the poor. Translation: And fī sabīl Allāh: according to Abū Yūsuf, it means the fighter who is cut off [from his wealth], because that is the understood meaning when the term is used absolutely. According to Muḥammad, it means the pilgrim who is cut off [from his wealth], because it is narrated that a man dedicated his camel fī sabīl Allāh and the Prophet ﷺ ordered him to carry a pilgrim on it. And according to us [Hanafis], zakāh is not to be given to wealthy fighters because the recipients are the poor. And Imām al-Shāfi‘ī said: it is permissible for a fighter to take zakāh even if he is wealthy, because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Charity is not permissible for a wealthy person except for five: the fighter, the collector, the debtor, the person who buys it with his money, and the person to whom a poor person gives it as a gift.'
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage discusses the meaning of 'fī sabīl Allāh' (in the path of Allah) as a zakat recipient category. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abū Yūsuf interprets it as the fighter (ghāzī) who is separated from his wealth and needs funds for jihad, while Muḥammad interprets it as the pilgrim (hājj) who is cut off from his wealth, based on a hadith where the Prophet directed a dedicated camel to be used for pilgrims. The author of al-Hidāyah notes that the Hanafi school does not permit giving zakat to wealthy fighters, as zakat is only for the poor. This leads to an inter-madhhab dispute with Imām al-Shāfi‘ī, who allows zakat for fighters even if they are wealthy, citing a hadith that lists a fighter among five categories for whom charity is permissible. The Hanafi response interprets 'ghani' in the hadith as one capable of earning, not one who actually owns nisāb; thus, the fighter is not wealthy in the sense of being a zakat-payer himself. The Hanafi position is that zakat is for the poor only, and fighters, if wealthy, should not receive it. The practical difference: according to Shafi‘i, a rich mujāhid can receive zakat; according to Hanafi, he cannot unless he is poor.

Key Terms
فی سبیل الله (fī sabīl Allāh): A category of zakat recipients; according to Hanafis, it refers to poor fighters or pilgrims who are cut off from their wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to a wealthy fighter (ghāzī) under the category 'fī sabīl Allāh'?
A) It is permissible because the hadith includes the fighter as an exception.
B) It is not permissible because zakat is solely for the poor.
C) It is permissible only if the fighter is on a pilgrimage.
D) It is permissible only if the fighter is cut off from his wealth but owns nisāb at home.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school strictly restricts 'fī sabīl Allāh' to needy individuals, excluding wealthy fighters, in contrast to the Shafi'i view.

Definition of Ibn al-Sabīl: The Wayfarer Eligible for Zakat
Defines ibn al-sabīl as a traveler away from his wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ibn al-sabīl and identify when a traveler qualifies for zakat.

Core Idea
A traveler with wealth at home but no cash during travel is considered poor and may receive zakat for immediate need only.

Allah mentions eight categories of zakat recipients in the Quran, including ibn al-sabīl (the wayfarer). This lesson clarifies the precise Hanafi definition: it is not any traveler, but one who is temporarily cut off from his wealth. Understanding this ensures zakat is distributed to those truly in need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that ibn al-sabīl is one of the eight zakat recipients in the Quran. The Hanafi school defines it specifically as a traveler who has wealth in his homeland but currently has no access to it.
2
Apply the condition
Determine if the traveler's wealth is in his homeland and he is in another place with nothing. If he has money with him, he does not qualify.
3
Understand the ruling
Such a traveler is considered temporarily poor (faqīr) at that moment, so it is permissible (jā'iz) to give him zakat, but only to the extent of his immediate need. Taking more is not permissible.
4
Note the recommendation
Scholars opine that it is better (afḍal) for him to take a loan and repay when he reaches his wealth, to preserve his dignity and avoid zakat if possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَابْنُ السَّبِيلِ مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ فِي وَطَنِهِ وَهُوَ فِي مَكَانٍ آخَرَ لَا شَيْءَ لَهُ فِيهِ تَرْجَمَةٌ وَابْنُ السَّبِيلِ وہ شخص کہ جس کا مال اس کے وطن میں ہو اور وہ خود ایسے مقام پر ہے کہ اس کے پاس یہاں کچھ نہیں ہے۔ تشریح ساتویں قسم ابن السبیل ہے۔ ابن سبیل سے مراد وہ مسافر ہے جس کے وطن میں اس کا بہت سا مال موجود ہے مگر اس وقت اس کے پاس کچھ نہیں ہے تو گویا یہ شخص فی الوقت فقیر ہوا اور فقیر کے لئے زکوۃ لینا جائز ہے مگر اس کے واسطے ضرورت سے زیادہ لینا حلال نہیں ہے علماء نے لکھا ہے کہ بہتر یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص قرضہ لے اور گھر جا کر ادا کر دے۔
And ibn al-sabīl is the one who has wealth in his homeland and he is in another place with nothing of it with him. Translation: And ibn al-sabīl is the person whose wealth is in his homeland and he himself is in a place where he has nothing. Commentary: The seventh category is ibn al-sabīl. Ibn al-sabīl refers to the traveler whose abundant wealth is in his homeland, but at the moment he has nothing with him. So such a person is temporarily poor, and it is permissible for a poor person to take zakat, but it is not permissible for him to take more than his need. Scholars have written that it is better for this person to take a loan and repay when he returns home.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement defining the seventh category of zakat recipients, ibn al-sabīl (wayfarer). The definition is: a person who has wealth in his homeland but is traveling and currently has no access to it. According to the Hanafi school, such a traveler is considered poor at that moment and thus eligible for zakat. However, he may only take what he needs for his immediate necessity, not more. The scholars recommend that he should take a loan instead of zakat if possible, and repay it when he returns to his wealth. This ruling is based on the principle of addressing immediate need while preserving the dignity of the recipient.

Key Terms
ابن السبیل (ibn al-sabīl): A traveler who has wealth at home but currently has no money with him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a traveler (ibn al-sabīl) eligible for zakat?
A) Because he is a traveler and all travelers can receive zakat.
B) Because he is temporarily poor, as his wealth is not accessible to him at that moment.
C) Because he is poor in his homeland as well.
D) Because he intends to use the zakat for a pilgrimage.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines ibn al-sabīl as a traveler with wealth at home but no cash in hand, making him temporarily poor and eligible for zakat only for his immediate needs.

Zakat Distribution: One Category or All Eight?
Ruling on whether zakat must be distributed to all eight categories or can be given to one

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on giving all zakat to one category, explain the linguistic basis for the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Zakat can be given entirely to one category; the Qur'anic categories are designations, not fixed shares.

When you pay zakat, do you need to divide it among all eight categories mentioned in the Qur'an, or can you give it all to the poor? This question has been debated between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The answer depends on how we understand the Arabic preposition 'lām' in the verse. This lesson unpacks the arguments and shows why Hanafis give flexibility to the payer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The dispute is whether the eight categories (jihāt) of zakat recipients are separate entitlements or simply examples of who may receive zakat.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the owner may give all zakat to a single category (e.g., all to the poor).
This is based on the view that the lām in the verse is for bayān (clarification), not istiḥqāq (entitlement).
3
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i requires distribution to all eight categories, with at least three individuals from each category.
He argues that the lām indicates each category has a right to a share.
4
Analyse the Hanafi dalīl
The Hanafi proof is that zakat is a right of Allah (ḥaqq Allāh), and the cause (ʿilla) for receiving it is poverty, not membership in a category. The lām simply designates appropriate recipients.
This is supported by the practice of ‘Umar and Ibn ‘Abbās.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi can give all zakat to one poor person; a Shafi'i must distribute among multiple categories and multiple individuals.
This affects how zakat is collected and distributed in Muslim communities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَهَذِهِ جِهَاتُ الزَّكَاةِ فَلِمَالِكٍ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ وَلَهُ أَنْ يَقْتَصِرَ عَلَى صِنْفٍ وَاحِدٍ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَصْرِفَ إِلَى ثَلَاثَةٍ مِنْ كُلِّ صِنْفٍ لِأَنَّ الْإِضَافَةَ بِحَرْفِ اللَّامِ لِلِاسْتِحْقَاقِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْإِضَافَةَ لِبَيَانِ أَنَّهُمْ مَصَارِفُ لَا لِإِثْبَاتِ الِاسْتِحْقَاقِ وَهَذَا لِمَا عُرِفَ أَنَّ الزَّكَاةَ حَقٌّ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى وَبِعِلَّةِ الْفَقْرِ صَارُوا مَصَارِفَ فَلَا يُبَالَى بِاخْتِلَافِ جِهَاتِهِ وَالَّذِي ذَهَبْنَا إِلَيْهِ مَرْوِيٌّ عَنْ عُمَرَ وَابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ تَرْجَمَةٌ مصنف نے کہا ہے کہ یہ زکوۃ کی راہیں ہیں پس مالک کو اختیار ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک کو دیدے اور اس کو یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ ایک ہی قسم پر اکتفا کرے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ ہر قسم کے تین تین آدمیوں کو دے اس لئے کہ لام حرف جر ہے استحقاق کے لئے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ اضافہ بیان کے لئے ہے کہ یہ لوگ مصارف ہیں استحقاق ثابت کرنے کے لئے نہیں اور یہ اس لئے کہ معلوم ہے کہ زکوۃ اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق ہے اور فقر کی علت سے یہ لوگ مصارف ہوئے ہیں پس اس کے جہات کے اختلاف کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا اور جس کی طرف ہم گئے ہیں وہ عمر اور ابن عباس سے مروی ہے۔
He said: These are the categories of zakāh; the owner may pay to each one of them, and he may restrict to one category. Al-Shāfi‘ī said: It is not permissible unless he gives to three from each category because the addition with the letter lām indicates entitlement. And we [argue] that the addition is to indicate that they are categories [masārif], not to establish entitlement; and this is because it is known that zakāh is a right of Allah, and by the cause of poverty they become recipients, so no attention is paid to the difference of their categories. And what we have gone to is narrated from ‘Umar and Ibn ‘Abbās. Translation: The author said: These are the pathways of zakāh; the owner has the choice to give to each one of them, and he also has the choice to restrict to a single category. Imām al-Shāfi‘ī said: It is not permissible unless he gives to three persons from each category, because the addition with the letter lām indicates entitlement. Our proof is that this addition is for indicating that they are recipients [masārif], not for establishing individual entitlement; and this is because it is known that zakāh is a right of Allah, and by the cause of poverty they have become recipients, so the difference of their categories is not considered. And that which we have adopted is narrated from ‘Umar and Ibn ‘Abbās.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the distribution of zakat among the eight categories mentioned in the Qur'an. The author (al-Qudūrī) states that the owner of wealth has the choice to give to each category or to restrict it to one category. Imām al-Shāfi‘ī argues that one must give to at least three individuals from each category, because the Arabic preposition 'lām' in 'lil-fuqarā'i wal-masākīni...' indicates entitlement of each category. The Hanafi response is that the 'lām' here merely indicates that these are the appropriate recipients (masārif) of zakat, not that each category has an individual claim. Zakat is fundamentally a right of Allah, and the reason (ʿilla) for making a person a recipient is poverty, regardless of which category they belong to. Therefore, if the owner gives all zakat to the poor (fuqarā'), that suffices. This view is supported by narrations from ‘Umar and Ibn ‘Abbās. The practical difference: according to Hanafis, one can give all zakat to one poor person; according to Shafi‘is, one must distribute among multiple categories and at least three individuals from each.

Key Terms
جهات الزکاة (jihāt al-zakāh): The eight categories of zakat recipients mentioned in the Qur'an.
إضافة بحرف اللام (iḍāfa bi-ḥarf al-lām): The grammatical construction using the preposition 'lām' to indicate ownership or entitlement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on giving all zakat to only one of the eight categories (e.g., all to the poor)?
A) It is not permissible; zakat must be distributed among all eight categories.
B) It is permissible, based on the view that the categories are merely designations of recipients.
C) It is permissible only if the other categories are not available in the area.
D) It is not permissible unless one gives to at least three from each category.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits giving all zakat to one category because the Qur'anic categories are examples of valid recipients, not fixed shares.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat Distribution: Hanafi vs. Shafi‘i on Single Category or All Eight
Hanafi vs Shafi‘i disagreement on distribution of zakat to recipient categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat distribution, explain the Hanafi proof from Arabic grammar, and compare it with the Shafi‘i position.

Core Idea
Zakat can be given to one category or one person; the eight categories are avenues, not entitled individuals.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools regarding how zakat must be distributed. The Quran lists eight categories of recipients, but does the owner have to give to all of them? The Hanafi school says no, while the Shafi‘i school requires distribution to at least three individuals from each category. We will explore the linguistic and legal reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that it is permissible to give zakat to any single category (e.g., only the poor) or even to one individual.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi‘i holds that zakat must be distributed to all eight recipient categories, with at least three individuals per category, totaling 21 recipients.
This is based on his interpretation of the Quranic verse.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi‘i evidence: the lam in 'lil-fuqara' indicates entitlement (istihqaq), the waw joining the categories obligates all to be included, and the plural form requires at least three per category.
These arguments are linguistic.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the lam indicates specificity (ikhtisas) to define avenues (masarif), not personal entitlement. The waw is merely coordinating, not imposing obligation. The plural form can refer to the generic plural, not necessarily three.
The underlying cause is need (faqr), which is common to all categories.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi allows all zakat to be given to one person; Shafi'i requires at least 21 recipients. This affects ease of distribution, especially when recipients are scarce.
The Hanafi view is supported by narrations from Umar and Ibn Abbas.

وَابْنُ سَبِيْلِ مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ مَالَ فِي وَطَيْهِ وَهُوَ فَى مَكَانِ اخَرَ لَاشَيْء لَهُ فِيهِ. ترجمہ اور ابن السبیل و مشخص کہ جس کا مال اس کے وطن میں ہو اور وہ خود ایسے مقام پر ہے کہ اس کے پاس یہاں کچھ نہیں ہے۔ تشریح ساتویں قسم ابن السبیل ہے۔ ابن سبیل سے مراد وہ مسافر ہے جس کے وطن میں اس کا بہت سا مال موجود ہے مگر اس وقت اس کے پاس کچھ نہیں ہے تو گویا یہ شخص فی الوقت فقیر ہوا اور فقیر کے لئے زکوۃ لینا جائز ہے مگر اس کے واسطے ضرورت سے زیادہ لینا حلال نہیں ہے علما ء نے لکھا ہے کہ بہتر یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص قرضہ لے اور گھر جا کر ادا کر دے۔
مذکورہ بالا مصارف زکوۃ ہیں مستحق زکوۃ نہیں
قَالَ هذه جَهَاتُ الزَّكَوةِ فَلِمَا لِي أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلى كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ وَلَهُ أَنْ يَقْتَصِرَ عَلَى صِنْفِ وَاحِدٍ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَصْرِفَ إِلَى ثَلَثَةٍ مِنْ كُلّ صِنْفٍ لِأَنَّ الإِضَافَةَ بِحَرْفِ اللَّامِ لِلاسْتِحْقَاقِ. وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْإِضَافَةَ لبَيَانِ أَنَّهُمْ مَصَارِفٌ لا لإثْبَاتِ الإِسْتِحْقَاقِ وَ هَذَا لِمَا عُرِفَ أَنَّ الزَّكَوةَ حَقٌّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَبِعِلَّةِ الْفَقْرِ صَارُوا مَصَارِفَ فَلَايُبَالِى بِاخْتِلَافِ جِهَاتِهِ وَالَّذِى ذَهَبْنَا إِلَيْهِ مَروِيٌّ عَنْ عُمَرَ وَابْن عَبَّاسِ. ترجمہ مصنف نے کہا ہے کہ یہ زکوۃ کی راہیں ہیں پس مالک کو اختیار ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک کو دیدے اور اس کو یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ ایک ہی قسم پر اکتفاء کرے اور امام شافعی نے کہا ہے کہ جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ ہر قسم کے تین افراد پر صرف کی جائے کیونکہ حرف لام کے ساتھ اضافت استحقاق کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اضافت اس بات کو بیان کرنے کے لئے ہے کہ مذکورہ اقسام مصارف زکوۃ ہیں نہ کہ استحقاق ثابت کرنے کی اسطے اور یہ چونکہ معلوم ہو چکا ہے کہ زکوۃ اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق ہی اور علت فقر کی وجہ سے مذکورہ اقسام مصارف ٹھہرے ہیں تو جہت فقر کے مختلف ہونے کی طرف توجہ نہ کی جائے گی اور یہ مذہب جس کی طرف ہم گئے حضرت عمر اور ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہم سے مروی ہے۔ تشریح مذکورہ ساتوں قسم کے لوگ ہمارے نزدیک زکوۃ کا مصرف ہیں زکوۃ کے مستحق نہیں ہیں۔ چنانچہ مالک مال اگر ان اقسام میں سے ہر ایک کو دیدے تب بھی جائز ہی اور اگر پوری زکوۃ ایک ہی قسم کے لوگوں کو دیدے یا ایک ہی آدمی کو دیدے تب بھی جائز ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ یہ ساتوں قسم کے لوگ زکوۃ کے مستحق ہیں۔ لہذا ساتوں اقسام میں سے ہر قسم کے تین تین افراد کو زکوۃ دینا ضروری ہوگا گویا امام شافعی کے نزدیک اگر ہر قسم کے تین تین افراد کوز کو دی گئی جن کی مجموعی تعدا دا کیس ہوتی ہے تو زکوۃ ادا ہوگی ور نہ نہیں ۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے مصارف زکوۃ کو بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ الاية عن صدقات کو فقراء کی طرف لام کے واسطے سے مضاف کیا گیا ہے اور باقی چھ قسمیں واؤ کی ساتھ اس پر معطوف ہیں اور لام آتا ہے استحقاق کے لئے اور واؤ جمعیت پر دلالت کرتا ہے تو اب مطلب یہ ہوا کہ یہ ساتوں قسمیں زکوۃ کی حقدار ہیں اور جب ساتوں قسمیں حقدار ٹھہریں تو ساتوں کو دینا ضروری ہوا اور ان ساتوں اقسام کو بصیغہ جمع ذکر کیا گیا ہے اور جمع کا اطلاع کم از کم تین پر ہوتا ہے تو گویا ہر قسم میں سے تین تین افراد کو ز کوۃ دینا ضروری ہوا۔ پس حضرت امام شافعی کے نزدیک مالک مال نے اگر ساتوں اقسام میں سے ہر قسم کے تین تین افراد کو زکوۃ دی تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی ورنہ ادا نہ ہوگی۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ لِلْفُقَراء کا لام اختصاص کے لئے ہے نہ کہ استحقاق کے لئے یعنی صدقات کا مصرف فقط یہ سات اقسام ہیں ان کے علاوہ نہیں ہے ان میں سے جس کو بھی صدقہ دیا جائے گا اپنے مصرف میں صرف ہو گا یہ مطلب نہیں ہے کہ یہ ساتوں اقسام صدقات کی حقدار ہیں جب تک سب کو نہیں دیا جائے گا صدقہ ادا نہیں ہوگا اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ در حقیقت اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق ہے اور علت فقر اور محتاجی کی وجہ سے یہ لوگ مصارف ہو گئے کیونکہ اللہ عزاسمہ غنی ہے اس کو کسی چیز کی حاجت نہیں ہے پس جب زکوۃ کا مصرف ہونے کی علت فقر اور محتاجی ہے تو محتاجی کی جہات مختلف ہونے کی طرف التفات نہ کیا جائے گا یعنی محتاجی بہت فقر ہو یا بہت مسکنت یا بہت غرامت بہت مسافرت ہو ان کا لحاظ نہ کیا جائے گا بلکہ جہاں بھی محتاجی پائی جائے گی وہی زکوۃ کا مصرف ہوگا یہی مذہب حضرت عمر اور حضرت ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالی عنہم کا ہے چنانچہ طبرانی میں اس آیت کی تفسیر میں مروی ہے عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى أَنَّهَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ الآية، قَالَ فِى أيّ صِفٍ وَضَعْتَهُ اَجْزَاكَ یعنی ابن عباس نے إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَات کی تفسیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ جس قسم کو بھی تو دے گاز کو ۃ ادا ہو جائے گی اور حضرت عمر سے مروی ہے قَالَ أَيْمَا صِنفٍ أَعْطَيْتَهُ مِنْ هَذَا أَجْزَ اعَنكَ حضرت عمر فرمایا کہ جس قسم کو بھی زکوۃ دے گا کافی ہو جائے گا۔
And the wayfarer: one who has wealth in his homeland and is in another place where he has nothing. Explanation: The seventh category is ibn al-sabil (wayfarer). Ibn al-Sabil refers to a traveler who has abundant wealth in his homeland but has nothing with him at that time. So he is effectively a faqir at the moment, and taking zakat is permissible for a faqir, but taking more than his need is not permissible. Scholars have written that it is better for such a person to take a loan and repay it when he returns home.
The above are the avenues (masarif) of zakat, not the entitled ones (mustahiqun).
He (al-Quduri) said: These are the avenues of zakat. So he (the owner) has the option to give to each one of them, and he has the option to confine himself to one category. And al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible unless he distributes to three from every category, because the idafah (genitive construction) with the letter lam indicates entitlement (istihqaq). For us (Hanafis): The idafah is only to indicate that they are avenues (masarif), not to establish entitlement. This is because it is known that zakat is a right of Allah the Exalted, and due to the cause of need (faqr) they have become avenues, so the variation in their specific sub-types (jihaat) is not considered. And the view we have adopted is narrated from Umar and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). Translation: The author said: These are the avenues of zakat; the owner has the option to give to each of them, and he also has the option to restrict to a single category. Imam al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible unless it is spent on three from each category, because the idafah with the letter lam indicates entitlement. And our evidence is that the idafah is to explain that the mentioned categories are avenues (masarif) of zakat, not to establish entitlement. And this is because it is already known that zakat is a right of Allah the Exalted, and due to the cause of need, the mentioned categories have become avenues; so the variation in the type of need is not considered. And this madhhab that we have adopted is narrated from Umar and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). Explanation: According to us, the seven categories of people are avenues (masarif) of zakat, not the entitled ones (mustahiqun). Thus, if the owner gives to each of these categories, it is valid; and if he gives the entire zakat to one category, or even to one person, it is also valid. Imam al-Shafi'i said that these seven categories are entitled to zakat, so it is necessary to give to three individuals from each of the seven categories. So according to al-Shafi'i, if the owner gives to three individuals from each of the seven categories (totaling twenty-one individuals), then the zakat is discharged; otherwise not.
Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that Allah the Exalted, when mentioning the avenues of zakat, said: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor...' (ayah). The charities are added to the poor by means of the letter lam, and the remaining six categories are co-ordinated by the letter waw. And the lam indicates entitlement, and the waw indicates joining and collectivity. So the meaning becomes that these seven categories are entitled to zakat. And since they are entitled, it becomes necessary to give to all seven. And these seven categories are mentioned in the plural form, and the plural implies at least three. Therefore, it is necessary to give to three individuals from each category. So according to Imam al-Shafi'i, if the owner gives to three individuals from each of the seven categories, the zakat is discharged; otherwise not.
Our evidence is that the lam in 'lil-fuqara' is for specificity (ikhtisas), not for entitlement. That is, the avenues (masarif) of charity are only these seven categories; there is no other. Whichever of them charity is given to, it will be spent in its correct avenue. The meaning is not that these seven categories are entitled such that until all are given, the charity is not discharged. The reason is that zakat is actually a right of Allah the Exalted, and due to the cause of need and poverty, these people have become avenues. Because Allah, the Exalted, is free of need, He does not need anything. So when the cause of being an avenue of zakat is need, then the variation in the specific type of need (whether it is extreme poverty, moderate poverty, debt, or travel) is not considered. Rather, wherever need is found, that is an avenue of zakat. This is the view of Umar and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). It is narrated in al-Tabarani regarding the interpretation of this verse: 'Ibn Abbas, in his commentary on the verse 'Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy...', said: Whichever category you place it, it will suffice you.' That is, Ibn Abbas said in the interpretation of 'Indeed the charities' that whichever category you give, the zakat will be discharged. And it is narrated from Umar that he said: 'Whichever category you give from these, it will suffice you.'
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the distribution of zakat among the eight categories of recipients mentioned in the Quran (Surah al-Tawbah 9:60). The Hanafi position, as stated in the text, is that zakat is a right of Allah, and the cause of being a valid recipient is need (faqr). Therefore, the categories are merely avenues (masarif) for spending zakat, not individuals who are personally entitled. Consequently, the owner of wealth may give all of his zakat to a single category, or even to a single person, and it is valid. The Shafi'i position is that the lam ('l') in 'lil-fuqara' indicates entitlement (istihqaq), and the waw joining the categories implies that all must be given. Further, the plural form of each category requires at least three recipients per category. Thus, a total of 21 recipients (3 from each of the 7 categories) is necessary for zakat to be discharged. The text then provides the Shafi'i evidence and the Hanafi response. The Hanafi respond by explaining that the lam indicates specificity (ikhtisas), not entitlement. The purpose of the verse is to define the categories among which zakat may be spent, not to obligate distribution to each. Moreover, the underlying cause is need, and need is the same regardless of the specific category. The Hanafi view is supported by narrations from Umar and Ibn Abbas, who both held that giving to any single category is sufficient. The passage also includes the ruling on ibn al-sabil (wayfarer): a traveler who has wealth at home but is currently in need may receive zakat to cover his immediate needs, but it is better for him to take a loan instead.

Key Terms
مصارف (masarif): The avenues or channels through which zakat is to be spent; the categories of recipients.
استحقاق (istihqaq): The state of being entitled to something; here, entitlement to receive zakat as a right.
ابن سبیل (ibn al-sabil): A traveler who is cut off from his wealth and is in need during his journey.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum number of individuals to whom zakat must be given?
A) At least one from each of the eight categories
B) At least three from each category
C) One individual suffices
D) At least eight individuals

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits giving all zakat to a single category or person; the eight categories are merely avenues for spending.

Zakat Distribution: One Category or All Eight?
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on distribution of zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that zakat may be given to a single category and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument requiring distribution to all eight categories with at least three individuals each.

Core Idea
The Quranic categories are channels, not entitled recipients; giving zakat to one suffices.

In this lesson, we examine a classic inter-madhhab dispute: must zakat be distributed to all eight categories mentioned in Quran 9:60, or may it be concentrated on one? The Hanafi school holds that the categories are permissible channels (masārif), not entitled recipients (mustaḥiqqūn). Imam al-Shafi‘i, however, regards them as entitled, requiring distribution to all eight with a minimum of three individuals per category. Understanding the linguistic and legal reasoning behind this difference is key to appreciating how each school derives rulings from the same divine text.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: it is permissible to give all zakat to one category (or even one individual) from the eight categories mentioned in the Quran.
This is the muftā bihī position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the Shafi‘i position: it is obligatory to distribute zakat to all eight categories, and each category must receive at least three individuals.
Imam al-Shafi‘i bases this on the interpretation of the particle lām and the plural form.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi‘i evidence: the lām in 'lil-fuqarā'' indicates entitlement (istiḥqāq), the wāw for conjunction requires all categories, and the plural form (جمع) implies at least three.
This is a linguistic argument rooted in Arabic grammar.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the lām indicates specification (ikhtiṣāṣ) of channels, not entitlement. The cause (ʿillah) for spending is need (ḥājah), so any aspect of need suffices. This is supported by narrations from ʿUmar and Ibn ʿAbbās.
The Hanafi usul principle that ‘al-ʿillah al-muʿarrifah’ (the discerning cause) is key.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf
Identify the practical difference: under the Hanafi view, giving all zakat to one poor person is valid; under the Shafi‘i view, it is invalid unless all eight categories receive at least three individuals each.
This affects how zakat is distributed in practice, especially when resources are limited.

كہ ایک ہی قسم پر اکتفاء کرے اور امام شافعی نے کہا ہے کہ جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ ہر قسم کے تین افراد پر صرف کی جائے کیونکہ حرف لام کے ساتھ اضافت استحقاق کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اضافت اس بات کو بیان کرنے کے لئے ہے کہ مذکورہ اقسام مصارف زکوۃ ہیں نہ کہ استحقاق ثابت کرنے کے لئے اور یہ چونکہ معلوم ہو چکا ہے کہ زکوۃ اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق ہے اور علت فقر کی وجہ سے مذکورہ اقسام مصارف ٹھہرے ہیں تو جہات فقر کے مختلف ہونے کی طرف توجہ نہ کی جائے گی اور یہ مذہب جس کی طرف ہم گئے حضرت عمر اور ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہم سے مروی ہے۔ تشریح مذکورہ ساتوں قسم کے لوگ ہمارے نزدیک زکوۃ کا مصرف ہیں زکوۃ کے مستحق نہیں ہیں۔ چنانچہ مالک مال اگر ان اقسام میں سے ہر ایک کو دیدے تب بھی جائز ہے اور اگر پوری زکوۃ ایک ہی قسم کے لوگوں کو دیدے یا ایک ہی آدمی کو دیدے تب بھی جائز ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ یہ ساتوں قسم کے لوگ زکوۃ کے مستحق ہیں۔ لہذا ساتوں اقسام میں سے ہر قسم کے تین تین افراد کو زکوۃ دینا ضروری ہوگا گویا امام شافعی کے نزدیک اگر ہر قسم کے تین تین افراد کو زکوۃ دی گئی جن کی مجموعی تعداد اکیس ہوتی ہے تو زکوۃ ادا ہوگی ورنہ نہیں۔

امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے مصارف زکوۃ کو بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ... الآية، ان صدقات کو فقراء کی طرف لام کے واسطے سے مضاف کیا گیا ہے اور باقی چھ قسمیں واو کے ساتھ اس پر معطوف ہیں اور لام آتا ہے استحقاق کے لئے اور واو جمعیت پر دلالت کرتا ہے تو اب مطلب یہ ہوا کہ یہ ساتوں قسمیں زکوۃ کی حقدار ہیں اور جب ساتوں قسمیں حقدار ٹھہریں تو ساتوں کو دینا ضروری ہوا اور ان ساتوں اقسام کو بصیغہ جمع ذکر کیا گیا ہے اور جمع کا اطلاق کم از کم تین پر ہوتا ہے تو گویا ہر قسم میں سے تین تین افراد کو زکوۃ دینا ضروری ہوا۔ پس حضرت امام شافعی کے نزدیک مالک مال نے اگر ساتوں اقسام میں سے ہر قسم کے تین تین افراد کو زکوۃ دی تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی ورنہ ادا نہ ہوگی۔

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ کا لام اختصاص کے لئے ہے نہ کہ استحقاق کے لئے یعنی صدقات کا مصرف فقط یہ سات اقسام ہیں ان کے علاوہ نہیں ہے ان میں سے جس کو بھی صدقہ دیا جائے گا اپنے مصرف میں صرف ہو گا، یہ مطلب نہیں ہے کہ یہ ساتوں اقسام صدقات کی حقدار ہیں جب تک سب کو نہیں دیا جائے گا صدقہ ادا نہیں ہوگا۔ اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ در حقیقت اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق ہے اور علت فقر اور محتاجی کی وجہ سے یہ لوگ مصارف ہو گئے کیونکہ اللہ عزاسمہ غنی ہے اس کو کسی چیز کی حاجت نہیں ہے۔ پس جب زکوۃ کا مصرف ہونے کی علت فقر اور محتاجی ہے تو محتاجی کی جہات مختلف ہونے کی طرف التفات نہ کیا جائے گا یعنی محتاجی بہت فقر ہو یا بہت مسکنت یا بہت غرامت یا بہت مسافرت ہو، ان کا لحاظ نہ کیا جائے گا بلکہ جہاں بھی محتاجی پائی جائے گی وہی زکوۃ کا مصرف ہوگا۔ یہی مذہب حضرت عمر اور حضرت ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہم کا ہے۔ چنانچہ طبرانی میں اس آیت کی تفسیر میں مروی ہے عن ابن عباس في قوله تعالى إنما الصدقات للفقراء والمساكين الآية، قال في أي صنف وضعته أجزاك یعنی ابن عباس نے إنما الصدقات کی تفسیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ جس قسم کو بھی تو دے گا زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی۔ اور حضرت عمر سے مروی ہے قال أيما صنف أعطيته من هذا أجزأ عنك، حضرت عمر نے فرمایا کہ جس قسم کو بھی زکوۃ دے گا کافی ہو جائے گا۔
That one may be content with one category, and Imam Shafi'i said it is not permissible unless it is spent on three individuals from each category because the particle 'lam' in the construction indicates entitlement. Our evidence is that the construction is to state that the mentioned categories are the channels of zakat, not to prove entitlement. And since it has become known that zakat is a right of Allah Almighty and the cause is poverty, the mentioned categories are channels, so attention will not be paid to the different aspects of poverty. This school that we follow is narrated from Umar and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). Explanation: The seven categories of people are, according to us, the channels (masrif) of zakat, not entitled (mustahiqq). So if the owner gives to each of these categories it is permissible, and if he gives all the zakat to one category or to one person, it is also permissible. Imam Shafi'i said that these seven categories are entitled to zakat. Therefore, it is obligatory to give zakat to three individuals from each category. Thus, according to Imam Shafi'i, if the owner gives to three individuals from each of the seven categories, totaling twenty-one, then zakat is discharged, otherwise not.

Imam Shafi'i's evidence: Allah Almighty said in explaining the channels of zakat: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy...' (the verse). The charities are annexed to the poor by the particle 'lam', and the remaining six categories are conjoined to it by 'waw'. 'Lam' indicates entitlement, and 'waw' indicates aggregation. So the meaning is that these seven categories are entitled to zakat. And when they are entitled, it is obligatory to give to all seven. And these seven categories are mentioned in plural form, and the plural implies at least three. So it is obligatory to give to three individuals from each category. Thus, according to Imam Shafi'i, if the owner gives zakat to three individuals from each of the seven categories, the zakat is discharged, otherwise not.

Our evidence: The 'lam' in 'lil-fuqara'' is for specification, not entitlement. That is, the channels of charities are only these seven categories, not others. Whichever of them is given charity, it will be spent in its channel. It does not mean that these seven categories are entitled such that zakat is not discharged until all are given. The reason is that zakat is essentially a right of Allah Almighty, and the cause for these people being channels is poverty and need, because Allah is Self-Sufficient, in no need. So when the cause for being a channel of zakat is poverty and need, attention will not be paid to different aspects of need—whether it is extreme poverty (faqr), neediness (maskanah), debt (gharamah), or travel (safr). Rather, wherever need is found, that is a channel of zakat. This is the school of Umar and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). Thus, in Tabarani, it is narrated in tafsir of this verse: From Ibn Abbas concerning the saying of Allah 'Innama al-sadaqatu lil-fuqara'i wal-masakini...' (the verse), he said: 'Whatever category you place it, it suffices you.' That is, Ibn Abbas said in tafsir of 'Innama al-sadaqat' that whichever category you give, zakat will be discharged. And from Umar it is narrated: He said: 'Whichever category you give from this, it will suffice you.' Umar said: Whichever category you give zakat, it will be sufficient.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding the distribution of zakat among the eight categories (asnaf) mentioned in Quran 9:60. The Hanafi position is that these categories are channels (masarif) for spending zakat, not entitled recipients (mustahiqqun) in the sense that each category must receive a share. Therefore, the zakat payer may give the entire zakat to one category, or even to one individual, and the zakat will be validly discharged. Imam Shafi'i holds that the eight categories are entitled (mustahiqqun) to zakat, and the payer must distribute to all eight categories, giving at least three individuals from each category, since the plural form implies a minimum of three. The Hanafi evidence is based on: (1) the linguistic argument that the lam in 'lil-fuqara'' indicates specification (ikhtisas) of the categories as permissible channels, not entitlement (istihqaq); (2) the substantive reasoning that zakat is a right of Allah, and the cause for spending is need (hajah), not the specific category; therefore, the variation in the types of need does not affect the validity of the payment. This is supported by narrations from Umar and Ibn Abbas. The passage first states the ruling, then presents the Shafi'i view and evidence, then gives the Hanafi response with its evidence, including the linguistic analysis and the reports from the Companions.

Key Terms
مصارف (masārif): Channels or categories for spending zakat; the eight categories mentioned in the Quran.
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): Entitlement; the quality of being legally entitled to receive zakat as a right.
لام (lām): The Arabic particle 'li' used in the verse for zakat categories; its meaning is debated between ikhtisas (specification) and istihqaq (entitlement).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Shafi'i, what is the minimum number of individuals that must be given zakat from each category?
A) One individual per category
B) Two individuals per category
C) Three individuals per category
D) No minimum requirement

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits giving all zakat to one category because the Quranic categories are channels, not entitled recipients, and the cause for spending is need.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Giving Zakat and Other Charity to a Dhimmi
Ruling on charity to a dhimmi with evidence and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat and other charity to a dhimmi, identify the evidence for each, and explain the difference with the Shafi'i/Maliki position.

Core Idea
Zakat to a dhimmi is haram; other charity is halal — the general hadith is specified by Mu'adh's hadith.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: can a Muslim give zakat or other charity to a dhimmi (a protected non-Muslim citizen)? The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction between zakat and other forms of sadaqah, based on the Prophet's instructions to Mu'adh ibn Jabal and a general hadith encouraging charity to all people. We will trace the evidence, the opposing views, and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two-part ruling: zakat to dhimmi is not permissible; other charity (obligatory and voluntary) is permissible.
Note the distinction between zakat (pillar) and sadaqah (general charity).
2
Identify the evidence for each part
Locate the hadith of Mu'adh (for zakat prohibition) and the general hadith 'Give charity to people of all religions' (for permissibility of other charity). Understand how each hadith is used.
The specific hadith restricts zakat to Muslims; the general hadith permits other charity.
3
Follow the opposing school's argument
Understand that al-Shafi'i (and a narration from Abu Yusuf) hold all charity to a dhimmi is prohibited, using analogy (qiyas) from zakat.
The opposing evidence is purely analogical, not textual.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the opposition
Explain why the Hanafi school rejects the analogy: the prohibition of zakat is based on a specific text, not a general illa, so it cannot be extended to other charities.
The general hadith overrides the analogy for non-zakat charity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Contrast the Hanafi result (zakat invalid to dhimmi, other charity valid) with the Shafi'i/Maliki result (any charity to dhimmi invalid).
This difference affects real-life distribution of zakat funds and optional charity.

ذمی کوزکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں

وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ الزَّكَاةَ إِلَى ذِمِّيٍّ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِمُعَاذٍ خُذْهَا مِنْ أَغْنِيَائِهِمْ وَرُدَّهَا فِي فُقَرَائِهِمْ وَيَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ مَا سِوَى ذَلِكَ مِنَ الصَّدَقَةِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يَدْفَعُ وَهُوَ رِوَايَةٌ عَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ اعْتِبَارًا بِالزَّكَاةِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ تَصَدَّقُوا عَلَى أَهْلِ الْأَدْيَانِ كُلِّهَا وَلَوْلَا حَدِيثُ مُعَاذٍ لَقُلْنَا بِالْجَوَازِ فِي الزَّكَاةِ

ترجمہ: اور کسی ذمی کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت معاذ کو فرمایا تھا کہ زکوۃ کو ان مسلمانوں کے مالداروں سے لے اور ان کے فقیروں میں پھیر دے۔ اور ذمی کو اس کے علاوہ ہر صدقہ دینا جائز ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ نہ دے، اور یہی ایک روایت ابو یوسف سے ہے، زکوۃ پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے: تمام دین والوں کو صدقہ دو۔ اگر معاذ کی حدیث نہ ہوتی تو ہم زکوۃ میں بھی جواز کے قائل ہوتے۔

تشریح: ذمی کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ دلیل ابن عباس کی حدیث ہے: أن رسول الله بعث معاذا إلى اليمن فقال: إنك تأتي قوما أهل الكتاب فادعهم إلى شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأني رسول الله، فإن هم أطاعوك لذلك فأعلمهم أن الله فرض عليهم خمس صلوات في كل يوم وليلة، فإن هم أطاعوك لذلك فأعلمهم أن الله افترض عليهم صدقة في أموالهم تؤخذ من أغنيائهم وترد على فقرائهم، فإن هم أطاعوك لذلك فإياك وكرائم أموالهم، واتق دعوة المظلوم فإنه ليس بينها وبين الله حجاب. (شرح نقایہ بحوالہ کتب سنہ) یعنی ابن عباس سے مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حضرت معاذ کو یمن کا قاضی بنا کر بھیجا تو فرمایا: تم ایک اہل کتاب کی قوم کے پاس جا رہے ہو، ان کو کلمہ شہادت کی دعوت دینا، اگر وہ اس بارے میں تیری فرمانبرداری کر لیں تو ان کو بتلا دینا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ان پر ایک دن رات میں پانچ نمازیں فرض کی ہیں، اور اگر وہ اس بارے میں بھی تیری اطاعت کر لیں تو ان کو باخبر کر دینا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ان پر زکوۃ فرض کی ہے، ان کے مالداروں سے لی جائے گی اور ان کے فقراء کو دی جائے گی، اور اگر وہ تیری اس میں بھی اطاعت کریں تو ان کے عمدہ مال سے بچ، اور مظلوم کی بددعا سے ڈر، اس لئے کہ مظلوم کی بددعا اور اللہ کے درمیان کوئی پردہ نہیں ہوتا۔ حاصل یہ کہ مسلمانوں سے لے کر انہیں کے فقراء میں تقسیم کر دی جائے گی۔ پس فتؤخذ من أغنيائهم فترد على فقرائهم کا لفظ دلالت کرتا ہے کہ غیر مسلم کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور زکوۃ کے علاوہ ذمی کو ہر صدقہ دینا جائز ہے، خواہ وہ صدقہ واجبہ ہو یا مستحبہ ہو۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ ذمی کو کسی طرح کا صدقہ دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہی قول امام مالک کا ہے، اور یہی ایک روایت امام ابو یوسف سے ہے۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل زکوۃ پر قیاس ہے، یعنی جس طرح زکوۃ ذمی کو دینا جائز نہیں، اسی طرح دیگر صدقات بھی جائز نہیں ہیں۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے: تصدقوا على أهل الأديان كلها، یعنی تمام مذاہب کے لوگوں کو صدقہ دو۔ یہ حدیث دو باتوں پر دلالت کرتی ہے: ایک یہ کہ حربی اور مستامن کو بھی صدقہ دینا جائز ہے، اس لئے کہ تمام ادیان کے لوگوں میں وہ بھی داخل ہیں۔ دوسرے یہ کہ ذمی کو بھی دینا جائز ہے کیونکہ لفظ تصدقوا زکوۃ کو بھی شامل ہے۔ دوسری بات کا جواب تو یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث بلاشبہ اس کا تقاضہ کرتی ہے کہ ذمی کو زکوۃ دینا بھی جائز ہو، مگر حدیث معاذ کی وجہ سے ہم اس کے جواز کے قائل نہیں ہوئے۔ حاصل یہ کہ قول نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم تصدقوا على أهل الأديان كلها تقاضہ کرتا ہے کہ ذمی اور غیر ذمی سب کو زکوۃ دینا...
And it is not permissible to pay zakat to a dhimmi because of his (peace be upon him) saying to Mu'adh: 'Take it from their rich and return it to their poor.' And it is permissible to pay to him (dhimmi) other than that from charity. And al-Shafi'i said: He does not pay, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf, by analogy with zakat. And our evidence is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Give charity to the people of all religions.' And if it were not for the hadith of Mu'adh, we would say permissibility in zakat.

Translation: And giving zakat to a dhimmi is not permissible because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Mu'adh: Take zakat from their wealthy and return it to their poor. And it is permissible to give to him (dhimmi) any charity other than that. And Imam Shafi'i said: He should not give, and this is also a narration from Abu Yusuf, by analogy with zakat. And our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Give charity to the people of all religions. If the hadith of Mu'adh were not there, we would hold permissibility even in zakat.

Explanation: Giving zakat to a dhimmi is not permissible. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah sent Mu'adh to Yemen and said: 'You are going to a people of the Book. Call them to testify that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah. If they obey you in that, inform them that Allah has obligated upon them five prayers every day and night. If they obey you in that, inform them that Allah has obligated upon them charity (zakat) from their wealth, taken from their rich and given to their poor. If they obey you in that, avoid their precious properties, and fear the prayer of the oppressed, for there is no veil between it and Allah.' (Sharh al-Niqayah, referencing books of Sunnah). That is, it is narrated from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah sent Mu'adh as a judge to Yemen and said... The gist is that it is taken from the Muslims and distributed among their poor. Thus the phrase 'taken from their rich and given to their poor' indicates that giving zakat to non-Muslims is not permissible. And other than zakat, giving any charity to a dhimmi is permissible, whether the charity is obligatory or supererogatory. Imam Shafi'i said that it is not permissible to give any kind of charity to a dhimmi. This is also the saying of Imam Malik, and it is a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf. Their evidence is analogy with zakat: just as it is not permissible to give zakat to a dhimmi, likewise other charities are not permissible. Our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Give charity to the people of all religions,' meaning give charity to the people of all religions. This hadith indicates two things: (1) that it is permissible to give charity to a harbi and a musta'min, because they are included among the people of all religions; (2) that it is permissible to give to a dhimmi, because the word 'charity' includes zakat. The response to the second point is that this hadith undoubtedly requires that giving zakat to a dhimmi would also be permissible, but due to the hadith of Mu'adh we do not hold permissibility. The conclusion is that the saying of the Prophet 'Give charity to the people of all religions' requires that zakat be given to both dhimmi and non-dhimmi...
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on giving zakat and other forms of charity (sadaqah) to a dhimmi (a non-Muslim protected citizen under Islamic rule). The Hanafi position, based on the hadith of Mu'adh, is that zakat specifically cannot be given to a dhimmi; it must be given to Muslims. However, other forms of charity, whether obligatory (like zakat al-fitr or kaffarah) or voluntary, are permissible to give to a dhimmi. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that no charity of any kind should be given to a dhimmi, and there is a narration from Abu Yusuf within the Hanafi school that agrees with this, reasoning by analogy (qiyas) with zakat. The Hanafi evidence for permissibility of other charity is the general hadith 'Give charity to the people of all religions.' This hadith would even suggest permissibility of zakat, but it is overridden by the specific hadith of Mu'adh which explicitly restricts zakat to Muslims. The passage highlights an intra-Hanafi difference (Abu Yusuf's narration) but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that non-zakat charity is permissible to give to dhimmis.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmī): A non-Muslim living under the protection of an Islamic state, bound by a contract of dhimmah.
زکوۃ (zakāh): The obligatory annual alms on wealth, one of the five pillars.
صدقہ (ṣadaqah): Charity, which includes both obligatory (like zakat al-fitr, kaffarah) and voluntary donations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi ruling that zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi?
A) The Quranic verse on zakat categories
B) The hadith of Mu'adh: 'Take it from their rich and return it to their poor'
C) The general hadith: 'Give charity to the people of all religions'
D) Analogy (qiyas) with other forms of charity

Key Takeaway
Zakat to a dhimmi is haram due to the specific hadith of Mu'adh; other charity is permissible based on the general hadith to all religions.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
6 min
Giving Zakat and Other Charity to Non-Muslims
Ruling on prohibition of giving zakat to non-Muslims with evidence and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat and other sadaqat to a dhimmi, and explain the evidence and the inter-madhhab disagreement.

Core Idea
Zakat is only for Muslims; other charity may be given to protected non-Muslims.

The ruling on giving zakat to non-Muslims is a point of disagreement between the Hanafi school and other madhhabs. This lesson presents the Hanafi position with its proofs, the opposing view, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core Hanafi ruling: zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi, but other sadaqat (obligatory and voluntary) may be given.
The prohibition is specific to zakat, not all charity.
2
Identify the opponent and their evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i (and a narration from Abu Yusuf) holds that no sadaqah at all may be given to a dhimmi, using qiyas on zakat.
Opponent's proof is analogy: if zakat is prohibited, then all sadaqat are prohibited.
3
Follow the Hanafi evidence for zakat
The hadith of Mu'adh (radiAllahu 'anhu) explicitly states that zakat is taken from wealthy Muslims and given to their poor Muslims, proving zakat is only for Muslims.
The hadith uses possessive pronouns referring to the Muslim community.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response for other sadaqat
The general hadith 'Tasaddaqu 'ala ahl al-adyan kulliha' (Give charity to people of all religions) permits sadaqah to non-Muslims, and this is not overridden by the specific zakat hadith.
The specific restriction on zakat does not extend to other sadaqat.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafis allow sadaqat al-fitr, kaffarat, and voluntary sadaqah to dhimmis; Shafi'is and Malikis do not.
This affects everyday charitable choices.

کا معاملہ مت کرو۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ لوگ دربی ہیں پس ان کو صدقہ وغیرہ دیکر ان کے ساتھ حسن سلوک نہ کیا جائے اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ حربی اور مستامن (جو در حقیقت حربی ہی ہوتا ہے ) کو کسی طرح کا صدقہ دینا And it is not permissible to pay zakat to a dhimmi because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Mu'adh: 'Take it from their wealthy and give it to their poor.' And other than that from sadaqah may be given to him. And al-Shafi'i said: He should not give, and that is a narration from Abu Yusuf, by analogy to zakat. And our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Give charity to the people of all religions.' If not for the hadith of Mu'adh, we would have said that it is permissible in zakat as well. Translation: And giving zakat to a dhimmi is not permissible because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Mu'adh: 'Take zakat from the wealthy of the Muslims and return it to their poor.' And giving other than that from sadaqah is permissible. And Imam al-Shafi'i said that it should not be given, and that is a narration from Abu Yusuf, by analogy to zakat. And our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Give charity to the people of all religions.' If the hadith of Mu'adh were not present, we would also hold permissibility for zakat. Commentary: Giving zakat to a dhimmi is not permissible. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sent Mu'adh to Yemen and said: 'You are coming to a people of the Book; call them to the testimony that there is no deity but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah. If they obey you in that, inform them that Allah has prescribed upon them five prayers in every day and night. If they obey you in that, inform them that Allah has prescribed upon them charity (sadaqah) from their wealth, taken from their wealthy and given to their poor. If they obey you in that, avoid their best properties and fear the prayer of the oppressed, for there is no veil between it and Allah.' The summary is that zakat is taken from Muslims and distributed to their poor. The words 'taken from their wealthy and given to their poor' indicate that giving zakat to non-Muslims is not permissible. And other than zakat, any sadaqah, whether obligatory or voluntary, may be given to a dhimmi. Imam al-Shafi'i said that no type of sadaqah may be given to a dhimmi. That is also the saying of Imam Malik, and it is a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf. Their proof is analogy to zakat: just as giving zakat to a dhimmi is not permissible, so too other sadaqat are not permissible. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Give charity to the people of all religions,' meaning give sadaqah to people of all faiths. This hadith indicates two things: first, that giving sadaqah to a harbi (enemy combatant) and musta'min (protected person) is permissible because people of all religions include them. Second, that giving sadaqah to these people is also permissible because the word 'tasaddaqu' includes zakat as well. The response to the second point is that this hadith indeed requires that giving zakat to a dhimmi is permissible, but due to the hadith of Mu'adh we do not hold its permissibility. The conclusion is that the Prophet's saying 'Tasaddaqu 'ala ahl al-adyan kulliha' requires that giving zakat to a dhimmi and non-dhimmi is permissible, and the hadith of Mu'adh requires non-permissibility for a dhimmi. So in the matter of zakat, we acted upon the hadith of Mu'adh and said that zakat can only be given to a Muslim, not to a dhimmi or others. And in the matter of other sadaqat, we acted upon the hadith 'Tasaddaqu 'ala ahl al-adyan kulliha' and said that to a dhimmi, other sadaqat besides zakat, such as sadaqat al-fitr and expiations, can be given. As for the first point, the response is that although this hadith seems to make giving sadaqat to people of all religions permissible, even to a harbi and musta'min, this hadith is specifically for harbi and musta'min, and it is specified by the saying of Allah: 'Allah only forbids you from those who fight you in religion and drive you out of your homes and assist in your expulsion, that you take them as allies. And whoever takes them as allies, then those are the wrongdoers.' The meaning is that Allah forbids you from those who fight you in religion, drove you from your homes, and assisted in your expulsion, that you befriend them. And whoever befriends them, they are the wrongdoers. The point is that those who are at war with you, do not treat them with friendship. And obviously they are harbis. So they should not be given sadaqah to show good treatment. From this verse it is learned that giving any type of sadaqah to a harbi and musta'min (who is essentially a harbi) is not permissible.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed Hanafi ruling on giving zakat and other sadaqat to non-Muslims, specifically dhimmis. The passage is structured around the core ruling (stated in the matn) that zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi, but other forms of sadaqah (both obligatory like sadaqat al-fitr and kaffarat, and voluntary) are permissible for dhimmis. The author then introduces the disagreement: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that no sadaqah can be given to dhimmis, analogizing all sadaqat to zakat. A narration from Abu Yusuf also supports this view. The Hanafi response relies on two key proofs. First, the hadith of Mu'adh (radiAllahu 'anhu) where the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam) instructed that zakat is taken from the wealthy Muslims and given to their poor, thereby restricting zakat to Muslims. Second, the general hadith 'Give charity to the people of all religions,' which the Hanafis use to permit other sadaqat to non-Muslims. The commentary then reconciles the two hadiths: the general hadith would include zakat, but the specific hadith of Mu'adh specifies that zakat is only for Muslims, so the general hadith is restricted to non-zakat sadaqat. Additionally, the commentary addresses the issue of harbis and musta'mins: the verse from Surah al-Mumtahanah (60:9) prohibits befriending those who fight Muslims, so giving sadaqah to such individuals is also not permissible. The Hanafi position thus differentiates between dhimmis (who are under Muslim protection and may receive non-zakat sadaqah) and harbis (who are at war and may not receive any sadaqah). The authority weight of this ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is based on well-known hadiths and is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ذِمّى (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen of an Islamic state who is protected under Islamic law, paying jizyah in return for protection and exemption from military service.
صدقة (sadaqah): In this context, sadaqah refers to any charitable giving, including both obligatory (zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, kaffarat) and voluntary charity.
حربى (harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under Islamic protection and is in a state of war with Muslims.
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim enemy combatant who has been granted temporary safe passage (aman) into Muslim territory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of charity is prohibited from being given to a dhimmi?
A) Sadaqat al-Fitr
B) Voluntary sadaqah
C) Zakat
D) Kaffarat

Key Takeaway
Zakat is exclusively for Muslims; other sadaqat may be given to dhimmis but not to harbis or musta'mins.

The Pillar of Tamlik in Zakat: Invalid Uses Explained
Ruling on invalid uses of zakat due to absence of tamlik.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why using zakat for building mosques, shrouding the deceased, and paying the deceased's debts is invalid, and apply the condition of tamlik to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Zakat's pillar is tamlik (ownership transfer); any use without it is invalid.

You might wonder why spending zakat on a mosque or a shroud for a deceased seems good but is not allowed. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that the very essence of zakat is transferring ownership to a living eligible recipient. Without tamlik, zakat is not fulfilled. Let's explore the operational rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three invalid uses
List the three scenarios the passage declares invalid: building a mosque, shrouding a deceased, and paying a deceased's debt.
All three share the same underlying flaw.
2
Recognize the key principle
The passage states that tamlik (making the recipient an owner) is the rukn (pillar) of zakat. This is derived from the Quranic term 'sadaqah' which linguistically means ownership transfer.
Rukn: if omitted, the act is batil (void) and must be repeated.
3
Apply the principle to each case
Explain why each case lacks tamlik: a mosque is not owned by any specific poor person; a deceased cannot own property; paying a deceased's debt does not transfer ownership to the deceased.
Focus on the absence of a living recipient who can receive ownership.
4
Note the exception
The passage allows paying a living person's debt with his authorization, because the money first goes to the debtor (tamlik achieved), then the creditor takes as agent.
This shows tamlik can be achieved through agency.
5
Generalize the rule
Any zakat expenditure that does not involve transferring ownership to a living, eligible recipient is invalid. This includes communal projects, funeral expenses, etc.
Good intentions do not substitute for the rukn.
