And a mosque should not be built with it, and a deceased should not be shrouded with it, due to the absence of ownership transfer (tamlik), which is the pillar (rukn). And a deceased's debt should not be paid with it, because paying the debt of another does not necessitate giving ownership from him, especially in the case of the deceased. Translation: And zakat funds should not be used to build a mosque, nor to shroud a deceased, because making the recipient an owner (tamlik) is absent, while it is the rukn. And a deceased's debt should not be paid with it, because paying the debt of another does not necessitate giving ownership to him, especially in the case of the deceased. Explanation: The issue is that it is not permissible to build a mosque with zakat funds, nor to shroud a deceased, because the rukn of zakat is tamlik (making the recipient owner). This is because Allah has described zakat as sadaqah, and sadaqah means making the poor person the owner of the wealth. Thus, for zakat to be valid, tamlik (transfer of ownership) is a condition. In building a mosque, the meaning of tamlik is not found, so it is not valid. Similarly, a deceased does not have the capacity to own, so shrouding him with zakat funds is not valid. And paying a deceased's debt with zakat is also not valid because paying a debt of another (the deceased) does not require that the wealth first be given in ownership to the deceased and then from him to the creditor, because the deceased absolutely lacks the capacity to own. Here, tamlik is not achieved, so zakat is not fulfilled. However, if a living person instructs someone to pay his debt, and that person pays it from zakat funds, it is valid because the wealth is given to the debtor (the living person) and then the creditor takes possession as his agent; thus tamlik is achieved, and the zakat is fulfilled.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage explains three invalid uses of zakat funds: building a mosque, shrouding a deceased person, and paying the debt of a deceased person. The underlying principle is that the rukn (pillar) of zakat is tamlik, meaning the transfer of ownership to the recipient. Zakat is called sadaqah in the Quran, and sadaqah linguistically means making the poor person the owner of the property. Therefore, any disbursement that does not involve making a living, eligible recipient the owner does not fulfill zakat. Building a mosque does not involve tamlik; the mosque itself is not owned by anyone specific. Similarly, a deceased person cannot own property, so buying a shroud for them does not transfer ownership. Paying a deceased person's debt directly to the creditor also fails because the money is not first given to the deceased (who cannot receive ownership). However, an exception is mentioned: if a living person instructs someone to pay his own (the living person's) debt using zakat, then the zakat is valid because the money is first given to the debtor (the living person), who then authorizes the creditor to take it as his agent. In that case, tamlik occurs. The ruling is clear that the essential condition of tamlik must be met for zakat to be valid. The authority weight is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is based on the definition of sadaqah in the Quran and is the standard Hanafi position.

Key Terms
تملیک (tamlik): The act of transferring ownership of property to another person, making them the owner.
ركن (rukn): An integral part of an act of worship; if omitted, the act is invalid and must be repeated in full.
صدقہ (sadaqah): In this context, sadaqah is used interchangeably with zakat in the Quranic verse, but the author explains its meaning as making the poor owner (tamlik).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid to use zakat funds to build a mosque?
A) Because a mosque cannot be owned by anyone
B) Because the rukn of zakat is tamlik, and building a mosque does not involve transferring ownership to a poor person
C) Because zakat funds are only for food and clothing
D) Because the mosque is considered a type of sadaqah jariyah, separate from zakat

Key Takeaway
Zakat requires ownership transfer (tamlik) to a living eligible recipient; any use that does not achieve tamlik, such as building mosques or shrouding the dead, is invalid and does not fulfill the obligation.

Giving Zakat to Non-Muslims: Hanafi Ruling and Evidence
Ruling with proof on zakat recipients

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to dhimmis and harbis, and explain the dalil and reconciliation of hadith.

Core Idea
Zakat is only for Muslims; other sadaqat may go to dhimmis but not to harbis.

This passage addresses a critical question in zakat: who are the eligible recipients? The Hanafi school, based on the hadith of Mu'adh, holds that zakat is restricted to Muslims. However, a general hadith seems to broaden charity to all religions. How do Hanafi scholars reconcile these proofs? Let's follow their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
What does the Hanafi school rule regarding zakat to non-Muslims? Note the distinction between zakat and other sadaqat.
2
Examine the primary proof
What is the hadith of Mu'adh and how does it support the ruling? Understand its specific indication for zakat.
3
Analyze the counter-evidence
What is the general hadith 'Give charity to all people of religions' and how is it addressed? Recognize the apparent conflict.
4
Apply the Quranic exception
How does the Quranic verse about harbis restrict the general hadith? Understand the principle of takhsis (specification).
5
Confirm the final ruling
What is the mufta bihi position on zakat vs. other sadaqat? Summarize the reconciled ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
کتاب الزكوة جائز ہو اور حدیث معاذ ذمی کے لئے عدم جواز کا تقاضہ کرتی ہے پس ہم نے زکوۃ کے سلسلہ میں تو حدیث معاذیر عمل کیا اور کہا کہ کو ۃ فقط مسلمان کو دی جاسکتی ہے ذمی وغیرہ کو نہیں دی جاسکتی۔ اور دوسرے صدقات کے سلسلہ میں حدیث تصدقوا اعلى اهل الاديان كلها پر عمل کیا اور کہا کہ ذمی کو زکوۃ کے علاوہ دوسرے صدقات مثلاً صدقۃ الفطر کفارات وغیرہ دیئے جاسکتے ہیں اور پہلی بات کا جواب یہی کہ اس حدیث سے اگر چہ تمام ادیان کے لوگوں کو صدقات کا دینا جائز معلوم ہوتا ہے حتی کہ حربی اور مستامن کو بھی لیکن یہ حدیث حربی اور مستامن کے حق میں مخصوص ہے اور مشخص باری تعالٰی کا قول إِنَّمَا يَنهَا كُمُ اللهُ عَنِ الَّذِينَ قَاتَلُوكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ وَآخَرِجُوكُم مِّنْ دِيَارِكُمْ وَظَاهَرُوا عَلَى الْحَرَاجِكُمْ أَنْ تَوَلَّهُمْ وَمَن يَتَوَلَّهُمْ فَوكَ هُمُ الظَّالِمُونَ ہے یعنی اللہ تو منع کرتا ہے تم کو ان سے جولڑے تم سے دین پر اور نکالا تم کو تمہارے گھروں سے اور شریک ہوئے تمہارے نکالنے میں کہ ان سے کرو دوستی اور جو کوئی ان سے دوستی کرے سو لوگ وہ وہی ہیں گنہگار حاصل یہ کہ جو لوگ تمہارے ساتھ برسر پیکار رہتے ہیں ان کے ساتھ دوستی کا معاملہ مت کرو۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ لوگ دربی ہیں پس ان کو صدقہ وغیرہ دیکر ان کے ساتھ حسن سلوک نہ کیا جائے اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ حربی اور مستامن (جو در حقیقت حربی ہی ہوتا ہے ) کو کسی طرح کا صدقہ دینا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
Zakat is permissible and the hadith of Mu'adh requires non-permissibility for dhimmi, so we acted upon the hadith of Mu'adh regarding zakat and said that zakat can only be given to Muslims, not to dhimmi etc. And regarding other sadaqat, we acted upon the hadith 'Give charity to all people of religions' and said that to dhimmi, besides zakat, other sadaqat such as sadaqat al-fitr and expiations can be given. And the answer to the first statement is that even though this hadith makes giving sadaqat to all people of religions permissible, even to harbi and musta'min, but this hadith is specific to harbi and musta'min, and the specification is the statement of Allah Most High: 'Allah only forbids you from those who fought you in religion and drove you out of your homes and supported [others] in your eviction, that you should take them as allies. And whoever takes them as allies, then those are the wrongdoers.' That is, Allah forbids you from those who fight you in religion and drove you out of your homes and supported your eviction, to befriend them. And whoever befriends them, they are the sinners. The upshot is: do not befriend those who are at war with you. And it is obvious that these people are harbis, so they should not be given sadaqah etc. to treat them kindly. From this verse it is understood that giving any kind of sadaqah to harbi and musta'min (who is effectively harbi) is not permissible.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that zakat can only be given to Muslims, not to dhimmis, but other voluntary sadaqat can be given to dhimmis. The text addresses a potential conflict between different hadiths. The hadith of Mu'adh (radiallahu anhu) indicates that zakat is taken from the rich of Muslims and given to the poor of Muslims, so it is specific to Muslims. However, another hadith says 'Give charity to all people of religions,' which seems to include non-Muslims. The Hanafi scholars reconcile by limiting the general command to harbi and musta'min, based on the Quranic verse that forbids befriending those who fight against Muslims. Thus, zakat is only for Muslims, other sadaqat can be given to dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects of the state), but not to harbis (those at war with Muslims) or musta'min (temporary safe-conduct non-Muslims). The authority weight here is from the Hanafi school's reliance on the hadith of Mu'adh for zakat and the general hadith for other sadaqat, with a Quranic exception for harbis.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim permanent resident of an Islamic state under protection.
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim from a territory at war with Muslims.
مستامن (musta'min): A non-Muslim given temporary safe passage (aman) into Muslim territory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, zakat is only for Muslims.
C) Only if the dhimmi is poor.
D) Yes, but only sadaqat al-fitr can be given.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is exclusively for Muslims; other sadaqat may be given to dhimmis but not to harbis.

Zakat Spending on Mosque, Shroud, and Deceased Debt
Ruling that zakat cannot build mosques, shroud dead, or pay dead's debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using zakat for mosques, shrouds, and deceased debts, and explain why tamlik (transfer of ownership) is essential for zakat validity.

Core Idea
Zakat must transfer ownership to a living recipient; mosque building, shrouding, and debt payment for the dead do not fulfill this.

Zakat is a fundamental obligation, but its validity hinges on a specific condition: tamlik (transfer of ownership). In this passage, the Hanafi school examines three common scenarios where people might want to use zakat for communal or posthumous benefits. Understanding why these are invalid clarifies the essential nature of zakat as direct ownership transfer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited uses
List the three actions the passage rules as invalid: building a mosque, shrouding a deceased person, and paying the debt of a deceased person from zakat funds.
2
State the essential condition for zakat validity
Identify tamlik (transfer of ownership) as the rukn (integral component) of zakat without which the payment is void.
The passage connects zakat to the Quranic term sadaqat, which linguistically implies tamlik.
3
Examine the proof: Quranic term sadaqat
Understand that Allah describes zakat as sadaqat, and sadaqah means making the poor owner of the wealth. This establishes tamlik as a necessary condition.
The dalil is linguistic: the word sadaqah inherently involves ownership transfer.
4
Apply the condition to each case
For each prohibited use, explain why tamlik is absent: a mosque is a building that cannot own, a deceased cannot own, and paying a deceased's debt does not transfer ownership to the deceased.
5
Note the exception: living person's debt payment
The passage allows paying a living person's debt from zakat if the debtor appoints someone as agent, because ownership is transferred first to the debtor vicariously.
This exception underscores that tamlik is the core requirement.

A mosque is not built with it, nor is a dead person shrouded with it due to the absence of tamlik (transfer of ownership) which is the integral. And a debt of a deceased is not paid with it because paying the debt of another does not necessitate tamlik from him, especially in the case of the deceased. Translation: And zakat money should not be used to build a mosque, nor should it be used to shroud a deceased, because making the recipient owner is absent, whereas it is the integral. And a debt of a deceased should not be paid with it because paying the debt of another does not necessitate giving possession to him, especially in the case of the deceased. Explanation: The issue is that it is not permissible to build a mosque from zakat money nor to shroud a deceased with it because the integral of zakat is making the recipient owner. This is because Allah Most High has described zakat as sadaqaat, and sadaqah means to make the poor person the owner of the wealth. So it is understood that for zakat to be fulfilled, tamlik (transfer of ownership) is a condition. In building a mosque, the meaning of tamlik is not found, so it is not permissible to build a mosque from zakat money. And because the deceased does not have the capacity to become an owner, it is also not permissible to shroud him with zakat money. And paying the debt of a deceased from zakat money is also not permissible, because paying the debt of another (i.e., the deceased) does not necessitate that this wealth was first given into the ownership of the deceased and then from his side to the creditor, because the deceased has absolutely no capacity to take into his own ownership. So when the meaning of tamlik is not found in this case, zakat is not fulfilled. However, if a living person instructed someone to pay his debt from his side, and that person paid the debt from zakat money, then zakat will be fulfilled, because in this case, even though the money was given to the creditor, the creditor took possession as a deputy on behalf of the debtor, so the meaning of making the debtor owner is found, and when that meaning is found, his zakat will be fulfilled.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with reasoning that zakat cannot be used for building mosques, shrouding the dead, or paying the debts of the deceased, because the essential requirement (rukn) of zakat is tamlik – transferring ownership to a living human recipient. Since a building cannot own, and a deceased cannot own, these expenditures do not fulfill the condition of tamlik. However, if a living person appoints someone to pay his debt from zakat, it is valid because the debtor becomes owner first through the agent's possession. The text uses the linguistic connection between zakat and sadaqah, which implies tamlik, as the basis. This is a Hanafi position based on the definition of sadaqah. The authority weight is from the Hanafi school's reliance on the Zahir al-Riwayah that tamlik is a necessary condition.

Key Terms
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership to the recipient, which is the essential condition for zakat validity in this passage.
رکن (rukn): The essential component without which the act is invalid; here tamlik is the rukn of zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid to pay the debt of a deceased person from zakat money according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the deceased does not need it.
B) Because tamlik (transfer of ownership) cannot occur as the deceased cannot own.
C) Because debt payment is not a form of charity.
D) Because the deceased's heirs will benefit instead.

Key Takeaway
Zakat requires tamlik; without transferring ownership to a living recipient, the payment is invalid.

Zakat Cannot Be Used to Purchase Slaves for Manumission
Ruling on using zakat to free slaves with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits using zakat to purchase slaves for manumission and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Zakat requires tamlik; freeing a slave removes ownership, so it does not fulfill zakat.

This passage addresses a classical inter-madhhab dispute regarding the interpretation of 'wa fi al-riqab' (and in the freeing of slaves) in the Quranic verse on zakat recipients (Surah At-Tawbah 9:60). The Hanafi school holds that this phrase refers to assisting mukatib slaves (those with a contract of manumission) and not to the outright purchase and freeing of slaves. The key legal principle is that the essential element (rukn) of zakat is tamlik (transfer of ownership), while freeing a slave (itiq) is the removal of ownership, not a transfer to the slave. Therefore, buying a slave with zakat money and freeing them does not constitute valid zakat fulfillment.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: purchasing a slave with zakat money to free is invalid (fasid). The zakat obligation remains unfulfilled.
The ruling is derived from the principle that zakat must involve tamlik.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik holds that it is valid based on his interpretation of 'wa fi al-riqab' as purchasing slaves to free them.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Maliki proof is the literal wording of the Quranic category 'fi al-riqab' which they take to include freeing slaves by purchasing them.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes itiq from tamlik: itiq is isqat al-milk (removal of ownership), not tamlik (conferring ownership). Since the rukn of zakat is tamlik, the act of freeing does not fulfill zakat. The phrase 'fi al-riqab' is interpreted as helping mukatib slaves, who need financial assistance to complete their purchase of freedom.
The Hanafi school also supports this by the general rule that zakat cannot be given to the wealthy (based on the hadith 'La tahillu al-sadaqatu li ghaniyyi') even if they are warriors (contra Shafi'i).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi scholars require the zakat payer to give money directly to eligible recipients (including mukatib slaves) rather than buying and freeing slaves. Maliki scholars allow the latter.
In modern contexts, this ruling means zakat cannot be used for programs that purchase slaves to free them; instead, it should be given to the poor, needy, or eligible categories.

Source Text

وَلَا تُشْتَرى بِهَا رَقَبَةُ تُعْتَقُ خِلَافًا مَالِكَ حَيْثُ ذَهَبَ إِلَيْهِ فِي تَاوِيلِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَ فِي الرِّقَابِ وَلَنَا الْإِعْتَاقُ اسْقَاطُ المِلْكِ وَلَيْسَ بِتَمُلِيْ وَلَا تُدْفَعُ إِلى عَنِي لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ لَا تَحِلُّ الصَّدَقَةَ لِعَنِي وَهُوَ بِإِطْلَاقِة حُجَّةً عَلَى الشَّافِعِي فِي غَنِي الْغُرَاةِ وَكَذَا حَدِيثُ مَعَادٍ عَلَى مَارَوَيْنَا
ترجمہ اور زکوۃ کے مال سے کوئی غلام یا با ندی خرید کر آزاد نہ کی جائے گی خلاف ہے امام مالک کا چنانچہ امام مالک باری تعالیٰ کے قول وفي الرقاب کی تاویل میں اسی طرف گئے ہیں اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتاق ملک ساقط کرنے کا نام ہے اور یہ تملیک نہیں ہے اور نہ کسی مالدار کو دے۔ کیونکہ رسول ہاشمی نے فرمایا ہے کہ زکوۃ مالدار کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے اور یہ حدیث اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے مالدار غازیوں میں امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہے اور یونہی حدیث معاذ اس کے مطابق جو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر زکوۃ کے مال سے غلام یا با ندی خرید کر آزاد کر دے تو زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی البتہ حضرت امام مالک کے نزدیک زکوۃ اداہ ہو جائے گی حضرت امام مالک نے وفی الرقاب " سے یہی مراد لیا ہے یعنی وفی الرقاب سے مرادز کوۃ کی رقم سے غلام خرید کر آزاد کرنا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک مکاتبوں کی اعانت کرنا مراد ہے ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتاق ملک ساقط کرنے کا نام ہے یعنی مملوک کی گردن سے اپنی ملک دور کرنا اعتناق تملیک (مالک کرنے کا نام نہیں ہے حالانکہ زکوۃ کا رکن تملیک ہے پس جب اعتاق میں مالک کرنے کے معنی نہیں پائے جاتے بلکہ ملک ساقط کرنے کے معنی پائے جاتے ہیں تو زکوۃ بھی ادا نہ ہوگی۔ غنی یعنی جو شخص نصاب کا مالک ہو اس کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے دلیل حدیث رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم لا تحل الصدقة لغنی ہے امام شافعی نے مالدار غازیوں کے لئے زکوۃ لینے کی اجازت دی ہے جیسا کہ تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے لیکن یہ حدیث اور حدیث معاذ فترد في فقرائهم ان کیخلاف حجت ہے۔
And a slave is not purchased with it to be freed, contrary to Malik, as he went to that interpretation of Allah's statement 'and in the freeing of slaves.' And our proof is that freeing is removal of ownership and is not tamlik. And it is not given to a rich person because of the Prophet's saying: 'Sadaqah is not permissible for a rich person,' and this hadith, by its generality, is a proof against al-Shafi'i regarding the rich warriors. And similarly the hadith of Mu'adh as we have narrated. Translation: And a slave or female slave will not be purchased with zakat money to free, contrary to Imam Malik. Indeed, Imam Malik went to that interpretation of Allah's statement 'and in the freeing of slaves.' And our proof is that itiq (freeing) is the removal of ownership and is not tamlik. And it is not given to a wealthy person because the Messenger of Allah said: 'Sadaqah is not permissible for a wealthy person,' and this hadith, by its generality, is a proof against al-Shafi'i regarding wealthy warriors. And similarly the hadith of Mu'adh as we have narrated. Explanation: The issue is that if one purchases a slave or female slave with zakat money and frees him, zakat will not be fulfilled. However, according to Imam Malik, zakat would be fulfilled. Imam Malik took from 'and in the freeing of slaves' the meaning of purchasing slaves to free with zakat money. And according to us, it means assisting mukatib slaves. Our proof is that itiq is the removal of ownership, i.e., removing one's ownership from the neck of the owned person; it is not tamlik (making someone owner). Whereas the integral of zakat is tamlik. So when the meaning of making owner is not found in itiq, rather the meaning of removing ownership is found, then zakat will not be fulfilled. A wealthy person, i.e., one who owns a nisab, cannot be given zakat. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet 'Sadaqah is not permissible for a wealthy person.' Imam Shafi'i permitted wealthy warriors to take zakat, as the detail has passed before, but this hadith and the hadith of Mu'adh 'take from their rich and return to their poor' are proofs against him.

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Malik on the interpretation of 'wa fi al-riqab' (in the freeing of slaves) in the zakat verse. The Hanafi position is that this phrase refers to helping mukatib slaves (slaves who have a contract of manumission) rather than purchasing slaves to free them outright. The reasoning is that the integral of zakat is tamlik (transfer of ownership), while freeing (itiq) is the removal of ownership, not creation of ownership for the freed slave. Therefore, buying a slave to free does not fulfill the zakat requirement. The text also addresses a second issue: giving zakat to a wealthy person is prohibited, and this applies even to wealthy warriors (ghuzat), contradicting Imam al-Shafi'i's view that warriors can receive zakat even if wealthy. The hadith of Mu'adh specifying the poor of Muslims as recipients is used as proof against giving to wealthy warriors. The authority weight is from the Hanafi school's reliance on the Zahir al-Riwayah interpretation of the Quranic verse.

Key Terms
اعتقاق (itiq): Freeing a slave, which is the removal of ownership from the slave's neck.
مکاتِب (mukatib): A slave who has a contract (kitabah) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
تملیک (tamlik): Ownership transfer; making someone the owner of a property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Freeing any slave regardless of method.
D) Buying and freeing female slaves only.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat must involve tamlik (ownership transfer); therefore, using zakat to buy and free slaves is invalid because itiq is the removal of ownership, not a transfer.

Giving Zakat to Close Relatives: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Wife to Husband
Ruling on zakat to close relatives with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to ascendants, descendants, and spouse, and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding a wife giving zakat to her husband.

Core Idea
Zakat to ascendants, descendants, and spouse is generally invalid; but for a wife giving to her husband, the Sahibayn allow it while Abu Hanifa prohibits it.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a crucial fiqh question: to which close relatives can zakat be given? The general rule is that zakat cannot be given to one's own parents, grandparents, children, grandchildren, or wife because the benefits of property are shared (ittisal manafi' al-amlak), preventing complete ownership (tamlik). However, a notable intra-madhhab dispute arises regarding a wife giving zakat to her husband. In this lesson, we will unpack the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and identify the operative (mufta bihi) position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
For ascendants and descendants, the text states zakat is invalid due to interconnected benefits. For wife from husband, also invalid due to shared benefits. Note the consistent principle.
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
On wife giving to her husband, Abu Hanifa maintains the general rule and prohibits it. The Sahibayn allow it based on a hadith.
3
Analyze the dalil
The Sahibayn cite the hadith of the Prophet to Umm Abd Allah: 'You have two rewards: reward of sadaqah and reward of silah rahim.' Abu Hanifa interprets this hadith as applying to nafl (supererogatory) charity, not wajib zakat.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn (permissible) because it is more facilitative and supported by a sound hadith, though some later scholars retain Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باپ، دادا، بیٹا، پوتا کوز کو ۃ دینا جائز نہیں ، مرد بیوی کو اور بیوی شوہر کوز کو نہیں دے سکتی
قَالَ وَ لَا يَدْفَعُ الْمُزَكَّى زَكَوةَ مَالِهِ إللى أَبِيهِ وَجَدِهِ وَإِنْ عَلَا وَلَا إِلى وَلَدِهِ وَ وَلَدِ وَلَدِهِ وَ إِنْ سَفِلَ لِأَنَّ مَنَافِعَ الأَمْلَاكِ بَيْنَهُمْ مُتَصِلَةٌ فَلَا يَتَحَقق التمليك عَلَى الكُمَالِ وَلَا إِلَى امْرَأَتِهِ لِلاشْتِرَاكِ فِي الْمَنَافِعَ عَادَةً وَلَا تَدْفَعُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلى زَوْجِهَا عِنْدَ أَبِى حَنِيفَةَ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَ قَالَا تَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَكِ أَجْرَانِ أَجُرُ الصَّدَقَةِ وَأَجْرُ الصَّلَةِ قَالَهُ لِأمْرَأَةٍ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ وَ قَدْ سَأَلْته عَنِ التَّصَدقِ عَلَيْهِ قُلْنَا هُوَ مَحمول عَلَى النَّافِلة
ترجمہ اور زکوۃ دینے والا اپنے مال کی زکوۃ نہ دے اپنے باپ کو اور دادا کو اگر چہ اونچے درجہ کا ہو۔ اور نہ اپنے ولد کو اور نہ ولد کے دلد کو رچہ نیچے درجہ کا ہو ۔ کیونکہ املاک کے منافع ان کے درمیان متصل ہیں تو تملیک پورے طور پر متفق نہ ہوگی اورنر اپنی بیوی کو دے کیونکہ عادةً منافع مشترک ہوتے ہیں اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نہ عورت اپنے شوہر کو دے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ عورت اپنے شوہر کو دے سکتی ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ تیرے لئے دو اجر ہیں۔ ایک صدقہ کا اجر ، دوم صلہ کا اجر ، یہ کلام آپ نے عبد اللہ بن مسعود کی بیوی سے فرمایا تھا درانحالیکہ اس نے ابن مسعود کو صدقہ دینے کے بارے میں دریافت کیا تھا ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ
The zakat giver should not give zakat of his wealth to his father and his grandfather, even if high, and not to his child and his child's child, even if low, because the benefits of properties are connected between them, so complete tamlik is not achieved. And not to his wife because normally benefits are shared. And according to Abu Hanifa, the woman does not give to her husband for the reason we mentioned. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: she gives to him because of the Prophet's saying: 'You have two rewards: the reward of charity and the reward of maintaining ties.' He said this to the wife of Ibn Mas'ud when she asked about giving charity to him. We say: this is carried upon supererogatory (charity).
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute on giving zakat to close relatives. The general principle is that zakat cannot be given to one's own father, grandfather, son, grandson, or wife because the benefits of property are shared among them (mutasilah manafi' al-amlak), meaning they benefit from each other's wealth, so tamlik is not considered complete. The text then addresses the specific case of a wife giving zakat to her husband. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is not valid for the same reason of shared benefits. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow it based on the hadith where the Prophet told Umm Abd Allah (the wife of Ibn Mas'ud) that she will get two rewards for giving charity to her husband: one for charity and one for maintaining family ties. Abu Hanifa responds that this hadith refers to voluntary (nafl) charity, not obligatory zakat. Thus, for zakat, the ruling is that a wife cannot give to her husband according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the Sahibayn she can. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn (that it is permissible) because it is more accommodating and supported by the hadith, though some later authorities follow Abu Hanifa. The authority weight here is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as this is a mas'alah from the matn with the ikhtilaf noted.

Key Terms
اتصال منافع الأملاك (ittisal manafi' al-amlak): The interconnection of benefits of properties between close relatives, such that they benefit from each other's wealth, which prevents complete tamlik.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, can a wife give her zakat to her husband?
A) No, according to Abu Hanifa it is invalid.
B) Yes, according to the Sahibayn it is valid.
C) Only if the husband is poor.
D) All Hanafi authorities agree it is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon position permits a wife to give zakat to her husband, while the general rule prohibits giving to ascendants, descendants, and one's own spouse (with husband to wife also prohibited).

Using Zakat to Purchase and Free a Slave
States ruling that zakat cannot be used to buy a slave to free, opposing Malik.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using zakat to free a slave, explain the proof that i'taq is isqat al-milk not tamlik, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Maliki interpretation of 'wa fi al-riqab'.

Core Idea
Zakat requires transfer of ownership; freeing a slave removes ownership, so it does not fulfill zakat.

This passage from al-Hidayah states a clear Hanafi ruling: zakat funds cannot be used to purchase and free a slave. The core reason is that zakat must involve tamlik (transfer of ownership) to the eligible recipient, while freeing a slave is isqat al-milk (removal of ownership) and does not give ownership to the slave. The Hanafi school also invokes the hadith forbidding charity to the rich to reinforce this. This ruling directly contradicts Imam Malik's interpretation of the Quranic phrase 'wa fi al-riqab' as permission. We will break down the legal reasoning, the proofs, and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under consideration is using zakat funds to purchase a slave and then free him. According to the Hanafi school, this does not discharge the zakat obligation; the ruling is that the act is invalid (batil) for fulfilling zakat.
The ruling is about the validity of discharging zakat, not about the permissibility of freeing slaves in general.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof (i'taq is isqat al-milk)
The Hanafi proof is that i'taq (freeing) is isqat al-milk (removal of ownership), not tamlik (transfer of ownership). Since zakat requires tamlik to a recipient, freeing a slave does not meet this condition.
The slave does not become a recipient of the zakat money; rather, the owner is compensated, and the slave's freedom is a removal of the owner's right.
3
Examine the hadith proof against giving to the rich
The hadith 'La tahillu al-sadaqatu li ghaniyyin' (Charity is not permissible for the rich) prohibits giving zakat to a rich person. Since the seller of the slave (or the slave himself if considered rich after freedom) may be wealthy, this further supports the prohibition. The generality of this hadith also serves as an argument against Imam al-Shafi'i, who permits zakat for rich ghazis (fighters).
The phrase 'la tahillu' indicates a clear prohibition (haram), and the hadith is used to stress that zakat must go to the needy.
4
Contrast with the Maliki position
Imam Malik permits using zakat to buy and free slaves based on his interpretation of the Quranic verse 'wa fi al-riqab' (and for freeing necks). The Hanafi response is that this verse refers to assisting mukatib slaves (those who have a contract of emancipation), not to purchasing slaves to free them. Hanafis maintain that freeing a slave is isqat al-milk, not tamlik.
The dispute hinges on the interpretation of 'riqab' and the nature of zakat expenditure.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: According to Malik, if a person uses his zakat to buy and free a slave, his zakat is discharged. According to the Hanafis, the zakat obligation remains, and the person must still give zakat to eligible recipients.
This shows that a difference in usul (definition of zakat expenditure) leads to a different practical ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا تُشْتَرى بِهَا رَقَبَةُ تُعْتَقُ خِلَافًا مَالِكَ حَيْثُ ذَهَبَ إِلَيْهِ فِي تَاوِيلِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَ فِي الرِّقَابِ وَلَنَا الْإِعْتَاقُ اسْقَاطُ المِلْكِ وَلَيْسَ بِتَمُلِيْ وَلَا تُدْفَعُ إِلى عَنِي لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ لَا تَحِلُّ الصَّدَقَةَ لِعَنِي وَهُوَ بِإِطْلَاقِة حُجَّةً عَلَى الشَّافِعِي فِي غَنِي الْغُرَاةِ وَكَذَا حَدِيثُ مَعَادٍ عَلَى مَارَوَيْنَا
And a slave shall not be purchased with it to be freed, contrary to Malik who went to that in interpretation of His statement 'and in freeing necks'. And our proof is that freeing is removal of ownership and is not granting ownership. And it shall not be given to a rich person due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Charity is not permissible for the rich.' And it is, by its generality, an argument against al-Shafi'i regarding the rich fighters. And likewise the hadith of Mu'ad as we have narrated.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school: zakat funds cannot be used to purchase a slave to free him, because zakat requires tamlik (transfer of ownership) to the recipient, whereas i'taq (freeing) is isqat al-milk (removing ownership) — it does not give ownership to the slave. This is contrary to Imam Malik, who interprets the Quranic phrase 'wa fi al-riqab' (and for freeing necks) as permission to use zakat to buy and free slaves. The Hanafi proof: freeing is not tamlik, so it does not fulfill the purpose of zakat. Additionally, zakat may not be given to a rich person (ghani), based on the hadith 'La tahillu al-sadaqatu li ghaniyyin'. This hadith also serves as a proof against Imam al-Shafi'i, who allows zakat for rich ghazis (fighters). The hadith of Mu'ad is also cited as evidence, as reported earlier.

Key Terms
اعْتاق (i'tāq): Freeing a slave; the act of removing ownership from a slave.
تَمْلِيك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership from one person to another; a required element in zakat according to Hanafis.
إسْقاط المِلْك (isqāṭ al-milk): Removal of ownership, as in freeing a slave; contrasts with tamlik.
زَكَاة (zakāh): Obligatory charity prescribed by Islam on specific wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not permissible to use zakat funds to purchase and free a slave according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because slaves are not eligible zakat recipients.
B) Because freeing a slave is isqat al-milk (removal of ownership), not tamlik (transfer of ownership), and zakat requires tamlik.
C) Because the Quranic verse 'wa fi al-riqab' does not mention freeing slaves.
D) Because the hadith prohibits giving to the rich, and a freed slave becomes rich.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires tamlik in zakat, so using zakat to free a slave (isqat al-milk) does not discharge the obligation.

Giving Zakat to Close Relatives and Spouses
States rulings on whom zakat may not be given among relatives: ascendants, descendants, and spouses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on giving zakat to ascendants, descendants, and spouses, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute on a wife giving zakat to her husband.

Core Idea
Zakat requires complete tamlik; giving to those with interconnected benefits invalidates it.

Zakat is a compulsory form of charity that must be given to specific categories of recipients. One key condition is that the ownership of the zakat funds must be fully transferred to the recipient. When the giver and recipient are too closely related—such as ascendants or descendants—the benefits of wealth are considered shared, so complete tamlik is not achieved. This lesson explores the prohibited recipients and the reasoning behind them, including a notable dispute within the Hanafi school regarding a wife giving zakat to her husband.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited recipients
List the relatives to whom zakat cannot be given according to the passage: father, grandfather (and upwards), child, grandchild (and downwards), and spouse. Note that the passage also addresses a wife giving to her husband, which is disputed.
The prohibition is due to interconnected benefits (manāfi' mutaṣila).
2
Understand the rationale: tamlik and shared benefits
Zakat requires complete transfer of ownership (tamlik). If the giver and recipient share benefits (e.g., the giver benefits from the recipient's wealth or vice versa), the transfer is not complete. This applies to ascendants/descendants (they are obligated to support each other) and spouses (customary sharing).
In Hanafi, the ruling is based on preventing a circular benefit.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute on wife giving to husband
Imam Abu Hanifa disallows it, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit it. Identify each position and their proofs: for Abu Hanifa, the same rationale of shared benefits; for the Sahibayn, a hadith promising two rewards.
The dispute hinges on whether the hadith applies to obligatory zakat or supererogatory charity.
4
Analyze the dalil: hadith of the wife of Ibn Mas'ud
Examine the hadith cited by the Sahibayn. The Hanafi response is that the hadith refers to nafl charity, not obligatory zakat, because the context was general charity (ṣadaqa) rather than specific zakat.
The hadith is aḥad, so its application to zakat is not definitive.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The passage indicates that the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view: a wife cannot give her obligatory zakat to her husband. This is based on the principle that zakat conditions are stricter.
This is the position given in zahir al-riwaya texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ لَا يَدْفَعُ الْمُزَكَّى زَكَوةَ مَالِهِ إللى أَبِيهِ وَجَدِهِ وَإِنْ عَلَا وَلَا إِلى وَلَدِهِ وَ وَلَدِ وَلَدِهِ وَ إِنْ سَفِلَ لِأَنَّ مَنَافِعَ الأَمْلاكِ بَيْنَهُمْ مُتَصِلَةٌ فَلَا يَتَحَقق التمليك عَلَى الكُمَالِ وَلَا إِلَى امْرَأَتِهِ لِلاشْتِرَاكِ فِي الْمَنَافِعَ عَادَةً وَلَا تَدْفَعُ الْمَرْأَةُ إِلى زَوْجِهَا عِنْدَ أَبِى حَنِيفَةَ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَ قَالَا تَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَكِ أَجْرَانِ أَجُرُ الصَّدَقَةِ وَأَجْرُ الصَّلَةِ قَالَهُ لِأمْرَأَةٍ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ وَ قَدْ سَأَلْته عَنِ التَّصَدقِ عَلَيْهِ قُلْنَا هُوَ مَحمول عَلَى النَّافِلة
He said: The one giving zakat shall not give the zakat of his wealth to his father or grandfather, even if high up, nor to his child or child's child, even if low down, because the benefits of properties are interconnected among them, so complete tamlik is not realized. Nor to his wife due to the customary sharing of benefits. And a woman shall not give to her husband according to Abu Hanifa for what we mentioned. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said she may give to him due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'You have two rewards: the reward of charity and the reward of maintaining ties.' He said this to the wife of Ibn Mas'ud when she asked about giving charity to him. We say: This is interpreted as supererogatory charity.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage details the rulings on to whom zakat may not be given due to close familial ties. The person giving zakat may not give it to his father, grandfather (upwards), nor to his son, grandson (downwards), because the benefits of their properties are interconnected — they share in each other's wealth, so if the giver gives zakat to them, it is like giving it to himself, and complete tamlik is not achieved. Similarly, a husband may not give zakat to his wife due to the customary sharing of benefits between spouses. As for a wife giving to her husband, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it impermissible for the same reason, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) permit it based on the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told the wife of Ibn Mas'ud that she would receive two rewards if she gave charity to her husband: one for charity and one for maintaining family ties. However, Abu Hanifa and his followers interpret this hadith as applying to supererogatory (nafl) charity, not obligatory zakat, because the conditions for zakat are stricter.

Key Terms
تَمْلِيك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; a required element for zakat validity.
مَنَافِع (manāfi'): Benefits or usufruct from property; interconnectedness of benefits prevents complete tamlik.
صَاحِبَان (Sāḥibān): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two major disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, may a woman give her obligatory zakat to her husband?
A) Yes, because it is a form of charity.
B) No, because the benefits between spouses are shared, preventing complete tamlik.
C) Yes, based on the hadith of the wife of Ibn Mas'ud.
D) No, but she may give supererogatory charity.

Key Takeaway
Zakat must be given to recipients with no shared benefits; ascendants, descendants, and one's spouse are excluded; the wife giving to husband is disputed but the relied-upon view is prohibition.

8 min
Zakat to Close Relatives: Prohibited Recipients and the Spousal Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat to close relatives and spouse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule prohibiting zakat to ascendants, descendants, and spouse, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on a wife giving zakat to her husband.

Core Idea
Zakat to close relatives fails due to shared benefits — tamlik is incomplete.

The rules of zakat recipients are precise: the poor and destitute, but not those whose benefits are already intertwined with yours. This lesson examines why one cannot give zakat to ascendants, descendants, or a spouse, and then delves into the hallmark intra-Hanafi dispute: may a wife give her zakat to her husband? The source text from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents both the foundational ruling and the scholarly exchange between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core prohibited recipients
The text first lists ascendants (father, mother, grandparents) and descendants (children, grandchildren). Understand the general rule: zakat cannot be given to anyone with a blood relationship (qarabah) because benefits are shared.
2
Grasp the legal reasoning: tamlik and shared benefits
The author argues that tamlik (transfer of ownership) is a pillar of zakat. With close relatives, benefits (manafi‘) are connected and shared, so tamlik is incomplete. This applies equally to spouses.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a wife cannot give zakat to her husband; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit it. Identify each position and its proof.
4
Analyze the opposing proof: the hadith of Zainab
The Sahibayn cite the hadith where women gave voluntary charity to their husbands and orphans. The Hanafi response distinguishes between obligatory zakat and voluntary sadaqah, noting that giving zakat to one's own children is unanimously prohibited.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the practical consequence
The author sides with Imam Abu Hanifa. The practical difference: if a wife gives zakat to her husband, according to Abu Hanifa her obligation remains undischarged; according to the Sahibayn, it is discharged and she earns double reward.

کہا کہ تم رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس جا کر خبر دو کہ دروازہ پر دو عورتیں ہیں آپ سے پوچھنا چاہتی ہیں کہ کیا ان دونوں کی طرف سے انکا صدقہ دینا اپنے شوہروں اور اپنے یتیم بچوں کو کافی ہے اور یہ نہ بتلانا کہ ہم دونوں کون میں زینب کہتی ہیں کہ بلال نے رسول کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی خدمت میں حاضر ہو کر دریافت کیا رسول اللہ نے بلال سے کہا کہ وہ کون دو عورتیں ہیں بلال نے کہا کہ ایک تو انصاری عورت ہے اور ایک زینب ہے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کون کسی زینب ہے کہا کہ عبداللہ بن مسعود بیگم صدقہ کی بیگم میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ان دونوں کے لئے دو، دو اجر میں ایک قرابت کا اجر اور دوسرے صدقہ کا اجر ، اس تفصیلی حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیوی کے واسطے اپنے شو ہر کوز کو ۃ دینا جائز ہے۔ ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ روایت صدقات نافلہ پر محمول ہے یعنی عورت اگر نفلی صدقہ اپنے شو ہر کو دیگی تو اس کو دو ہرا ثواب ملے گا ایک صلہ رحمی کا دوسرے صدقہ کا۔ صاحبین کی طرف سے جو حدیث پیش کی گئی ہے اس سے بھی یہی ظاہر ہے کیونکہ زینب نے اپنے شوہر اور اپنے سابقہ شوہر کے یتیم بچوں کو دینے کے بارے میں دریافت کرایا تھا اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے دونوں کو دینے کی اجازت دی ہے حالانکہ اولادکو زکوۃ دینا بالاتفاق جائز نہیں ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ اس حدیث میں صدقات نافلہ مراد ہیں نہ کہ زکوۃ۔
Explanation of the issue: The person giving zakat from his wealth should not give it to his father, nor to his grandfather, nor to ancestors above him (great-grandfather, etc.), similarly not to his mother, nor to his grandmother, nor to his children, nor to his grandchildren. In summary, he should not give zakat to his ascendants from whom he is born, nor to his descendants who are born from him. In short, it is not permissible to give zakat from his wealth to those with whom he has a blood relationship. The proof is that the benefits of wealth are connected and shared among these people, so if zakat is given to them, complete ownership (tamlik) is not realized, whereas tamlik is an integral part of zakat. And it is not permissible for a husband to give zakat to his wife because usually benefits are shared between spouses, meaning the wife's wealth is considered the husband's wealth and vice versa, and each benefits from the other's wealth. Thus the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'And He found you in need and made you self-sufficient.' It was interpreted that the Prophet was made self-sufficient by his wife Khadija's wealth. So it is understood that if the wife is wealthy, the husband is considered wealthy, and vice versa. Therefore, a husband giving zakat to his wife is like taking from one pocket and putting into another, so how can zakat be discharged? And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is also not permissible for a woman to give zakat to her husband. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said that a wife giving zakat to her husband is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is the same as before: benefits are shared between spouses. The Sahibayn's proof is the hadith narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, and Nasa'i, as mentioned in Fath al-Qadir: from Zainab, the wife of Ibn Mas'ud... (hadith text)... meaning that this detailed hadith shows that a wife may give zakat to her husband. Our response is that this narration refers to voluntary charity (sadaqah nafilah), i.e., if a woman gives voluntary charity to her husband, she gets double reward: one for maintaining ties and one for charity. This is also clear from the hadith because Zainab inquired about giving to her husband and orphan children, whereas giving zakat to one's own children is unanimously not permissible. Thus it is understood that the hadith refers to voluntary charity, not zakat.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of a wife giving zakat to her husband, nested within the broader ruling on prohibited recipients. The author first states the general rule: zakat cannot be given to one's ascendants (parents, grandparents, etc.) or descendants (children, grandchildren) because the benefits of their wealth are considered shared (manafi' mushtaraka), preventing complete ownership transfer (tamlik), which is a condition for zakat. The same reasoning applies to spouses, because customarily spouses share financial benefits, as illustrated by the Quranic verse (93:8) interpreted to show that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was enriched by Khadija's wealth. Thus, a husband giving zakat to his wife is like moving money within the same household. Then the author notes the intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa held that a wife also cannot give zakat to her husband for the same reason, while the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argued it is permissible, citing the hadith of Zainab bint Jahsh (or Zainab, wife of Ibn Mas'ud) in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that women giving charity to their husbands receive double reward. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah responds on behalf of Abu Hanifa: this hadith refers to voluntary charity (sadaqah nafilah), not obligatory zakat, because the hadith also mentions giving to orphans, and giving zakat to one's own children is universally prohibited. Thus the hadith cannot be evidence for zakat. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in this commentary is that of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; a necessary condition for zakat validity.
منافع مشترکہ (manafi' mushtaraka): Shared benefits; the idea that close relatives and spouses commonly share the benefit of each other's wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in this lesson, may a wife give her zakat to her husband?
A) Yes, because the hadith of Zainab permits it.
B) No, because shared benefits prevent complete tamlik.
C) Yes, but only if she has no other eligible recipients.
D) No, because the husband is not considered poor.

Key Takeaway
Zakat to close relatives and spouses is invalid because shared benefits prevent complete ownership transfer; the wife-to-husband issue is a settled intra-Hanafi dispute following Abu Hanifa.

Zakat — Almsgiving
beginner

Prohibition of Giving Zakat to One's Own Slaves
Ruling with rational proof: prohibition due to incomplete tamlik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on giving zakat to one's own mudabbar, mukatab, and umm walad and explain why it does not discharge the zakat obligation.

Core Idea
Giving zakat to your own slave is like giving it to yourself — ownership is not transferred.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: the prohibition of paying zakat to certain categories of one's own slaves. Understanding the concept of tamlik (transfer of ownership) is key to grasping why zakat is not discharged in these cases. The ruling is based on the principle that the slave's earnings belong to the master, so tamlik is incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories and the ruling
Read the text to identify: mudabbar (slave whose freedom is suspended on master's death), mukatab (slave with a contract to purchase freedom), and umm walad (slave woman who bore master's child). The ruling: it is not permissible (haram) to give zakat to any of them because the zakat will not be discharged.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the mudabbar is absolute or restricted.
2
Understand the condition of tamlik for zakat validity
For zakat to be valid, the giver must transfer full ownership (tamlik) to the recipient. This means the recipient must become the exclusive owner of the zakat property, with no residual ownership rights for the giver.
Tamlik is a necessary condition; mere permission to use is insufficient.
3
Analyze why tamlik fails for each category
For mudabbar and umm walad: they are fully owned slaves; their earnings belong to the master. Giving zakat to them effectively transfers ownership back to the master, so tamlik is not achieved. For mukatab: the master has a right in the mukatab's earnings, so tamlik is also incomplete.
The proof is rational (qiyas): it is like giving zakat to oneself, which is invalid.
4
Apply the principle to other similar cases
Consider whether giving zakat to a slave owned by someone else is valid. Since tamlik would be complete (the slave becomes owner), it is valid. Also consider giving zakat to a dependent who is not owned: tamlik is achieved because the dependent can own property.
The key is whether the giver retains any ownership or right over the recipient's property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يَدْفَعُ إِلى مَدَتِرِهِ وَمُكَاتِبِهِ وَامَ وَلَدِهِ لِفُقْدَانِ التَّمْلِيْكِ إِذْ كَسُبُ الْمَمْلُوكِ لِسَيّدِهِ وَلَهُ حَقٌّ فِي كَسْبِ مُكَاتِبِه فَلَمْ يُتِمُّ التمليك ترجمہ اور ز کو نہ اپنے مد بر کودے اور نہ اپنے مکاتب کو اور نہ اپنی ام ولد کو کیونکہ تملیک مفقود ہے۔ کیونکہ مملوک کی کمائی اس کے مالک ہوتی ہے اور مالک کا اپنے مکاتب کی کمائی میں حق ہے پس تملیک پوری نہ ہوئی۔ تشریح مسئلہ اپنے مدبر کو زکوۃ دینا بھی جائز ہے مدبرخواہ مطلق ہو خواہ مقید ہومد بر مطلق وہ ہے جس کی آزادی کو مولی نے اپنی موت پر معلق کر دیا ہے مثلا کہا کہ تو میرے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہے۔ اور مد بر مقید وہ ہے کہ مولیٰ نے جس کی آزادی کو اپنی کس مخصوص قسم کی موت پر معلق کر دیا ہو مثلاً کہا کہ اگر فلاں بیماری میں مر گیا تو تو آزاد ہے اور اپنے مکاتب اور اپنی ام ولد کوز کو ۃ دینا بھی نا جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان تینوں صورتوں میں تملیک نہیں پائی گئی کیونکہ مدبر اور ام ولد من کل وجہ مملوک ہوتے ہیں اور مملوک کی کمائی اس کے موٹی کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور مکاتب کی کمائی میں مولیٰ کا حق ہوتا ہے پس ان کو ز کوۃ دینا گویا اپنے آپ کو دینا ہے اور اپنے مال کی زکوۃ خود اپنے آپ کو دینے سے ادا نہیں ہوتی ۔ کیونکہ زکوۃ ادا ہونے کے لئے غیر کو مالک کرنا شرط ہے اور یہ معنیٰ یہاں پائے نہیں گئے اس لئے ان کو زکوۃ دینا درست نہیں ہے۔
He said: And do not give (zakat) to his mudabbar, nor to his mukatab, nor to his umm walad, due to the lack of ownership transfer (tamlik), because the earnings of a slave belong to his master, and (the master) has a right in the earnings of his mukatab, so ownership transfer is not complete. Translation: And do not give zakat to his mudabbar, nor to his mukatab, nor to his umm walad, because tamlik is absent. Because the earnings of a slave belong to his master, and the master has a right in the earnings of his mukatab, so tamlik is not complete. Explanation of the issue: Giving zakat to one's mudabbar is also permissible (should read: not permissible) whether the mudabbar is absolute (mudabbar mutlaq, whose freedom is suspended on the master's death) or restricted (mudabbar muqayyad, whose freedom is suspended on a particular illness). And giving zakat to one's mukatab and one's umm walad is also not permissible. The proof is that in these three situations, tamlik is not found because the mudabbar and umm walad are completely owned slaves, and the slave's earnings are for the master, and the master has a right in the mukatab's earnings. So giving them zakat is like giving to oneself, and giving zakat to oneself does not discharge it. Because for zakat to be valid, making someone else the owner is a condition, and this meaning is not found here, so giving them zakat is not correct.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the text of al-Hidayah along with its Urdu commentary. It states that one should not give zakat to one's own mudabbar (a slave whose emancipation is suspended on the master's death), mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom), or umm walad (a slave woman who has borne a child to her master). The reason is that in all these cases, the master still has ownership rights over the slave's earnings, so transferring zakat to them does not constitute true ownership (tamlik) because the benefit ultimately returns to the giver. The commentary defines mudabbar mutlaq and mudabbar muqayyad, confirming that both are still slaves in the master's possession. The ruling is unanimous within the Hanafi school; there is no dispute mentioned. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as it comes from the core texts of the school.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose emancipation is suspended on the master's death, either absolutely (mutlaq) or conditionally (muqayyad).
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master.
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; a necessary condition for zakat validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid to give zakat to one's mukatab according to the Hanafi school?
A) He is rich
B) He is a non-Muslim
C) The master has a right in his earnings
D) He is a family member

Key Takeaway
Zakat is not discharged when given to one's own slaves because the condition of transferring full ownership (tamlik) is not met.

Giving Zakat to a Partially Freed Slave: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for partially freed slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on giving zakat to a partially freed slave, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of each view.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa sees the partially freed slave as a mukatab; Sahibayn see him as a free debtor—the tag of zakat changes with the legal characterization.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a concise intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The question is whether zakat can be given to a slave who has been partially freed. The two positions hinge on different analogies (qiyas) to established categories of zakat recipients—the mukatab (a slave with a freedom contract) and the free debtor (gharim). Understanding this debate will sharpen your ability to parse conflicting analogies within Hanafi fiqh and recognize the role of legal characterization in determining rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
State clearly what Abu Hanifa holds and what the Sahibayn hold regarding giving zakat to a partially freed slave. Use the source text to extract the exact ruling (permissible or not).
Notice that both imams are from the Hanafi school—this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Extract the underlying analogy (qiyas) for each view
Abu Hanifa compares the partially freed slave to a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to buy his freedom). The Sahibayn compare him to a free debtor (hurr madyun). Write down the analogy each uses.
The text explicitly states: 'like a mukatab' (Abu Hanifa) and 'a free debtor' (Sahibayn).
3
Understand the legal basis of each analogy
Why does the analogy matter? For Abu Hanifa, a mukatab is not a valid recipient of zakat because the master still has a claim on his earnings; ownership is incomplete. For the Sahibayn, a free debtor is a valid recipient (gharim is one of the eight categories). Trace the reasoning.
The key difference is whether the partial freedom creates a 'debt' (which qualifies) or an 'ownership share' (which disqualifies).
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Determine how each ruling affects the validity of zakat given to such a person. According to Abu Hanifa, the zakat is invalid and must be repeated; according to the Sahibayn, it is valid and discharges the obligation.
This practical difference is the 'fruit of the disagreement'.
5
Note the mufta bihi (operative position)
The text does not explicitly give tarjih, but in later Hanafi fatwa, the view of the Sahibayn (permissibility) is generally relied upon. Why might that be? Consider that the partially freed slave is considered free in many legal respects, and his obligation to the master is treated as a debt.
This illustrates how later muftis resolve intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا إِلَى عَبْدِ قَدْ أُعْتِقَ بَعْضُهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِأَنَّهُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْمُكَاتِبِ عِندَهُ وَقَالَا يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ حُرِّمَدْيُونَ عِنْدَهُمَا ترجمہ اور ز کوۃ نہ دے اس غلام کو جس کا بعض حصہ آزاد ہو گیا ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کیونکہ وہ ان کے نزدیک مکاتب کی منزلت میں ہے اور دونوں صاحبوں نے فرمایا کہ وہ اس کو زکوۃ دے سکتے ہیں کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک وہ مدیون حر ہے
And do not give (zakat) to a slave who has been partially freed according to Abu Hanifa, because he is like a mukatab in his view. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He may give to him because he is a free debtor in their view. Translation: And do not give zakat to a slave whose part has been freed according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because in his view he is like a mukatab. And the two Sahibayn said that he may give zakat to him because in their view he is a free debtor.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This is a concise intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of giving zakat to a partially freed slave (a slave who has been partially emancipated by his master). The text from al-Hidayah presents the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is not permissible to give zakat to such a person because he compares him to a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to buy his freedom), meaning the master still retains a right in his earnings as a proportion of his unfree status, so tamlik is not complete. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that it is permissible because they consider him a free debtor (hurr madyun) – a free man burdened with a debt (the remaining value of his freedom) – and it is permissible to give zakat to debtors. The text does not explicitly state which view is mufta bihi, but in the later Hanafi school, the view of the Sahibayn is often preferred because the partially freed slave is indeed considered free in many legal aspects, and his obligation to his master is a debt, which qualifies him as a recipient of zakat under the category of gharimun (debtors).

Key Terms
عبد قد أعتق بعضه (abd qad u'tiqa ba'dahu): A slave who has been partially freed; still partially owned by the master.
مدیون (madyun): A person burdened with debt; in this context, the partially freed slave owes the master for the remaining portion of his value.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has contracted to buy his freedom; the master still has a right in his earnings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, to what is a partially freed slave compared?
A) A free debtor
B) A mukatab
C) A mudabbar
D) A full slave

Key Takeaway
The characterization of the recipient's legal status determines the zakat ruling—here, the dispute turns on whether the partially freed slave is considered like a mukatab (Abu Hanifa) or like a free debtor (Sahibayn).

Wife Giving Zakat to Husband: Hanafi Position
Refuting permissibility of wife giving zakat to husband via hadith interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits a wife from giving her obligatory zakat to her husband and apply the hadith interpretation to distinguish between zakat and voluntary charity.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot be given to one's husband; the hadith permitting it refers to voluntary charity only.

In this lesson, we examine a debated issue: may a Muslim woman give her obligatory zakat (zakah) to her husband? While some schools permit it based on a hadith of Zainab bint Jahsh, the Hanafi school interprets the hadith differently. We will follow the Hanafi argument that the hadith applies only to voluntary charity, not obligatory zakat, and understand the proof from the inclusion of orphan children.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the clear ruling of the Hanafi school: a wife may not give her obligatory zakat to her husband. The act is invalid (batil) and the obligation remains.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Recognize that some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) cite a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted a woman to give charity to her husband and orphan children.
The opponent's apparent basis is the general wording of the hadith.
3
Follow the opponent's argument
Understand that the opponent takes the hadith at face value: if the Prophet allowed it, then zakat must be permissible to the husband.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response points out that the hadith includes giving to orphan children, which is unanimously prohibited in zakat. Therefore, the hadith cannot be about zakat; it must be about voluntary charity (sadaqat al-nafilah).
This is the key proof: the inclusion of orphans forces a restrictive interpretation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the Shafi'i view, a wife may pay zakat to her husband and the obligation is discharged. Under the Hanafi view, the payment is invalid and the zakat remains due; she must pay to other eligible recipients.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).

Source Text

کہتی ہیں کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم پر مہابت اور رعب القاء کر دیا گیا تھا یعنی آپ کی ذات اقدس پر رعب تھی لوگ آپ سے بات کرتے ہوئے ہیبت کھاتے تھے ) زینب کہتی ہیں کہ بلال باہر آئے تو میں نے کہا کہ تم رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس جا کر خبر دو کہ دروازہ پر دو عورتیں ہیں آپ سے پوچھنا چاہتی ہیں کہ کیا ان دونوں کی طرف سے انکا صدقہ دینا اپنے شوہروں اور اپنے یتیم بچوں کو کافی ہے اور یہ نہ بتلانا کہ ہم دونوں کون میں زینب کہتی ہیں کہ بلال نے رسول کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی خدمت میں حاضر ہو کر دریافت کیا رسول اللہ نے بلال سے کہا کہ وہ کون دو عورتیں ہیں بلال نے کہا کہ ایک تو انصاری عورت ہے اور ایک زینب ہے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کون کسی زینب ہے کہا کہ عبداللہ بن مسعود بیگم صدقہ کی بیگم میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ان دونوں کے لئے دو، دو اجر میں ایک قرابت کا اجر اور دوسرے صدقہ کا اجر ، اس تفصیلی حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیوی کے واسطے اپنے شو ہر کوز کو ۃ دینا جائز ہے۔ ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ روایت صدقات نافلہ پر محمول ہے یعنی عورت اگر نفلی صدقہ اپنے شو ہر کو دیگی تو اس کو دو ہرا ثواب ملے گا ایک صلہ رحمی کا دوسرے صدقہ کا۔ صاحبین کی طرف سے جو حدیث پیش کی گئی ہے اس سے بھی یہی ظاہر ہے کیونکہ زینب نے اپنے شوہر اور اپنے سابقہ شوہر کے یتیم بچوں کو دینے کے بارے میں دریافت کرایا تھا اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے دونوں کو دینے کی اجازت دی ہے حالانکہ اولادکو زکوۃ دینا بالاتفاق جائز نہیں ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ اس حدیث میں صدقات نافلہ مراد ہیں نہ کہ زکوۃ۔
They say that awe and majesty were cast upon the Prophet (peace be upon him)... Zainab says that Bilal came out, and I said to him: Go to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and inform him that there are two women at the door who wish to ask whether giving charity on their behalf to their husbands and their orphan children is sufficient, and do not tell him who we are... The detailed hadith indicates that it is permissible for a wife to give zakat to her husband. Our response is that this narration is interpreted as voluntary charity, meaning if a woman gives voluntary charity to her husband, she will receive double reward: one for upholding kinship and one for charity. The hadith presented by the two companions (Sahibayn) also shows this, because Zainab inquired about giving to her husband and the orphan children of her former husband, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted giving to both, even though giving zakat to children is unanimously impermissible. Thus, it is clear that the hadith refers to voluntary charity, not zakat.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The opponent (likely citing a hadith) argues that a wife may give her obligatory zakat to her husband. The Hanafi response interprets the hadith as applying to voluntary charity (sadaqat al-nafilah), not obligatory zakat. The proof is that the hadith includes giving to orphans, which is prohibited in zakat by consensus. Thus, the ruling stands: obligatory zakat cannot be given to one's husband.

Key Terms
صدقات نافلہ (sadaqat al-nafilah): Voluntary charity given for extra reward, not obligatory zakat.
زکوۃ (zakah): Obligatory alms due on wealth meeting nisab, one of the five pillars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school interpret the hadith of Zainab (RA) as referring to voluntary charity rather than obligatory zakat?
A) Because the Prophet (SAW) specifically mentioned it was nafil.
B) Because the hadith includes giving to one's own children, which is not allowed in zakat.
C) Because the hadith is weak in transmission.
D) Because the Hanafi school does not accept giving zakat to relatives.

Key Takeaway
A wife cannot discharge her zakat obligation by giving it to her husband; the hadith allowing it is restricted to voluntary charity.

Zakat Invalid When Given to One's Own Mudabbir, Mukatab, or Umm Walad
Ruling with proof: prohibition of giving zakat to one's mudabbir, mukatab, and umm walad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that zakat given to one's own mudabbir, mukatab, or umm walad is invalid, explain why tamlik is not achieved, and apply the illa to determine recipient eligibility.

Core Idea
Zakat requires complete ownership transfer; giving to a slave you own fails this condition.

This lesson addresses a subtle issue in zakat distribution: can you pay your zakat to certain slaves who are legally connected to you? The Hanafi school rules that giving zakat to your mudabbir, mukatab, or umm walad does not discharge the obligation. The reason is fundamental: zakat requires making someone else the owner of the wealth (tamlik), but these individuals do not have independent ownership from you.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its object
What act is being ruled upon? Giving zakat to one's own mudabbir, mukatab, or umm walad. The ruling: invalid (batil) — the zakat obligation is not discharged.
2
Find the legal cause (illa)
The text states the reason: lack of complete tamlik (ownership transfer). The illa is that these slaves' earnings belong to the master, so giving to them is like giving to oneself.
The illa is derived from the condition that zakat requires transferring ownership to someone else (tamlik ila ghayr).
3
Apply the qiyas
This is a qiyas jaliy: the original case (asl) is giving zakat to oneself, which is invalid. The new case (far‘) is giving to these slaves. The illa is shared: the wealth effectively remains under the giver's ownership.
Qiyas is explicit: 'giving zakat to them is like giving to oneself'.
4
Confirm the result
Therefore, zakat given to any of these three categories is not valid; the obligation remains on the giver until proper tamlik is achieved with an eligible recipient.
The ruling is unanimous within the Hanafi school and widely agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يَدْفَعُ إِلى مَدَتِرِهِ وَمُكَاتِبِهِ وَامَ وَلَدِهِ لِفُقْدَانِ التَّمْلِيْكِ إِذْ كَسُبُ الْمَمْلُوكِ لِسَيّدِهِ وَلَهُ حَقٌّ فِي كَسْبِ مُكَاتِبِه فَلَمْ يُتِمُّ التمليك
ترجمہ اور ز کو نہ اپنے مد بر کودے اور نہ اپنے مکاتب کو اور نہ اپنی ام ولد کو کیونکہ تملیک مفقود ہے۔ کیونکہ مملوک کی کمائی اس کے مالک ہوتی ہے اور مالک کا اپنے مکاتب کی کمائی میں حق ہے پس تملیک پوری نہ ہوئی۔
تشریح مسئلہ اپنے مدبر کو زکوۃ دینا بھی جائز ہے مدبرخواہ مطلق ہو خواہ مقید ہومد بر مطلق وہ ہے جس کی آزادی کو مولی نے اپنی موت پر معلق کر دیا ہے مثلا کہا کہ تو میرے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہے۔ اور مد بر مقید وہ ہے کہ مولیٰ نے جس کی آزادی کو اپنی کس مخصوص قسم کی موت پر معلق کر دیا ہو مثلاً کہا کہ اگر فلاں بیماری میں مر گیا تو تو آزاد ہے اور اپنے مکاتب اور اپنی ام ولد کوز کو ۃ دینا بھی نا جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان تینوں صورتوں میں تملیک نہیں پائی گئی کیونکہ مدبر اور ام ولد من کل وجہ مملوک ہوتے ہیں اور مملوک کی کمائی اس کے موٹی کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور مکاتب کی کمائی میں مولیٰ کا حق ہوتا ہے پس ان کو ز کوۃ دینا گویا اپنے آپ کو دینا ہے اور اپنے مال کی زکوۃ خود اپنے آپ کو دینے سے ادا نہیں ہوتی ۔ کیونکہ زکوۃ ادا ہونے کے لئے غیر کو مالک کرنا شرط ہے اور یہ معنیٰ یہاں پائے نہیں گئے اس لئے ان کو زکوۃ دینا درست نہیں ہے۔
He said: Do not give (zakat) to his mudabbir, his mukatab, or his umm walad due to lack of ownership transfer (tamlik), for the earnings of the owned (slave) belong to his master, and he (the master) has a right in the earnings of his mukatab, so the ownership transfer is not complete. ... Clarification: The issue is that giving zakat to one's own mudabbir is not permissible, whether the mudabbir is absolute or conditional... because in all three cases, ownership transfer (tamlik) is not achieved. The mudabbir and umm walad are fully owned, and the earnings of the owned belong to the master; the master has a right in the earnings of the mukatab. Thus giving zakat to them is like giving to oneself, and paying zakat to oneself does not fulfill the obligation. For zakat to be discharged, making someone else the owner is a condition, and this meaning is not found here.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The passage states that a person cannot give his obligatory zakat to his mudabbir, mukatab, or umm walad. The reason (illa) is the lack of complete ownership transfer (tamlik). The mudabbir and umm walad are fully owned slaves; their earnings belong to the master. The mukatab is partially owned; the master has a right to his earnings. Therefore, giving zakat to them is effectively giving to oneself, which does not discharge zakat because zakat requires transferring ownership to another person.

Key Terms
مُدَبَّر (mudabbir): A slave whose manumission is suspended upon the master's death, either absolute (mudabbar mutlaq) or conditional (mudabbar muqayyad).
مُكَاتَب (mukatab): A slave who has contracted with the master to pay for his freedom in installments; he is partially free and partially owned.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has given birth to a child of her master; she becomes free upon the master's death.
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership from the giver to the recipient, a condition for zakat validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid to give zakat to one's own mudabbir?
A) Because the mudabbir is already free.
B) Because the mudabbir's earnings belong to the master, so giving zakat to him is like giving to oneself.
C) Because the mudabbir is not a Muslim.
D) Because the mudabbir is wealthy.

Key Takeaway
Zakat requires complete ownership transfer; giving to a slave you own fails this condition, so the obligation remains.
