Zakat to a Partially Freed Slave: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat to mu'taq al-ba'd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on giving zakat to a mu'taq al-ba'd and explain the basis of each position using qiyas.

Core Idea
Giving zakat to a partially freed slave is disputed within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa prohibits it (like a mukatab); the Sahibayn allow it (as a free debtor).

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakat eligibility. The point of contention is a slave who is partially freed (mu'taq al-ba'd) and owes the remaining price to one of his former joint owners. The dispute turns on whether this slave is analogous to a mukatab (slave under contract for freedom) or to a free debtor. Understanding this qiyas is key to grasping the legal reasoning within the school.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the factual scenario
Imagine a slave jointly owned by two partners. One partner frees his share but is insolvent. The other partner can either free his share or make the slave work to pay the price. If the second partner chooses payment, the slave owes a debt. The legal status of this slave is disputed.
The slave is not fully freed; he is partially free and indebted to one partner.
2
Trace Abu Hanifa's analogy
Abu Hanifa considers the slave to be like a mukatab because the partner retains a right to the slave's earnings. Just as zakat cannot be given to one's own mukatab, it cannot be given to this slave.
The key is the ongoing financial claim that resembles the master's right in a mukatab's earnings.
3
Trace the Sahibayn's analogy
The Sahibayn view the slave as completely free but indebted. A free debtor is eligible for zakat. Therefore, giving zakat to this slave is permissible, just as one may give zakat to a debtor and then collect the debt.
They emphasize that the slave's freedom is complete; the debt does not create a master-slave relationship.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the zakat must be given to another eligible recipient; under the Sahibayn, it may be given to this slave. In later Hanafi practice, the Sahibayn's view is often relied upon for fatwa.
The mufta bihi is not explicitly stated here, but the trend favors the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا إِلَى عَبْدِ قَدْ أُعْتِقَ بَعْضُهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِأَنَّهُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْمُكَاتِبِ عِندَهُ وَقَالَا يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ حُرِّمَدْيُونَ عِنْدَهُمَا
ترجمہ اور زکوۃ نہ دے ایسے غلام کو جس کا کچھ حصہ آزاد ہو گیا ہے ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک کیونکہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ غلام بمنزلہ مکاتب کے ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس کوز کو دیدے کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک وہ آزاد قرضدار ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے ان میں سے ایک نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دیا۔ اور یہ آزاد کرنے والا تنگدست ہے تو شریک آخر اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دے یا غلام سے کمائی کرا کر اپنے حصہ کی قیمت وصول کرے۔ اگر شریک آخر نے اپنے حصہ کی قیمت لینا اختیار کر لیا تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ غلام اس شریک آخر کے حق میں بمنزلہ مکاتب کے ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک آزاد ہے مگر اس کا قرضدار ہے پس ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک چونکہ یہ غلام شریک آخر کے حق میں بمنزلہ مکاتب کے ہے اور اپنے مکاتب کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے اس شریک آخر کے واسطے اپنے اس غلام کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ یہ غلام پورے کا پورا آزاد ہو چکا ہے البتہ اس شریک آخر کا قرضدار ہے اس لئے یہ شریک آخر اگر اس کو زکوۃ دینا چاہے تو شرعاً جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کوئی شخص اپنے قرضدار کو اپنے مال کی زکوۃ دیدیے پھر اس مال سے اپنا قرضہ وصول کرلے تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اسی طرح شریک آخر کے لئے جائز ہے کہ وہ اپنے مال کی زکوۃ اس معتق البعض غلام کو دیدے۔
And do not give (zakat) to a slave some of whom has been freed according to Abu Hanifa, because for him it is like a mukatab. And they (the two companions) said: give to him, because for them he is a free debtor. ... Clarification: The scenario is a slave jointly owned by two persons; one of them frees his share but is insolvent. The other partner may either free his share or make the slave work to pay the price of his share. If the other partner chooses to take the price, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this slave is like a mukatab in relation to that partner, and giving zakat to one's mukatab is not permissible. According to the Sahibayn, the slave is completely free but owes a debt to the partner, so giving zakat to him is permissible, just as one may give zakat to a debtor and then collect the debt from the zakat wealth.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding giving zakat to a slave who is partially freed (mu'taq al-ba'd). The scenario: two partners own a slave; one partner frees his share but is insolvent. The other partner can free his share or take the price from the slave's earnings. If the second partner opts for the price, the slave becomes like a mukatab (according to Abu Hanifa) or a free debtor (according to Sahibayn). Abu Hanifa likens the slave to a mukatab, making zakat invalid; Sahibayn consider the slave fully free but indebted, making zakat valid. The mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated here, but the text gives both views.

Key Terms
مُعْتَقُ الْبَعْض (mu'taq al-ba'd): A slave who is partially freed (e.g., one of two joint owners freed his share).
مَدْيُون (madyun): A person who owes a debt; in this context, the partially freed slave owes the remaining price to the partner.
مُكَاتِب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission with his master and is obligated to pay a sum for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the slave is considered like a mukatab, and giving zakat to one's mukatab is invalid.
C) Because the slave is wealthy.
D) Because the slave is not Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of giving zakat to a partially freed slave hinges on whether the ongoing financial relationship is seen as akin to mukatabah (Abu Hanifa) or as a simple debt (Sahibayn).

Zakat to Slave of Wealthy, Minor Child of Wealthy, and Wife of Wealthy
Rulings on zakat eligibility for dependents of a wealthy person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on zakat eligibility for four categories of dependents of a wealthy person and explain the principle of imputed wealth.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot indirectly benefit a wealthy person; recipients must be personally poor, not deemed wealthy through another.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the boundaries of zakat eligibility by focusing on individuals connected to a wealthy person. The key principle is that zakat must not indirectly benefit a wealthy person through his dependents. You will learn four distinct rulings that hinge on whether the recipient is legally deemed wealthy through another's wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
Read the passage and list the four types of people discussed: the slave of a wealthy person, the minor child of a wealthy person, the adult poor child of a wealthy person, and the poor wife of a wealthy person.
2
Determine the ruling for each
For each category, state whether giving zakat is permissible or impermissible. Note the reasoning given: ownership transfers to the master, the minor is considered wealthy through the father, the adult is not, the wife is not considered wealthy through her husband.
3
Identify the exception
Note the exception for the mukatab (slave contracted for freedom) of a wealthy person. Why is this permissible? Because the Qur'anic category 'fi al-riqab' includes mukatab.
4
Extract the principle
Generalize: A person is considered wealthy through another's wealth only if they are legally dependent (slave, minor child). Adults and wives retain their own legal personality for zakat eligibility.
This principle is specific to Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَايَدْفَعُ إِلى مَسْلُوكِ غَنِي لِأَنَّ الْمِلْكَ وَاقِعٌ لِمَوْلَاهُ وَلَا إِلَى وَلَدِ غَنِي إِذَا كَانَ صَغِيرًا لِأَنَّهُ يُعَدُّ غَنِيَّا بِمَالٍ بخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ كَثِيرًا فَقِيرًا لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُعَدُّ غَنِيًّا بِيَسَارٍ أَبِيهِ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ نَفَقَتُهُ عَلَيْهِ وَبِخِلَافِ امْرَأَةِ الغَنِي لِأَنَّهَا إذَا كَانَتْ فَقِيْرَةً لَا تَعدُّ غَيَّةٌ بِيَسَارٍ زَوْجِهَا وَ بِقَدْرِ النَّفَقَةِ لَا تَصِيرُ مُوسِرَةٌ
ترجمہ اور کسی مالدار کے مملوک کو زکوۃ نہ دے کیونکہ ملک تو اس کے مولی کے لئے واقع ہوگی اور نہ دے مالدار کے بچہ کو بشرطیکہ وہ نابالغ ہو کیونکہ نابالغ بچہ اپنے باپ کے مال سے مالدار شمار ہوتا ہے۔ برخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ وہ بالغ ہو اور فقیر ہو کیونکہ بالغ اپنے باپ کے مالدار ہونے سے مالدار شمار نہیں ہوتا اگر چہ اس کا نفقہ اس کے باپ پر واجب ہے۔ اور برخلاف مالدار کی بیوی کے، کیونکہ بیوی اگر خود محتاج ہو تو اپنے شوہر کے مالدار ہونے سے مالدار شار نہیں ہوتی ہے اور نفقہ کی مقدار سے وہ مالدار نہ ہوگی۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مالدار کے مملوک کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے مملوک خواہ غلام محض ہو یا مد بر ہو یا ام ولد ہو، دلیل یہ ہے کہ مملوک کا ہر مال مولیٰ کی ملک ہوتا ہے پس اگر غنی کے مملوک کو زکوۃ دی گئی تو وہ مال زکوۃ غنی کی ملک میں داخل ہو جائے گا اور غنی کے لئے زکوۃ جائز نہیں اس لئے اس کے مملوک کے واسط بیجا جائز نہ ہوگی ہاں مالدار کے مکاتب کو ز کوۃ دینا جائز ہے اور وجہ جواز نص قرآنی و فِی الرّقَابِ ہے۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مالدار کے نابالغ بچہ کوبھی زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ نابالغ اولا د اپنے باب کے مال کی وجہ سے مالدار شمار ہوتی ہے اور اگر مالدار کی اولاد بالغ فقیر ہو تو اس کو زکوۃ دینا جائز ہے کیونکہ بالغ اولاد اپنے باپ کے مالدار ہونے سے مالدار شمار نہیں ہوتی اگر چہ اس کا نفقہ اس کے باپ پر واجب ہے مگر چونکہ یہ در حقیقت خود فقیر ہے اس لئے اس کو زکوۃ دینا جائز ہے اور اسی طرح مالدار کی بیوی اگر فقیر ہو تو اس کو بھی زکوۃ دینا جائز ہے کیونکہ بیوی ، اپنے شوہر کے مالدار ہونے سے مالدار شمار نہیں کی جاتی ۔ اور رہی نفقہ کی مقدار تو وہ اس کی مالدار نہ کر سکے گی یعنی مقدار نفقہ سے عورت مالدار نہیں ہوتی ۔ اس لئے زکوۃ دینا اس کو بھی درست ہو گا۔
And do not give (zakat) to a slave of a wealthy person because ownership accrues to his master; and do not give to a child of a wealthy person if he is a minor, because he is considered wealthy by virtue of his father's wealth. Unlike the case when he is an adult and poor, because an adult is not considered wealthy by his father's wealth even if his maintenance is obligatory upon him. And unlike the wife of a wealthy person, because if the wife is poor, she is not considered wealthy by her husband's wealth, and the amount of maintenance does not make her wealthy. ... Clarification: The ruling is that zakat cannot be given to a slave owned by a wealthy person, whether the slave is a mere slave, mudabbir, or umm walad, because all the slave's property belongs to the master, so the zakat would become the master's property, and a wealthy person cannot receive zakat. However, it is permissible to give zakat to the mukatab of a wealthy person due to the Qur'anic verse 'fi al-riqab' (for freeing slaves). Secondly, zakat cannot be given to a minor child of a wealthy person because the minor is considered wealthy through the father. But an adult child who is poor may receive zakat because an adult is not considered wealthy by the father's wealth, even if the father must pay maintenance. Similarly, a poor wife of a wealthy man may receive zakat because she is not considered wealthy by her husband's wealth; the maintenance owed does not make her wealthy.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage enumerates several rulings: (1) A slave owned by a wealthy person cannot receive zakat because any zakat given becomes the master's property, and the wealthy master is ineligible for zakat. This applies to all types of slaves except the mukatab, who may receive zakat based on the Qur'anic category 'fi al-riqab' (for emancipation). (2) A minor child of a wealthy father cannot receive zakat because the child is deemed wealthy through the father's wealth. (3) An adult poor child of a wealthy father may receive zakat because adult children are not considered wealthy by their father's wealth. (4) A poor wife of a wealthy husband may receive zakat because she is not considered wealthy by her husband's wealth. The maintenance allowance does not make her wealthy. These rulings are based on the principle that zakat must go to a truly needy person who is not deemed wealthy through another's wealth.

Key Terms
مَمْلُوك غَنِي (mamluk ghani): A slave owned by a wealthy person (one who possesses nisab).
صَغِير (saghir): Minor child considered wealthy through his father's wealth for zakat eligibility.
غَنِي (ghani): Wealthy person who owns nisab and is ineligible to receive zakat.
مُكَاتَب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract with his master to purchase his freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following can receive zakat from a wealthy person's household according to this passage?
A) The wealthy person's slave (ghulam).
B) The wealthy person's minor son.
C) The wealthy person's adult poor son.
D) The wealthy person's minor daughter.

Key Takeaway
Zakat eligibility depends on the recipient's personal wealth status, not the wealth of those upon whom they depend financially.

Giving Zakat to a Partially Freed Slave (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on giving zakat to a partially freed slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on giving zakat to a partially freed slave and explain the legal analogy (ta'lil) behind each position.

Core Idea
A partially freed slave is either a mukatab or a debtor — the zakat ruling hinges on this characterization.

The Hanafi school debates whether a partially freed slave (mu'ataq al-ba'd) can receive zakat from the co-owner who has not freed his share. Imam Abu Hanifa compares this slave to a mukatab, making zakat impermissible, while the Sahibayn consider the slave fully free but indebted, allowing zakat as a debt repayment. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace legal analogy in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Set the scenario
A slave is jointly owned by two persons. One co-owner frees his share but is insolvent. The other co-owner chooses to recover the value of his share from the slave's earnings. Identify the slave's legal status: still partly unfree and indebted to the second owner.
The scenario assumes the second partner takes the value, not frees his share.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and analogy
Abu Hanifa rules that it is not permissible to give zakat to this slave. His analogy: the slave is like a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) because he owes the value. Since giving zakat to one's own mukatab is prohibited, it is prohibited here.
The key ta'lil: the debt creates a relationship similar to ownership via the mukatab contract.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and analogy
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule that it is permissible. Their analogy: the slave is fully free but indebted to the giver. Giving zakat to a debtor is permissible, akin to giving zakat and then recovering the debt.
For Sahibayn, the slave's freedom is paramount; the debt does not re-enslave him.
4
Compare the illah (effective cause)
Abu Hanifa's illah: the slave owes money, creating a legal status similar to mukatab. Sahibayn's illah: the slave is free; the debt is a financial obligation, not a status. The practical difference stems from whether the debt changes the legal personality.
This is a classic example of how different characterizations of the same fact lead to different rulings.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa, the co-owner cannot give zakat to the slave; under Sahibayn, he can. The later mufta bihi position follows Sahibayn, allowing flexibility.
The dispute is legitimate; both have valid usul foundations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكوة اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم ترجمہ اور زکوۃ نہ دے ایسے غلام کو جس کا کچھ حصہ آزاد ہو گیا ہے ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک کیونکہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ غلام بمنزلہ مکاتب کے ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس کوز کو دیدے کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک وہ آزاد قرضدار ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے ان میں سے ایک نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دیا۔ اور یہ آزاد کرنے والا تنگدست ہے تو شریک آخر اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دے یا غلام سے کمائی کرا کر اپنے حصہ کی قیمت وصول کرے۔ اگر شریک آخر نے اپنے حصہ کی قیمت لینا اختیار کر لیا تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ غلام اس شریک آخر کے حق میں بمنزلہ مکاتب کے ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک آزاد ہے مگر اس کا قرضدار ہے پس ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک چونکہ یہ غلام شریک آخر کے حق میں بمنزلہ مکاتب کے ہے اور اپنے مکاتب کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے اس شریک آخر کے واسطے اپنے اس غلام کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ یہ غلام پورے کا پورا آزاد ہو چکا ہے البتہ اس شریک آخر کا قرضدار ہے اس لئے یہ شریک آخر اگر اس کو زکوۃ دینا چاہے تو شرعاً جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کوئی شخص اپنے قرضدار کو اپنے مال کی زکوۃ دیدیے پھر اس مال سے اپنا قرضہ وصول کرلے تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اسی طرح شریک آخر کے لئے جائز ہے کہ وہ اپنے مال کی زکوۃ اس معتق البعض غلام کو دیدے۔
Book of Zakat. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume Three. Translation: And do not give zakat to a slave whose some portion has become free, according to Abu Hanifa, because according to Abu Hanifa this slave is like a mukatab. And the Sahibayn said: give him zakat, because according to them he is a free debtor. Explanation: The form of the issue is that a slave is shared between two men; one of them freed his share, and that freed is insolvent. Then the other partner either frees his share or makes the slave earn and recovers the value of his share. If the other partner chooses to take the value of his share, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this slave is like a mukatab vis-à-vis the other partner, and according to the Sahibayn he is free but indebted to him. So according to Abu Hanifa, since this slave is like a mukatab vis-à-vis the other partner, and giving zakat to one's mukatab is not permissible, therefore it is not permissible for this partner to give zakat to this slave. And according to the Sahibayn, since this slave has become completely free, except that he is indebted to that partner, therefore if that partner wants to give him zakat, it is legally permissible, because it has become like a person giving his zakat to his debtor, then recovering his debt from that property – there is no harm in that. Similarly, it is permissible for the other partner to give the zakat of his property to that partially freed slave.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding giving zakat to a partially freed slave (mu'ataq ba'dihi). The scenario: a slave is jointly owned by two persons. One owner frees his share but is insolvent. The other owner has the option to either free his share or have the slave work to pay off the value. If he chooses to take the value, the slave remains in a contractual relationship. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this slave is likened to a mukatab (a slave under contract of manumission) with respect to the other owner, because he owes the value of the share. Since the owner cannot give zakat to his own mukatab, giving zakat to this slave is not permissible. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the slave is fully free but indebted to the owner. Thus giving zakat to this slave is permissible, as it is akin to giving zakat to a debtor and then recovering the debt. The commentary explains the reasoning of each party. The mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated here, but the Sahibayn's view is generally relied upon.

Key Terms
معتق البعض (mu'ataq al-ba'd): A slave who is partially freed, specifically where one of two co-owners frees his share and the other retains his share or takes its value.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission with his master, agreeing to pay a sum of money over time in exchange for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is giving zakat to a partially freed slave permissible?
A) Because the slave is considered fully owned by the giver
B) Because the slave is free but indebted to the giver, like giving zakat to a debtor
C) Because the slave is a mukatab and zakat to a mukatab is allowed
D) Because the slave is poor and deserving of zakat

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of giving zakat to a partially freed slave depends on whether he is legally classified as a mukatab or a free debtor – a dispute resolved in favor of the Sahibayn in later fatwa.

Prohibition of Zakat for Banu Hashim
Prohibition of giving zakat to Banu Hashim with hadith and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to Banu Hashim and explain the evidence from the hadith and the analogy with water.

Core Idea
Obligatory zakat is prohibited for Banu Hashim; voluntary charity is permitted.

This lesson examines why the Hanafi school prohibits giving obligatory zakat to Banu Hashim, the clan of the Prophet. The primary proof is a hadith in which the Prophet declares zakat like 'washings of people' and compensates them with a share of khums. A supporting analogy compares zakat to water used for impurity—rendered impure—while voluntary charity is like pure water for cooling. Understanding this ruling clarifies the honored status of Banu Hashim and the precise scope of zakat prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that giving obligatory zakat to Banu Hashim is prohibited (haram). Note that voluntary charity (sadaqah tatawwu') is excluded.
The prohibition is specific to fard (obligatory) zakat, not all charity.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet (SAW) said, 'O Banu Hashim, Allah has forbidden you the washings of people and compensated you with khums al-khums.' This explicit text (dalil) is a hadith ahad, but its meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalala) and forms the core evidence.
The hadith is quoted in the expanded commentary by Ibn al-Humam.
3
Analyze the analogy (qiyas)
The text draws an analogy: obligatory zakat is like water used to remove ritual impurity (which becomes dirty), while voluntary charity is like water used for cooling (which remains pure). Thus, zakat wealth is considered unfit for the noble lineage of Banu Hashim.
The analogy reinforces the prohibition through legal reasoning.
4
Distinguish between obligatory and voluntary
The prohibition applies only to obligatory zakat. Voluntary charity is analogized to pure water and is permissible for Banu Hashim. This distinction is crucial for practical application.
Banu Hashim may accept voluntary sadaqah, gifts, or bequests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا تَدْفَع إلى بَنِى هَاشِمٍ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ يَا بَنِى هَاشِمٍ إِنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى حَرَّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ غُسَالَةَ النَّاسِ وَأَوْسَاحَهُم وَعَوَّضَكُمْ مِنْهَا بِخُمْسِ الْحُمْسِ بِخِلَافِ التَّطَوُّعِ لِأَنَّ الْمَالَ هُهُنَا كَالْمَاءِ يَتَدَنَّسُ بِإِسْقَاطِ الْفَرْضِ أَمَّا التَّطَوُّعُ بِمَنْزَلَةِ التَّبَرُّد بِالْمَاءِ. ترجمہ اور بنو ہاشم کو بھی زکوۃ نہ دے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ اے بنی ہاشم اللہ تعالیٰ نے تم پر حرام کر دیا لوگوں کا دھوون اور ان کا میل کچیل اور اس کے عوض تم کو شمس کا ٹس دیا ہے برخلاف نفلی صدقہ کے کیونکہ مال اس جگہ پانی کے مانند ہے اسقاط فریضہ سے میل دار ہو جاتا ہی رہا نفلی صدقہ تو وہ پانی سے ٹھنڈک حاصل کرنے کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ تشریح بنو ہاشم کوز کو ۃ دینا بھی جائز نہیں ہے دلیل رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے علامہ ابن الہمام نے یہ حدیث ان الفاظ کی ساتھ ذکر کی ہے يا بني هاشم إِنَّ اللهَ كَرِهَ لَكُمْ غُسَالَةَ ايْدِى النَّاسِ وَأَوْسَاحَهُمْ وَعَرَضُكُمْ مِنْهَا بِخُمُسِ الْخُمْسِ یعنی اے بنو ہاشم اللہ نے تمہارے واسطے لوگوں کے ہاتھوں کے دھوون اور ان کا میل کچیل نا پسند کیا ہے اور اس کے عوض تم کو شمس کا خمس عطا فرمایا ہے یعنی مال غنیمت کے پانچ حصوں میں سے چار تو غازیوں میں تقسیم ہوں گے اور رہا ایک حصہ تو اس کے پھر پانچ حصہ ہوں گے ان میں سے ایک حصہ تو بنو ہاشم کا ہے اور باقی چار حصے دوسرے مصارف میں خرچ ہوں گے برخلاف نفلی صدقہ کے کہ وہ بنو ہاشم کو دیا جاسکتا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مال اس جگہ پانی کے مانند ہے پس پانی اگر فرض ساقط کرنے کے لئے یعنی حدث دور کرنے کے لئے استعمال کیا گیا ہے تو پانی گندہ شمار ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح جو مال فریضہ زکوۃ ساقط کرنے کے لئے استعمال کیا جاتا ہے وہ بھی میل کچیل سے لبریز اور گندہ شمار ہوگا۔ اور اگر کوئی خص غیر محدث ہو اور وہ پھر ٹھنڈک حاصل کرنے کے لئے پانی استعمال کرے تو وہ پانی پاک اور مطہر ہے حتی کہ اس سے وضولر نا جائز ہے اسی طرح نفلی صدقہ کا مال بھی پاک ہے بنو ہاشم کے لئے اس کا لینا جائز ہے۔
And do not give to Banu Hashim because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'O Banu Hashim, Allah has forbidden you the washings of people and their dirt, and compensated you with the khums of khums.' Contrary to voluntary charity, because the wealth here is like water, it becomes dirty by dropping the obligation. As for voluntary charity, it is like cooling with water. Translation: And do not give zakat to Banu Hashim either, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'O Banu Hashim, Allah has forbidden you the washings of people's hands and their dirt, and compensated you with the khums of khums.' That is, out of the five shares of war booty, four are distributed among the soldiers, and the remaining one share is further divided into five; one of those is for Banu Hashim, and the remaining four are spent on other recipients. Contrary to voluntary charity, it may be given to Banu Hashim. The proof is that wealth here is like water: if water is used to remove an obligation (i.e., to remove ritual impurity), it is considered dirty. Similarly, wealth used to discharge the obligatory zakat is considered filthy and dirty. But if a person who is not in a state of ritual impurity uses water for cooling, that water is pure and purifying, so that wudu from it is permissible. Similarly, the wealth of voluntary charity is pure; taking it is permissible for Banu Hashim.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of giving obligatory zakat to Banu Hashim (the clan of the Prophet). The primary proof is a hadith in which the Prophet said that Allah has forbidden them the 'washings of people' i.e., the charity that cleanses wealth, and compensated them with the khums of khums (a portion of the war booty). The commentary by Ibn al-Humam provides the wording. The analogy: obligatory zakat is like water used to remove ritual impurity – it becomes dirty. Similarly, zakat money is considered impure in the sense that it is taken to purify the giver's wealth, so it is not fit for the noble lineage of Banu Hashim. However, voluntary charity (sadaqah tatawwu') is like water used for cooling – it remains pure and can be given to them. Thus, Banu Hashim may accept voluntary charity but not obligatory zakat.

Key Terms
بنو ہاشم (Banu Hashim): The clan of the Prophet Muhammad (SAW) descended from Hashim bin Abd Manaf. They are prohibited from receiving obligatory zakat.
خمس الخمس (khums al-khums): One-fifth of one-fifth of the war booty, i.e., 1/25 of the total, which is allocated to Banu Hashim as compensation for not receiving zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is obligatory zakat prohibited for Banu Hashim?
A) Because they are wealthy and do not need zakat
B) Because the Prophet declared zakat to be like 'washings of people' which is unfit for their honor
C) Because they are not Muslims
D) Because they receive a share from the state treasury

Key Takeaway
Obligatory zakat is prohibited for Banu Hashim due to explicit hadith and analogy; voluntary charity remains permissible.

Defining Banu Hashim for Zakat Prohibition
Defining Banu Hashim and their mawali

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Banu Hashim and determine whether a mawla is included in the zakat prohibition.

Core Idea
Zakat is prohibited for Banu Hashim and their mawali alike.

Who exactly is a Hashimi? The answer matters because receiving zakat is prohibited for them. This lesson defines the five families that constitute Banu Hashim and extends the prohibition to their freed slaves (mawali) based on a direct Prophetic command.

Guided Path
1
List the five families of Banu Hashim
Identify the descendants mentioned: Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and Harith bin Abd al-Muttalib.
These are all sons of Abd al-Muttalib, not just the Prophet's immediate family.
2
Understand the basis for their prohibition
They are traced to Hashim bin Abd Manaf, the common ancestor of the clan.
Lineage defines the prohibition.
3
Examine the evidence for including mawali
The hadith where the Prophet told his mawla: 'You are our mawla' – denying him charity.
The mawla is treated as part of the clan for this ruling.
4
Distinguish from other Quraysh mawali
A Qurashi freeing a slave does not bring that slave under the prohibition; jizya is still taken from the freed slave.
The ruling is specific to Banu Hashim, not all Quraysh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وُهُمُ العَلِي وَال عَبَّاس وَ الجَعْفَرٍ وَال عَقِيلِ وَالُ الْحَارِثِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْمُطَّلِب وَمَوَالَيْهِمْ أمَّا هَؤُلَاءِ فَلأَنَّهُم يُنسَبُونَ إِلى هَاشِمِ بْنِ عَبْدِمُنَافِ وَنَسْبَةُ الْقَبْيلَةِ إِلَيْهِ وَأَمَّا مَوَالَيْهِمْ فَلِمَا رُوى أَنَّ مَوْلَى لَرَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم سَأَلَهُ اَ تَحِلُّ لِيَ الصَّدَقَةُ فَقَالَ لَا أَنْتَ مَوْلَانَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا اَعْتَقَ الْقُرَيْشِيُّ عَبْدًا نَصْرَانِيًّا حَيْثُ تُؤخَذَ مِنْهُ الْجِزْيَةُ وَ يُعْتَبَرُ حَالَ المُعْتَقِ لأنَّهُ القِياسُ والإِلْحَاقُ بِالمَولى بِالنَّصَّ وَقَدْ خَصَّ الصَّدَقَةَ. ترجمہ فرمایا کہ وہ حضرت علی، حضرت عباس، حضرت جعفر ، حضرت عقیل اور حارث بن عبد المطلب کی اولاد ہیں۔ اور ان لوگوں کے موالی بھی بہر حال یہ لوگ تو اس لئے کہ یہ ہاشم بن عبد مناف کی طرف منسوب ہیں اور قبیلہ کی نسبت ہاشم کی طرف ہے اور رہے ان کے موالی تو مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے مولیٰ نے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے دریافت کیا کہ کیا میرے لئے صدقہ حلال ہے آپ نے فرمایا کہ نہیں تو ہمارا مولیٰ ہے برخلاف اس کے جب کسی قریشی نے اپنا نصرانی غلام آزاد کر دیا تو اس آزاد شدہ غلام سے جزیہ لیا جائے گا اور آزاد کئے ہوئے کا حال معتبر ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ قیاس یہی ہے اور آزاد کرنے والے سے لاحق کرنا نص کی وجہ سے ہے اور صدقہ کو خاص کیا۔
He said: They are the family of Ali, the family of Abbas, the family of Ja'far, the family of Aqil, and the family of Harith bin Abd al-Muttalib, and their mawali. As for these, because they are traced to Hashim bin Abd Manaf, and the lineage of the tribe is to him. And as for their mawali, because it is narrated that a mawla of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) asked him: 'Is charity permissible for me?' He said: 'No, you are our mawla.' Contrary to when a Qurashi frees a Christian slave, where jizya is taken from him, and the status of the freed person is considered. Because this is the analogy, and joining to the master is by text, and charity is specified.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage defines the scope of Banu Hashim for the purpose of zakat prohibition. It includes five families: the descendants of Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and Harith bin Abd al-Muttalib. The reason is that they all trace lineage to Hashim bin Abd Manaf. Additionally, their mawali (freed slaves) are included in the prohibition. The proof is a hadith where a mawla of the Prophet asked about charity, and the Prophet told him that he (the mawla) is considered one of them (mawla means client). However, this does not apply universally to all freed slaves of Quraysh: if a Qurashi frees a Christian slave, that slave is still subject to jizya and is not considered a Hashimi. The general rule (qiyas) would be to consider the statue of the freed person, but in this case, due to the specific text (nass), the mawla of Banu Hashim is attached to them for the prohibition of zakat only.

Key Terms
موالی (مولی) (mawali (mawla)): Freed slaves of Banu Hashim; they are considered part of the clan for the prohibition of zakat.
قریشی (Qurashi): A person belonging to the Quraysh tribe. If a Qurashi frees a slave, the slave does not automatically become a Hashimi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A Christian slave freed by a Qurashi
B) A non-Hashimi Arab
C) A mawla of a Hashimi
D) A poor Qurayshi who is not Hashimi

Key Takeaway
Banu Hashim includes five families, and their mawali are also prohibited from receiving zakat, as established by a direct Prophetic narration.

Zakat Forbidden for Banu Hashim: Proof and Analogy
States the ruling and proof for prohibiting zakat to Banu Hashim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to Banu Hashim, cite the prophetic hadith as proof, and explain the analogy distinguishing obligatory zakat from voluntary charity.

Core Idea
Zakat is like dirty water; Banu Hashim are compensated with khums, making it haram for them.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Al-Hidayah: the prohibition of giving obligatory zakat to the Banu Hashim, the Prophet's clan. The ruling is based on a direct hadith and a striking analogy comparing zakat to dirty washing water. Understanding this distinction clarifies why voluntary charity is permitted for them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
What exactly is being ruled prohibited, and for whom? The text says 'do not give (zakat) to Banu Hashim'. Note that it specifically refers to obligatory zakat.
Banu Hashim are the descendants of Hashim, the Prophet's great-grandfather.
2
Memorize the proof text
The hadith is quoted directly: 'O Banu Hashim, indeed Allah has forbidden upon you the washings of people and their dirt and compensated you with a fifth of the fifth.' Commit the key words to memory.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Analyze the analogy
Why is zakat called 'ghusalah' (washing water) and 'awsakh' (dirt)? The commentator explains: wealth used for zakat becomes like dirty water because it is used to fulfill an obligation, which is compared to cleansing impurity.
This metaphor highlights the perceived impurity of obligatory charity for Banu Hashim.
4
Understand the compensation
Banu Hashim are compensated by being given khums al-khums (one-fifth of the fifth of war booty) instead of zakat. This substitutes the need for zakat.
Khums is a portion of war booty allocated to the Prophet's family.
5
Distinguish voluntary charity
The text explicitly says 'unlike voluntary charity' because voluntary charity is like cooling oneself with clean water – it does not carry the stain of obligation. Therefore, Banu Hashim may receive voluntary sadaqah.
This distinction is crucial to avoid misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا تَدْفَع إلى بَنِى هَاشِمٍ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ يَا بَنِى هَاشِمٍ إِنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى حَرَّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ غُسَالَةَ النَّاسِ وَأَوْسَاحَهُم وَعَوَّضَكُمْ مِنْهَا بِخُمْسِ الْخُمْسِ بِخِلَافِ التَّطَوُّعِ لِأَنَّ الْمَالَ هُهُنَا كَالْمَاءِ يَتَدَنَّسُ بِإِسْقَاطِ الْفَرْضِ أَمَّا التَّطَوُّعُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ التَّبَرُّد بِالْمَاءِ
And do not give (zakat) to Banu Hashim because of his (peace be upon him) saying: O Banu Hashim, indeed Allah has forbidden upon you the washings of people and their dirt and compensated you with a fifth of the fifth. Unlike voluntary charity, because wealth here is like water, it becomes dirty by dropping an obligation, while voluntary charity is like cooling oneself with water.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Prophet's hadith. The text prohibits giving zakat to Banu Hashim, using the analogy that zakat is like dirty water used for purification, whereas voluntary charity is like clean water for cooling. Banu Hashim are compensated by the khums (one-fifth of the fifth of war booty). The prohibition is specific to obligatory zakat, not voluntary sadaqah.

Key Terms
غُسَالَة (ghusalah): The dirty water used for washing, here metaphorically referring to the impurities of obligatory charity.
أَوْسَاخ (awsakh): Dirt or filth, referring to the perceived impurity of zakat money.
خُمْس الْخُمْس (khums al-khums): One-fifth of the fifth of war booty (i.e., 1/25 of the total booty), allotted to Banu Hashim as compensation.
تَطَوُّع (tatawwu'): Voluntary charity, which is permissible for Banu Hashim to receive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof used in the text to prohibit giving zakat to Banu Hashim?
A) A verse from the Quran
B) A hadith of the Prophet
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy with khums

Key Takeaway
Zakat is prohibited for Banu Hashim due to the Prophet's hadith and the compensation of khums; voluntary charity remains permissible.

Definition of Banu Hashim and Inclusion of Mawali
Defines Banu Hashim and includes mawali

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five families of Banu Hashim and explain why their mawali are also prohibited from receiving zakat.

Core Idea
Zakat is haram for Banu Hashim and their freed slaves — a text-based rule, not analogical.

This passage from Al-Hidayah provides a precise definition of who is considered Banu Hashim for the prohibition of zakat. It names five specific families and then addresses the status of their freed slaves (mawali). The ruling is grounded in a hadith where the Prophet explicitly told his mawla that sadaqah was not permissible for him. The text also contrasts this with the general rule for jizyah, highlighting that the annexation (ilhaq) of mawali is based on specific text, not qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five families
List the five lineages mentioned: the families of Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and Harith ibn Abd al-Muttalib. These are the descendants of Hashim ibn Abd Manaf.
Other families from Hashim are not included; only these specific lines.
2
Define mawali in this context
Mawali refers to the freed slaves of these families. They are considered part of the tribe for certain rulings.
The hadith 'You are our mawla' establishes this.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith of the Prophet's mawla asking about sadaqah, and the Prophet saying 'No, you are our mawla' directly prohibits sadaqah for mawali of Banu Hashim.
This is a textual (nass) proof, not analogy.
4
Contrast with the jizyah example
If a Qurayshi frees a Christian slave, the slave is not considered Qurayshi for jizyah; jizyah is taken based on the slave's original status. This shows that the rule of inclusion is specific to sadaqah.
Analogy (qiyas) would have extended the rule, but the text restricts it.
5
Summarize the scope
The ruling that mawali are included is limited to sadaqah (zakat) and does not apply to other matters like jizyah.
The text says 'wa qad khass al-sadaqah' – it is specific to sadaqah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وُهُمُ العَلِي وَال عَبَّاس وَ الجَعْفَرٍ وَال عَقِيلِ وَالُ الْحَارِثِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْمُطَّلِب وَمَوَالَيْهِمْ أمَّا هَؤُلَاءِ فَلأَنَّهُم يُنسَبُونَ إِلى هَاشِمِ بْنِ عَبْدِمُنَافِ وَنَسْبَةُ الْقَبْيلَةِ إِلَيْهِ وَأَمَّا مَوَالَيْهِمْ فَلِمَا رُوى أَنَّ مَوْلَى لَرَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم سَأَلَهُ اَ تَحِلُّ لِيَ الصَّدَقَةُ فَقَالَ لَا أَنْتَ مَوْلَانَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا اَعْتَقَ الْقُرَيْشِيُّ عَبْدًا نَصْرَانِيًّا حَيْثُ تُؤخَذَ مِنْهُ الْجِزْيَةُ وَ يُعْتَبَرُ حَالَ المُعْتَقِ لأنَّهُ القِياسُ والإِلْحَاقُ بِالمَولى بِالنَّصَّ وَقَدْ خَصَّ الصَّدَقَةَ
He said: They are the family of Ali, the family of Abbas, the family of Ja'far, the family of Aqil, the family of Harith ibn Abd al-Muttalib, and their mawali. As for these, they are attributed to Hashim ibn Abd Manaf, and the affiliation of the tribe is to him. As for their mawali, because it is narrated that a mawla of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) asked him: Is sadaqah permissible for me? He said: No, you are our mawla. Contrary to when a Qurayshi frees a Christian slave, where jizyah is taken from him, and the status of the freed slave is considered, because that is the analogy, and the annexation to the mawla is by text, and it is specific to sadaqah.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This is a definition passage that identifies the specific families included in Banu Hashim: the offspring of Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and Harith ibn Abd al-Muttalib. Their freed slaves (mawali) are also included based on the hadith of Abu Rafi' that a mawla is considered part of the tribe. The text then contrasts this with the case of a Qurayshi freeing a Christian slave: here, the slave is not treated as Qurayshi for jizyah, but rather jizyah is taken based on the slave's original status. This shows that the rule of inclusion by mawali is specific to sadaqah and not generalizable by qiyas.

Key Terms
مَوَالِي (mawali): Freed slaves who are considered part of the tribe of their former masters for certain rulings like sadaqah.
جِزْيَة (jizyah): Poll tax levied on non-Muslim citizens of the Islamic state.
قِيَاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used in legal deduction, contrasted here with text-based ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) The poor of any tribe

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of zakat extends to the five specified families of Banu Hashim and their freed slaves, based on a direct prophetic hadith, and this rule is specific to sadaqah and not generalizable by analogy.

Exception for Abu Lahab's Descendants from Zakat Prohibition
Explains why Abu Lahab's offspring can receive zakat despite being Hashimi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for Muslim descendants of Abu Lahab and explain the rationale based on the honor (ikram) cause.

Core Idea
The prohibition on zakat for Banu Hashim is based on honor, not blood; thus Abu Lahab's descendants are excepted.

This passage addresses a specific exception within the general rule that Banu Hashim cannot receive zakat. The commentator explains that the prohibition is linked to the honor earned by the Prophet's family for their support, and since Abu Lahab opposed the Prophet, his family does not share that honor, making zakat permissible for his Muslim descendants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule and Exception
State the general Hanafi rule that Banu Hashim are prohibited from receiving zakat, and that this passage provides an exception for the descendants of Abu Lahab.
2
Understand the Rationale (Illah)
The prohibition is based on 'ikram' (honor) due to the support Banu Hashim gave to the Prophet. Recognize that this cause is not present in Abu Lahab's line.
3
Apply the Rationale to Abu Lahab
Abu Lahab harmed the Prophet, so he forfeited the honor. Consequently, his descendants do not share in the cause of prohibition.
4
Derive the Ruling for His Descendants
Since the cause is absent, the ruling of prohibition does not apply. Thus, if a descendant of Abu Lahab is Muslim, zakat is permissible (mubah) for them.
Ensure the condition of being Muslim is met, as zakat is only for Muslims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابولہب جو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا چا ہے اور ہاشم بن عبد مناف کی اولاد میں سے ہے اگر اس کی اولاد میں کوئی مسلمان ہو تو اس کے لئے صدقہ حلال ہے۔ کیونکہ بنو ہاشم کے لئے صدقہ ان کے اکرام کے پیش نظر حرام کیا گیا ہے اور یہ اکرام اولاً تو آباء کے لئے ثابت ہے پھر ان کے واسطے سے ان کی اولاد کے لئے ثابت ہے۔ اور بنو ہاشم کا اکرام اس لئے ضروری کیا گیا ہے کہ انہوں نے جاہلیت اور اسلام کے زمانہ میں رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی نصرت اور مدد کی ہے اور بد بخت ابولہب نے معصوم نبی کو اذیت ناک تکلیفیں پہنچائی ہیں اس لئے نہ وہ اکرام کا مستحق اور نہ اس کی اولاد اکرام کی مستحق ہے اگر چہ اس کی اولاد مسلمان ہو اس وجہ سے اس کی مسلمان اولاد کے لئے صدقہ حلال ہے۔
Abu Lahab, who is the uncle of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and from the offspring of Hashim ibn Abd Manaf, if someone from his offspring is Muslim, then sadaqah is permissible for him. Because the prohibition of sadaqah for Banu Hashim is due to honoring them, and this honor is established first for the forefathers, then for their children through them. The honor for Banu Hashim was made necessary because they supported and helped the Prophet in the time of Jahiliyyah and Islam. But the ill-fated Abu Lahab inflicted painful harms on the innocent Prophet, so neither he nor his offspring deserve honor, even if his offspring are Muslim. For this reason, sadaqah is permissible for his Muslim offspring.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage provides a critical refinement to the general rule that Banu Hashim cannot receive zakat. The commentator explains that the prohibition is based on honor (ikram), specifically the honor earned by the Banu Hashim for supporting the Prophet. Abu Lahab, despite being a Hashimi, opposed and harmed the Prophet, thus forfeiting that honor. Consequently, his Muslim descendants are not included in the prohibition and can lawfully receive zakat. This is an exception grounded in the rationale of the ruling.

Key Terms
إكرام (ikram): Honor or respect, which is the underlying cause (illah) for prohibiting zakat to Banu Hashim according to this commentary.
أبو لهب (Abu Lahab): An uncle of the Prophet who opposed Islam and is mentioned in Surah al-Masad.
بني هاشم (Banu Hashim): The clan of the Prophet, generally prohibited from receiving zakat in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are the Muslim descendants of Abu Lahab allowed to receive zakat according to the passage?
A) Because Abu Lahab was a companion of the Prophet
B) Because Abu Lahab died a Muslim
C) Because Abu Lahab opposed the Prophet, so his descendants do not share in the honor that prohibits zakat
D) Because all descendants of Hashim are allowed to receive zakat

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits zakat for Muslim descendants of Abu Lahab because the prohibition's cause (honor) is absent in their lineage.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Banu Hashim and Prohibition of Sadaqah
Definition and ruling on Banu Hashim and mawali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Banu Hashim, identify which individuals and groups are included in the prohibition of receiving sadaqah, and state the Hanafi position including the exception for Abu Lahab's descendants.

Core Idea
Sadaqah is haram for Banu Hashim and their mawali — the mawla of a people is one of them.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah defines precisely who belongs to Banu Hashim and clarifies the ruling on sadaqah (obligatory charity) for them and their freed slaves. The ruling is based on a hadith that establishes the mawla as part of the tribe. We also learn that the honor of being exempt from sadaqah does not extend to the line of Abu Lahab, who opposed the Prophet. Understanding this definition is essential for correctly distributing zakat.

Guided Path
1
Define Banu Hashim
List the individuals and families included: Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, 'Aqil, Harith ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib, their offspring, and their freed slaves (mawali). All are attributed to Hashim ibn 'Abd Manaf.
The definition includes both paternal and maternal descendants of Ali.
2
Identify the ruling for Banu Hashim
State that sadaqah (obligatory charity like zakat) is haram for all these individuals and their mawali, based on the hadith that prohibits sadaqah for the Prophet's family.
The prohibition is specific to obligatory sadaqah; voluntary sadaqah is allowed.
3
Examine the hadith proof
Read the hadith from Abu Dawud: 'The mawla of a people is one of themselves, and sadaqah is not lawful for us.' Understand how it proves the inclusion of mawali and the prohibition.
The phrase 'لا تحل' indicates a clear prohibition.
4
Note the exception for Abu Lahab's line
Recognize that Abu Lahab and his Muslim descendants are not included in the prohibition because he actively harmed the Prophet, thus losing the honor that exempts from sadaqah.
This exception shows the wisdom behind the ruling: honor based on support.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school agrees that sadaqah is haram for Banu Hashim but disagrees on including mawali. Note this as a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The difference stems from interpretation of 'mawla al-qawm min anfusihim'.

کے ایک شخص کو صدقات وصول کرنے پر عامل مقرر کیا۔ اس نے ابورافع سے کہا کہ میرے ساتھ چل تا کہ صدقات میں سے تجھ کو بھی حاصل ہوا ابو رافع نے کہا کہ نہیں یہاں تک کہ میں رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس جا واسطے سے ان کی اولاد کے لئے ثابت ہے۔ اور بنو ہاشم کا اکرام اس لئے ضروری کیا گیا ہے کہ انہوں نے جاہلیت اور اسلام کے زمانہ میں رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی نصرت اور مدد کی ہے اور بد بخت ابولہب نے بَخِلافِ مَا إِذَا عُتَقَ الْقُرَيْشِ ... الخ سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں کہا گیا کہ قوم کا مولیٰ ( آزاد کردہ غلام ) اسی قوم میں سے شمار ہوتا ہے پس اس قاعدہ کے تحت اگر کسی قریشی نے غیر مسلم غلام آزاد کر دیا تو اس غلام پر جزیہ واجب نہ ہونا چاہئے تھا کیونکہ قریشی پر جزیہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ حالانکہ قریشی کے آزاد کردہ نصرانی غلام پر جز یہ واجب کیا گیا ہے۔ جواب معتق (بلح التاء ) یعنی آزاد کردہ غلام کے حال کا اعتبار ہے کیونکہ قیاس یہی ہے یعنی قیاس یہی ہے کہ آزاد کردہ غلام کو آزاد کرنے والے کے ساتھ کسی بھی حالت میں لاحق نہ کیا جائے اس لئے کہ دونوں بنفسہ اصل ہیں کیونکہ دونوں بالغ ہیں عاقل ہیں اور آزاد ہیں۔ اور شریعت کے مکلف ہیں اور رہا یہ حرمت صدقہ میں آزاد کردہ غلام کو مولی یعنی آزاد کرنے والے کے ساتھ کیوں لاحق کیا گیا ہے سو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ
الحاق خلاف قياس نص مَولَى الْقَوْمِ مِنْ اَنفُسِهِمْ سے ثابت ہے اس لئے یہ اپنے مورد پر منحصر رہے گا۔ اس سے متجاوز نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Zakat. Explanation: In this passage it is stated who Banu Hashim are. He said: The offspring of Ali, whether from Fatima or other wives, and Ali himself are included in Banu Hashim. And the offspring of Abbas, and Abbas himself, and Ja'far and his offspring, and 'Aqil and his offspring, and Harith ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib and his offspring, and their freed slaves are all included in Banu Hashim. These persons and their offspring are Banu Hashim because they are all attributed to the great grandfather of the Prophet (SAW), Hashim ibn Manaf, and the tribe of Banu Hashim, attributed to Hashim ibn 'Abd Manaf, is called Hashimi. And their mawali, i.e., freed slaves, are called Hashimi because in Abu Dawud there is a detailed narration: from Abu Rafi', the freed slave of the Messenger of Allah (SAW), that the Prophet (SAW) sent a man from Banu Makhzum to collect sadaqah. He said to Abu Rafi': 'Accompany me so you may get some of it.' He said: 'Not until I ask the Prophet (SAW).' So he went to the Prophet and asked, and he said: 'The mawla of a people is one of themselves, and sadaqah is not lawful for us.' The freed slave of the Prophet, Abu Rafi', narrated that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) appointed a man from Banu Makhzum as an agent to collect sadaqat. He said to Abu Rafi': 'Come with me so you may also get some of the sadaqat.' Abu Rafi' said: 'No, until I go and ask the Messenger of Allah.' Then Abu Rafi' went to the court of the Prophet and asked: 'Is sadaqah lawful for me?' The Prophet said: 'The mawla of a people is one of themselves, and sadaqah is not lawful for us.' That is, since the mawali of Banu Hashim are included in Banu Hashim, sadaqah will not be lawful for them just as for Banu Hashim. Note that Abu Lahab is the uncle of the Prophet (SAW) and is from the offspring of Hashim ibn 'Abd Manaf; if any of his offspring is Muslim, sadaqah is lawful for him. Because sadaqah was made haram for Banu Hashim due to their honor, and this honor is established first for the fathers, then through them for their offspring. And honoring Banu Hashim was made necessary because they aided and helped the Prophet (SAW) in the times of Jahiliyyah and Islam, whereas the wretched Abu Lahab caused painful troubles to the innocent Prophet; thus he is not deserving of honor, nor is his offspring, even if they are Muslims; therefore sadaqah is lawful for his Muslim offspring.
Contrary to the case when a Qurayshi frees a slave... from here is the answer to a question. The question is: The hadith said that the mawla (freed slave) of a people is counted as one of them. So based on this rule, if a Qurayshi freed a non-Muslim slave, jizya should not be obligatory on that slave because jizya is not obligatory on a Qurayshi. Yet jizya is made obligatory on a Christian slave freed by a Qurayshi. The answer: The consideration is of the freed slave's own condition (with the letter 'ta'), because analogy is this: that the freed slave is not attached to the manumitter in any state, because each is an original entity in himself, as both are adult, sane, and free, and are obligated by Shari'ah. As for why in the prohibition of sadaqah the freed slave is attached to the manumitter, the answer is that this attachment is contrary to analogy, established by the text 'Mawla al-qawm min anfusihim', so it will be confined to its own context and will not be extended beyond it.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It first defines Banu Hashim: the descendants of Hashim ibn 'Abd Manaf, including the Prophet's family members like Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, 'Aqil, and Harith, and their offspring and freed slaves. The ruling is that sadaqah (obligatory charity like zakat) is haram for Banu Hashim and their mawali (freed slaves) based on a hadith from Abu Dawud. The hadith shows that the mawla of a people is considered part of that people, so the prohibition applies to them as well. An exception is made for the descendants of Abu Lahab, who actively harmed the Prophet and thus are not included in this honor—their Muslim descendants may receive sadaqah. The passage then addresses a potential objection: if the hadith makes a mawla part of the tribe, why doesn't a Qurayshi's freed slave get exemption from jizya? The answer distinguishes the hadith as a text (nass) that is specific to the ruling on sadaqah and not to be extended by analogy to other rulings like jizya. The general principle is that each individual's ruling is based on their own status, not their patron's.

Key Terms
بنو ہاشم (Banu Hashim): The descendants of Hashim ibn 'Abd Manaf, the great-grandfather of the Prophet Muhammad, including the families of Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, 'Aqil, and their freed slaves.
مولی (mawla): A freed slave who is considered part of the tribe of the manumitter for certain rulings, such as the prohibition of sadaqah.
صدقہ (sadaqah): Obligatory charity such as zakat; here it specifically refers to obligatory sadaqah that is forbidden for the Prophet's family.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following persons is prohibited from receiving zakat?
A) A freed slave of a descendant of Abbas
B) A Muslim descendant of Abu Lahab
C) A non-Muslim relative of the Prophet
D) A freed slave of a Qurayshi

Key Takeaway
Sadaqah is haram for Banu Hashim and their mawali, except for the line of Abu Lahab, based on the hadith that attaches the mawla to the tribe.

Zakat — Almsgiving

The Limited Scope of the Hadith on Mawla
Usul point: scope of the hadith on mawla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the hadith 'mawla al-qawm min anfusihim' applies only to the prohibition of sadaqah and not to exemption from jizya, and apply the principle that a textual exception (khilaf al-qiyas) is confined to its own case.

Core Idea
A nass contrary to qiyas is confined to its own case — the mawla is attached for sadaqah but not for jizya.

This passage addresses a potential contradiction: if a freed slave is considered part of the tribe, why does a freed slave of a Qurayshi still have to pay jizya? The answer teaches a fundamental usul principle: when a text overrides analogy (qiyas), it is limited to the specific ruling and not extended by analogy. This lesson explores that principle and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection states: if the hadith makes the mawla part of the tribe, then a freed slave of a Qurayshi should be exempt from jizya, since Quraysh are exempt. Yet jizya is still obligatory on such a freed slave.
The exemption of Quraysh from jizya is a separate ruling.
2
Apply qiyas to the objection
The objection uses qiyas: asl = Qurayshi is exempt from jizya; far' = his freed slave; illa = being part of Quraysh; hukm = exemption. But this qiyas is rejected.
This is an attempted qiyas that the text blocks.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes the hadith as a text (nass) that is contrary to the default qiyas (khilaf al-qiyas). The default qiyas would treat each person individually. The hadith overrides qiyas only for sadaqah. It is not to be extended to other rulings like jizya.
The principle: a text contrary to qiyas is confined to its own case.
4
Identify the legal principle
The principle is that a nass that departs from qiyas is limited to its specific context (yakhuss bihi mahallihi). The hadith specifically addresses sadaqah, so it does not affect jizya.
This is a key usul principle applied in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Consider whether this hadith could be used to exempt a freed slave of a Hashimi from jizya if Hashimi is also exempt? The answer is no, because the hadith is limited to sadaqah. The exemption from jizya is based on different evidence.
The ruling on jizya follows general principles, not this specific text.

معصوم نبی کو اذیت ناک تکلیفیں پہنچائی ہیں اس لئے نہ وہ اکرام کا مستحق اور نہ اس کی اولاد ا کرام کی مستحق ہے اگر چہ اس کی اولا د مسلمان ہو اس وجہ سے اس کی مسلمان اولاد کے لئے صدقہ حلال ہے۔
بَخِلافِ مَا إِذَا عُتَقَ الْقُرَيْشِ ... الخ سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں کہا گیا کہ قوم کا مولیٰ ( آزاد کردہ غلام ) اسی قوم میں سے شمار ہوتا ہے پس اس قاعدہ کے تحت اگر کسی قریشی نے غیر مسلم غلام آزاد کر دیا تو اس غلام پر جزیہ واجب نہ ہونا چاہئے تھا کیونکہ قریشی پر جزیہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ حالانکہ قریشی کے آزاد کردہ نصرانی غلام پر جز یہ واجب کیا گیا ہے۔ جواب معتق (بلح التاء ) یعنی آزاد کردہ غلام کے حال کا اعتبار ہے کیونکہ قیاس یہی ہے یعنی قیاس یہی ہے کہ آزاد کردہ غلام کو آزاد کرنے والے کے ساتھ کسی بھی حالت میں لاحق نہ کیا جائے اس لئے کہ دونوں بنفسہ اصل ہیں کیونکہ دونوں بالغ ہیں عاقل ہیں اور آزاد ہیں۔ اور شریعت کے مکلف ہیں اور رہا یہ حرمت صدقہ میں آزاد کردہ غلام کو مولی یعنی آزاد کرنے والے کے ساتھ کیوں لاحق کیا گیا ہے سو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ
الحاق خلاف قياس نص مَولَى الْقَوْمِ مِنْ اَنفُسِهِمْ سے ثابت ہے اس لئے یہ اپنے مورد پر منحصر رہے گا۔ اس سے متجاوز نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Zakat. Explanation: In this passage it is stated who Banu Hashim are. He said: The offspring of Ali, whether from Fatima or other wives, and Ali himself are included in Banu Hashim. And the offspring of Abbas, and Abbas himself, and Ja'far and his offspring, and 'Aqil and his offspring, and Harith ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib and his offspring, and their freed slaves are all included in Banu Hashim. These persons and their offspring are Banu Hashim because they are all attributed to the great grandfather of the Prophet (SAW), Hashim ibn Manaf, and the tribe of Banu Hashim, attributed to Hashim ibn 'Abd Manaf, is called Hashimi. And their mawali, i.e., freed slaves, are called Hashimi because in Abu Dawud there is a detailed narration: from Abu Rafi', the freed slave of the Messenger of Allah (SAW), that the Prophet (SAW) sent a man from Banu Makhzum to collect sadaqah. He said to Abu Rafi': 'Accompany me so you may get some of it.' He said: 'Not until I ask the Prophet (SAW).' So he went to the Prophet and asked, and he said: 'The mawla of a people is one of themselves, and sadaqah is not lawful for us.' The freed slave of the Prophet, Abu Rafi', narrated that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) appointed a man from Banu Makhzum as an agent to collect sadaqat. He said to Abu Rafi': 'Come with me so you may also get some of the sadaqat.' Abu Rafi' said: 'No, until I go and ask the Messenger of Allah.' Then Abu Rafi' went to the court of the Prophet and asked: 'Is sadaqah lawful for me?' The Prophet said: 'The mawla of a people is one of themselves, and sadaqah is not lawful for us.' That is, since the mawali of Banu Hashim are included in Banu Hashim, sadaqah will not be lawful for them just as for Banu Hashim. Note that Abu Lahab is the uncle of the Prophet (SAW) and is from the offspring of Hashim ibn 'Abd Manaf; if any of his offspring is Muslim, sadaqah is lawful for him. Because sadaqah was made haram for Banu Hashim due to their honor, and this honor is established first for the fathers, then through them for their offspring. And honoring Banu Hashim was made necessary because they aided and helped the Prophet (SAW) in the times of Jahiliyyah and Islam, whereas the wretched Abu Lahab caused painful troubles to the innocent Prophet; thus he is not deserving of honor, nor is his offspring, even if they are Muslims; therefore sadaqah is lawful for his Muslim offspring.
Contrary to the case when a Qurayshi frees a slave... from here is the answer to a question. The question is: The hadith said that the mawla (freed slave) of a people is counted as one of them. So based on this rule, if a Qurayshi freed a non-Muslim slave, jizya should not be obligatory on that slave because jizya is not obligatory on a Qurayshi. Yet jizya is made obligatory on a Christian slave freed by a Qurayshi. The answer: The consideration is of the freed slave's own condition (with the letter 'ta'), because analogy is this: that the freed slave is not attached to the manumitter in any state, because each is an original entity in himself, as both are adult, sane, and free, and are obligated by Shari'ah. As for why in the prohibition of sadaqah the freed slave is attached to the manumitter, the answer is that this attachment is contrary to analogy, established by the text 'Mawla al-qawm min anfusihim', so it will be confined to its own context and will not be extended beyond it.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It first defines Banu Hashim: the descendants of Hashim ibn 'Abd Manaf, including the Prophet's family members like Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, 'Aqil, and Harith, and their offspring and freed slaves. The ruling is that sadaqah (obligatory charity like zakat) is haram for Banu Hashim and their mawali (freed slaves) based on a hadith from Abu Dawud. The hadith shows that the mawla of a people is considered part of that people, so the prohibition applies to them as well. An exception is made for the descendants of Abu Lahab, who actively harmed the Prophet and thus are not included in this honor—their Muslim descendants may receive sadaqah. The passage then addresses a potential objection: if the hadith makes a mawla part of the tribe, why doesn't a Qurayshi's freed slave get exemption from jizya? The answer distinguishes the hadith as a text (nass) that is specific to the ruling on sadaqah and not to be extended by analogy to other rulings like jizya. The general principle is that each individual's ruling is based on their own status, not their patron's.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic jurisprudence. Here, the default qiyas treats each free adult individual independently regarding obligations like jizya.
نص (nass): A clear textual evidence from Quran or Sunnah. Here, the hadith is a nass that overrides qiyas.
خلاف القیاس (khilaf al-qiyas): A ruling that contradicts analogical reasoning, established by a specific text (nass). Such rulings are not extended by qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a freed slave of a Qurayshi still required to pay jizya despite the hadith 'mawla al-qawm min anfusihim'?
A) Because Quraysh are not exempt from jizya
B) Because the hadith is weak
C) Because the hadith applies only to the prohibition of sadaqah
D) Because the freed slave is not a true mawla

Key Takeaway
A text that overrides qiyas is confined to its own context; the hadith on mawla applies only to sadaqah, not to jizya.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Zakat Given to an Ineligible Recipient: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat repetition after mistaken disbursement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which the Hanafi school holds that zakat given mistakenly to an ineligible recipient is valid without repetition, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Zakat given with diligent investigation (taharri) to a presumed eligible recipient is valid even if the recipient is later found ineligible — intention governs, not retrospective certainty.

When you give zakat, you must ensure it reaches a valid recipient. But what if you carefully investigate and later discover the person was not eligible? Does your zakat count or must you pay again? This lesson examines a classic Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on one side, and Imam Abu Yusuf on the other, focusing on the role of intention and investigation.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (no repetition) and the opposing view of Abu Yusuf (repetition required). Note the underlying rationale for each.
Abu Yusuf's position is based on certainty of error and possibility of avoidance.
2
Analyze the hadith proof (dalil naqli)
Examine the hadith of Ma'n ibn Yazid: the Prophet said, 'For you is what you intended.' Consider how this supports the position that intention and effort (taharri) suffice.
The hadith validates the giver's good faith despite the mistake.
3
Evaluate Abu Yusuf's qiyas
Abu Yusuf analogizes giving zakat to the wrong person to giving the wrong item (vessels/clothes). Understand why he thinks this analogy demands repetition.
He argues that the error is certain and could have been avoided through careful verification.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that knowledge of recipient status is by ijtihad, not certainty, similar to determining qiblah. The giver acts on predominant opinion (zann ghalib).
This analogy reframes the issue as one of practical diligence rather than absolute knowledge.
5
Identify the condition for validity
Determine that the relied-upon position requires taharri (investigation) and zann ghalib (predominant opinion) that the recipient is eligible. Without these, zakat is not valid.
The text distinguishes between acting with investigation versus doubt or mistaken belief of ineligibility.

Source Text

كسی کو فقیر سمجھ کر زکوۃ دی پھر وہ غمنی نکلا یا ہا شمی یا کافر نکلا یا اندھیرے میں دی وہ اس کا باپ یا بیٹا نکلا اس پر زکوۃ کا اعادہ نہیں ہے
قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ وَ مُحَمَّدٌ إِذَا دَفَعَ الزَّكَوةَ إِلى رَجُلٍ يَظْنَّهُ فَقِيرًا ثم بان انه غنى او هاشمی او کافر او دفع في ظُلْمَةٍ فَبَانَ أَنَّهُ أَبُوهُ أَوِ ابْنَهُ فَلَا إعَادَةَ عَلَيْهِ وَقَالَ ابويوسف عليه الاعادة لظهور خطائه بيقين و امكان الوقوف عَلى هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ وَ صَارَ كَالا واني و القِيَابِ وَلَهُمَا حَدِيثُ معن بن يزيد فانه علیه السلام قال فیه پایزید لک مَانَوَيْتَ وَيَا مَعْنُ لَكَ مَا أَخَذَتَ وَ قَدْ دَفَعَ إِلَيْهِ وَ ِكيلُ أَبِيهِ صَدَقَتَهُ ولان الوقوف على هذه الاشياء بالاجتهاد دُونَ القَطَع فَيَبْنِى الْأَمْرُ فِيهَا عَلَى مَا يَقَعُ عِنْدَهُ كَمَا إِذَا اشْتَبَهَتْ عَلَيْهِ الْقَبْلَةٌ وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ فِي غَيْرِ العَنى انه لا يُجْزِيهِ وَالظَّاهِرُ هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ وَهَذَا إِذَا تَحَرَّى وَدَفَعَ وَفِي اكْبَرِ رَأْيِهِ أَنَّهُ مَصْرَفْ أَمَّا إِذَا شَكَ وَلَمْ يَتَحَرِّ او تحرى فَدَفَعَ وَ فِي أَكْبَرِ رَابِهِ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِمَصْرَف لَا يُجْزِيهِ إِلَّا إِذَا عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ فَقِيرُ هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ
ترجمہ امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد نے کہا کہ اگر مزکی نے کسی آدمی کو فقیر سمجھ کر ز کو دیدی۔ پھر ظاہر ہوا کہ وہ آدمی مالدار ہے یا ہاشمی ہے یا کافر ہے یا رات کی تاریکی میں زکوۃ دی پھر ظاہر ہوا کہ وہ اس لئے وہ اشرفیاں ہیں جو تو نے لے لیں ۔ حالانکہ معنی کو اس کے باپ کے وکیل نے اس کے باپ کا صدقہ دیا تھا اور اس لئے کہ ان چیزوں پر واقف ہونا بذریعہ اجتہاد کے ہے ، نہ کہ بذار یہ یقین کے تو ان چیزوں میں بنائے کار اسی اجتہاد پر ہوگی جو اس کے نزدیک واقع ہے جیسے جبکہ مصلی پر قبلہ مشتبہ ہو جائے۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے غنی کے علاوہ میں مروی ہوا کہ جائز نہیں ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ تو وہی اول ہے یہ اس وقت تھا نہ ہوگی مگر جبکہ اس کو معلوم ہو گیا کہ وہ فقیر ہے یہی قول صحیح ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے کسی کوز کوۃ کا مصرف سمجھ کر ز کوۃ دیدی تو اب اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں: (۱) یہ کہ بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ جس کو زکوۃ دی گئی ہے وہ زکوۃ کا مصرف ہے۔ (۲) یہ کہ مزکی کو اس کا حال قطعاً معلوم نہ ہو سکا کہ جس کو زکوۃ دی گئی ہے وہ زکوۃ کا مصرف ہے یا نہیں ۔ (۳) یہ کہ مزکی کو معلوم ہو گیا کہ جس کو ز کو دی گئی ہے وہ زکوۃ کا مصرف نہیں ہے مثلا کہ جس کو زکوۃ کا مصرف خیال کر کے زکوۃ دی گئی ہے وہ مالدار ہے یا ہاشمی گھرانے سے تعلق رکھتا ہے یا کافر ہے یا مز کی کا باپ ہے۔ یا اس کا بیٹا ہے اول کی دوصورتوں میں بالا تفاق زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی اور تیسری صورت میں طرفین کے نزدیک تو جائز ہے چنانچہ طرفین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں دوبارہ زکوۃ دینا لازم نہ ہو گا۔ بلکہ جو دی جا چکی وہ کافی ہے اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس صورت میں زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی، بلکہ مزکی پر دوبارہ زکوۃ دینا لازم ہوگا۔ اور مزکی نے جو مال بطور ز کوۃ دیا ہے اس کو اس سے واپس نہ لے۔
If someone gave zakat to a person thinking he is poor, then he turned out to be rich, or Hashimi, or a disbeliever, or he gave in darkness and it turned out to be his father or son, there is no repetition of zakat upon him. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said: If he paid zakat to a man thinking him poor, then it became clear that he was rich, or Hashimi, or a disbeliever, or he paid in darkness and it became clear that he was his father or son, then there is no repetition upon him. Abu Yusuf said: Repetition is upon him because his error became certain and it was possible to ascertain these things, and it becomes like vessels and clothes. Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) proof is the hadith of Ma'n ibn Yazid, because the Prophet said in it: 'O Yazid, for you is what you intended, and O Ma'n, for you is what you took.' And he had paid to the agent of his father his father's sadaqah. And because ascertaining these things is by ijtihad, not by certainty, so the matter relies on what occurs to him, as when the qiblah becomes ambiguous to a person praying. And from Abu Hanifa regarding other than the rich, it was narrated that it is not valid, but the apparent position is the first. This is when he made an effort (taharri) and gave, and in his predominant opinion that it was a valid disbursement. As for when he doubted and did not make an effort, or made an effort and gave while in his predominant opinion it was not a valid disbursement, then it is not valid except if he knows that he is poor; this is the correct view.
Translation: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad said: If the zakat giver gave zakat to a person thinking him poor, then it appeared that that person was wealthy, or Hashimi, or a disbeliever, or he gave zakat in the darkness of night, then it appeared that he was his father or his son, then there is no repetition of zakat upon him. And Imam Abu Yusuf said: Repetition upon him is obligatory because his error became manifest certainly and it was possible to know these things, and this matter becomes like vessels and clothes. And the proof of both sides is the hadith of Ma'n ibn Yazid because the Prophet said in this matter: 'O Yazid, for you is the reward you intended, and O Ma'n, for you are the coins you took.' While Ma'n's father's agent had given him his father's sadaqah. And because knowing these things is by ijtihad, not by certainty, so the matter will be based on what occurs to him, like when the qiblah becomes ambiguous to the one praying. And from Abu Hanifa regarding other than the rich, it is narrated that it is not valid, but the apparent position is the first. This is when he made an investigation (taharri) and gave, and in his predominant opinion that it was a valid disbursement. But when he doubted and did not investigate, or investigated and gave while in his predominant opinion it was not a valid disbursement, then it is not valid except when he knows that he is poor; this is the correct view.
Explanation: The issue is that a person gave zakat to someone thinking him to be a recipient of zakat. There are three scenarios: (1) Later it became known that the one to whom zakat was given is actually a recipient of zakat. (2) The giver could not ascertain the status of the recipient at all. (3) The giver came to know that the one to whom he gave zakat is not a valid recipient, e.g., he is wealthy, or a Hashimi, or a disbeliever, or the giver's father or son. In the first two scenarios, zakat is fulfilled by consensus. In the third scenario, according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is valid; thus no repetition is necessary; what was given is sufficient. But Imam Abu Yusuf said that in this scenario, zakat is not fulfilled and the giver must repeat it, and he should not take back what he gave as zakat.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether zakat must be repeated if the recipient turns out to be ineligible. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that if the giver made a reasonable investigation (taharri) and had a predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) that the recipient was eligible, then the zakat is valid and no repetition is required, citing the hadith of Ma'n ibn Yazid where the Prophet validated charity given with the right intention despite a mistake. Abu Yusuf argues that since the error is certain and the real status could have been determined, the zakat is invalid like giving someone the wrong item (e.g., vessels or clothes). The passage also notes a conflicting narration from Abu Hanifa regarding other-than-rich, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the first. It further clarifies that if the giver acted without investigation (e.g., doubt) or had a predominant view that the recipient was NOT eligible, then the zakat is not valid. The commentary summarizes three scenarios: (1) recipient confirmed eligible, (2) status unknown, (3) recipient known to be ineligible. In (1) and (2), zakat is valid by consensus. In (3), Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say valid, Abu Yusuf says invalid.

Key Terms
زکوۃ (zakat): Obligatory alms tax, one of the Five Pillars, which must be given to specific eligible recipients.
اعادہ (i'adah): Repetition or remaking of the zakat obligation; i.e., paying zakat again.
تحری (taharri): The act of making a best-effort investigation or ijtihad to determine the correct ruling or fact.
ظن غالب (zann ghalib): Predominant opinion or strong probability that arises from evidence.
مصرف (masrif): Eligible recipient of zakat as defined by Shari'ah (e.g., poor, needy, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
