Zakat to a Non-Deserving Recipient: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Zakat validity when recipient not deserving

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Zakat given to a non-deserving recipient based on preponderant opinion, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Zakat given based on preponderant opinion (zann) is valid even if later proven wrong; the giver's effort suffices.

What happens if you give Zakat to someone you believe is poor, only to discover later they were wealthy, a Hashimi, a disbeliever, or even your own father? Did your Zakat count? The Hanafi school addresses this through an internal disagreement between the founding imams. This passage presents the positions, proofs, and conditions for the Zakat to be valid or requiring repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Hanafi positions
Read the first sentence: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say no repetition; Abu Yusuf says repetition is required. Note the specific cases: rich, Hashimi, kafir, father/son.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school itself.
2
Examine the proof for the majority position
The hadith of Ma'n ibn Yazid shows the Prophet (SAW) did not order repetition when charity was given to an unintended recipient. Also, the analogy to Qibla: just as ijtihad suffices for Qibla direction, it suffices for determining recipient eligibility.
The hadith is sahih but its implication (dalala) is zanni.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's counterargument
Abu Yusuf argues that since the error is certain and the giver could have investigated, the Zakat is invalid, like purification with impure vessels where investigation was possible.
He relies on certainty of error vs possibility of investigation.
4
Understand the condition of taharrī and preponderant opinion
The majority view applies only if the giver exerted effort (taharrā) and had a preponderant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) that the recipient was deserving. If the giver doubted or had the opposite preponderant opinion, the Zakat is not valid.
This condition is crucial: the ruling is not absolute.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text says 'the apparent (position) is the first,' meaning the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is relied upon. The hadith supports this, and it is the Zahir al-Riwayah.
Thus, in practice, Zakat is valid if based on sound assumption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ وَ مُحَمَّدٌ إِذَا دَفَعَ الزَّكَاةَ إِلَى رَجُلٍ يَظُنُّهُ فَقِيرًا ثُمَّ بَانَ أَنَّهُ غَنِيٌّ أَوْ هَاشِمِيٌّ أَوْ كَافِرٌ أَوْ دَفَعَ فِي ظُلْمَةٍ فَبَانَ أَنَّهُ أَبُوهُ أَوِ ابْنُهُ فَلَا إِعَادَةَ عَلَيْهِ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ عَلَيْهِ الْإِعَادَةُ لِظُهُورِ خَطَئِهِ بِيَقِينٍ وَإِمْكَانِ الْوُقُوفِ عَلَى هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ وَصَارَ كَالْأَوَانِي وَالْقِيَابِ. وَلَهُمَا حَدِيثُ مَعْنِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ فَإِنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قَالَ فِيهِ: يَا يَزِيدُ لَكَ مَا نَوَيْتَ وَيَا مَعْنُ لَكَ مَا أَخَذْتَ، وَقَدْ دَفَعَ إِلَيْهِ وَكِيلُ أَبِيهِ صَدَقَتَهُ. وَلِأَنَّ الْوُقُوفَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ بِالِاجْتِهَادِ دُونَ الْقَطْعِ، فَيَبْنِي الْأَمْرُ فِيهَا عَلَى مَا يَقَعُ عِنْدَهُ كَمَا إِذَا اشْتَبَهَتْ عَلَيْهِ الْقِبْلَةُ. وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ فِي غَيْرِ الْغَنِيِّ أَنَّهُ لَا يُجْزِئُهُ وَالظَّاهِرُ هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ. وَهَذَا إِذَا تَحَرَّى وَدَفَعَ وَفِي أَكْبَرِ رَأْيِهِ أَنَّهُ مَصْرِفٌ. أَمَّا إِذَا شَكَّ وَلَمْ يَتَحَرَّ أَوْ تَحَرَّى فَدَفَعَ وَفِي أَكْبَرِ رَأْيِهِ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِمَصْرِفٍ لَا يُجْزِئُهُ إِلَّا إِذَا عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ فَقِيرٌ هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ.
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said: When a person pays Zakat to a man he thinks is poor, then it becomes apparent that he is rich, or a Hashimi, or a disbeliever, or he paid in darkness and it becomes apparent that he is his father or his son, then there is no repetition upon him. Abu Yusuf said: Repetition is obligatory upon him because his error has become apparent with certainty and it was possible for him to ascertain these things, and it becomes like vessels and cloths. And for them both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is the hadith of Ma'n ibn Yazid, for the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in it: 'O Yazid, for you is what you intended, and O Ma'n, for you is what you took.' And indeed his father's agent had given his charity to him. And because ascertaining these things is through ijtihad, not with certainty, so the matter in these cases is based on what occurs to him, just as when the Qibla is ambiguous for him. And from Abu Hanifa regarding other than the rich, that it does not suffice, but the apparent (position) is the first. And this is when he exerted his effort (taharra) and paid, and in his preponderant opinion that he is a valid recipient. But when he doubted and did not exert, or he exerted but paid while his preponderant opinion was that he is not a valid recipient, it does not suffice unless he knows that he is poor; that is the correct position.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of Zakat when the payer later discovers the recipient was not deserving. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that if the payer gave Zakat based on a reasonable assumption (i.e., he thought the person was poor, or in darkness he thought it was a stranger), and later finds out the recipient was actually rich, a Hashimi, a disbeliever, or his own father/son, the Zakat is valid and need not be repeated. Their proof is the hadith of Ma'n ibn Yazid, where the Prophet (SAW) told Yazid he gets reward for his intention and Ma'n can keep the money given as charity, even though it was given to his son. Also, they argue that determining the status of a recipient is based on ijtihad, not certainty, so the payer's effort suffices, similar to determining Qibla direction. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that since the error is certain and the payer could have investigated, the Zakat is invalid and must be repeated, analogous to purification cases with impure vessels and cloths. The passage then clarifies conditions: if the payer had a preponderant opinion that the recipient was deserving, his Zakat is valid; but if he doubted or his preponderant opinion was that the recipient was not deserving, his Zakat is not valid unless he later confirms the recipient was poor.

Key Terms
تَحَرَّى (taharrā): To exert effort and judgment to determine the correct course of action; here, to determine if a recipient is deserving of Zakat through investigation and ijtihad.
ظَنَّهُ (zannahu): Strong assumption or predominant opinion, not mere doubt; here, the giver's belief that the recipient is poor.
إِعَادَة (iʿādah): Repetition of the Zakat payment; i.e., paying again because the first payment was invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the ruling if a person gives Zakat to someone he thinks is poor, but later discovers the recipient is his own son?
A) The Zakat is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The Zakat is valid and no repetition is required.
C) The Zakat is valid only if the son is also poor.
D) The Zakat is valid but must be given again as an expiation.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, if you give Zakat based on a reasonable assumption (taharrā) that the recipient is eligible, your Zakat is valid even if your assumption turns out to be wrong.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat Given to a Non-Deserving Recipient: Validity and Repetition
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat given to non-deserving recipient with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the validity of zakat given with ijtihad to a non-deserving recipient and identify the conditions under which repetition is required.

Core Idea
Zakat given with ijtihad is valid even if the recipient is later found non-deserving; repetition is not required.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether zakat must be repeated if the recipient is later discovered to be non-deserving. Imam Abu Yusuf argues for repetition, while the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that if ijtihad was performed with predominant suspicion, the zakat is valid. Understanding this dispute clarifies the role of ijtihad and predominant suspicion in zakat obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the contested ruling? Is zakat valid if given to a non-deserving recipient?
2
Examine Imam Abu Yusuf's argument
What proofs does he present? Certainty of mistake, possibility of verification, analogy to wudu/prayer cases with impure items.
3
Analyze the relied-upon position
What is the proof from hadith and analogy? Hadith of Ma'n ibn Yazid and qibla analogy.
4
Understand the narration from Abu Hanifa
How does it distinguish between types of non-deserving recipients? Rich vs. Hashimi/kafir/father/son.
5
Apply the conditions for validity
What are the conditions for zakat to be valid in these cases? Ijtihad, predominant suspicion, lack of certainty of non-deservingness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مزکی کو یقین کے ساتھ معلوم ہو گیا ہے کہ میں نے زکوۃ ادا کرنے میں غلطی کی ہے اور زکوۃ غیر مصرف میں دی اور مزکی کے لئے ان چیزوں پر واقفیت حاصل کرنا کہ جس کو زکوۃ دی ہے وہ مالدار ہے یا نہیں ، ہاشمی ہے یا غیر ہاشمی ، کافر ہے یا مسلمان، اس کا باپ یا بیٹا ہے یا نہیں ممکن بھی تھا پس جب ان چیزوں پر واقف ہونا ممکن بھی تھا اور مزکی کو یقین کے ساتھ اپنی غلطی کا بھی علم ہو گیا تو کہا جائے گا کہ مصرف زکوۃ نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اس کو زکوۃ ادا نہیں ہوئی اور جب زکوۃ ادا نہیں ہوئی تو اس کا اعادہ واجب ہوگا اور یہ بالکل ایسا ہے جیسے پاک برتن ناپاک برتنوں کے ساتھ مل گئے کسی نے تحری کر کے ایک برتن کے پانی سے وضو کر لیا پھر واضح ہوا کہ اس برتن کا پانی ناپاک تھا تو ایسی صورت میں وضو کا اعادہ لازم ہے اسی طرح اگر پاک کپڑے ناپاک کپڑوں کے ساتھ مل گئے اور کوئی ایسی علامت بھی نہیں جس سے ان کا پاک یا ناپاک ہونا معلوم ہو پھر کسی نے تحری کر کے ان میں سے کپڑے پہن کر نماز پڑھ لی بعد میں ظاہر ہوا کہ یہ کپڑے جن کو پہن کر نماز پڑھی ہے ناپاک ہیں تو اس شخص پر نماز کا اعادہ واجب ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح ان دونوں صورتوں میں وضو اور نماز کا اعادہ لازم ہے اسی طرح مسئلہ زکوۃ میں زکوۃ کا اعادہ لازم ہوگا۔ اور غیر مصرف میں دیا ہوا مال واپس اس لئے نہ لے کر جہت زکوۃ کا فاسد ہونا ادا کو نہیں توڑتا پس ادائے سابق علی حالہ باقی رہے گی لیکن طریقہ ادا کے فاسد ہونے کی وجہ سے اس پر دوبارہ زکوۃ دینا لازم ہوگا۔

طرفین کی دلیل امام بخاری کے بیان کے مطابق معن بن یزید کی حدیث ہے علامہ ابن الہمام نے فتح القدیر میں اور ملا علی قاری نے شرح نقایہ میں یہ حدیث ان الفاظ کے ساتھ ذکر کی ہے عَن مَعْنِ بْنِ يَزِيدٍ قَالَ بَايَعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَا وَ أَبِي وَجَدِّي وَخَطَبَ عَلَيَّ فَانْكَحَنِي وَخَاصَمْتُ إِلَيْهِ وَكَانَ أَبِي يَزِيدُ أَخْرَجَ دَنَانِيرَ يَتَصَدَّقُ بِهَا فَوَضَعَهَا عِنْدَ رَجُلٍ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ فَجِئْتُ فَأَخَذْتُهَا فَأَتَيْتُهُ بِهَا فَقَالَ وَاللهِ مَا إِيَّاكَ أَرَدْتُ فَخَاصَمْتُهُ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ لَكَ مَا نَوَيْتَ يَا يَزِيدُ وَلَكَ مَا أَخَذْتَ يَا مَعَنُ (بخاری) معن بن یزید کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے اور میرے باپ اور میرے دادا نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے بیعت کی اور آپ ہی نے میرے نکاح کا پیغام دیا پھر آپ ہی نے میرا نکاح کرایا اور میں نے ایک مسئلہ میں آپ سے مخاصمہ بھی کیا معن بن یزید نے اپنے اس تعارف کے بعد فرمایا کہ میرے باپ یزید نے کچھ اشرفیاں نکالیں تا کہ ان کو صدقہ کرے پس ان کو مسجد میں ایک شخص کے پاس رکھ دیا پھر میں ان اشرفیوں کو لے کر چلا آیا تو (میرے باپ یزید) نے کہا کہ واللہ میں نے تیری نیت نہیں کی تھی پس میں نے یہ معاملہ دربار رسالت میں پیش کیا تو آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اے یزید تیری واسطے وہ ثواب ہے جو تو نے نیت کی ہے اور اے معن تیرے لئے یہ اشرفیاں ہیں جو تو نے لے لیں۔ اس حدیث میں یزید کو اعادہ کا اور معن کو واپس کرنے کا حکم نہیں دیا ہے حالانکہ معن کو اس کے باپ یزید کے وکیل نے باپ کا صدقہ دیا تھا اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بعد میں اگر غیر مصرف میں زکوۃ ادا کرنے کا علم ہو گیا تو مزکی پر زکوۃ کا اعادہ واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ سابقہ زکوۃ ادا ہو گئی اگر کوئی شخص یہ کہے کہ ممکن ہے کہ یزید نے بطور نفلی صدقہ کے یہ اشرفیاں دی ہوں اور نفلی صدقہ بیٹے کے واسطے جائز ہے لہذا یہ حدیث طرفین کا مستدل کیسے ہو سکتی ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بلاشبہ یہ احتمال ہے لیکن رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول "لَكَ مَا نَوَيْتَ" میں "ما" موصولہ کی وجہ سے عموم سے یعنی ہر نیت کے صدقہ میں جواز ہے یعنی نفلی صدقہ کی نیت کی تو اس کا ثواب ملے گا اور اگر زکوۃ (صدقہ مفروضہ) کی نیت کی تو اس کا ثواب ملے گا۔ طرفین کی دوسری دلیل اور امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ چیزوں پر واقفیت حاصل کرنا ممکن ہے یہ بات مسلم ہے لیکن

ان چیزوں کا علم ظن غالب کے طور پر ہوگا نہ کہ یقین کے طور پر کیونکہ یہ بات بہت دشوار ہے کہ قطعی طور پر کسی کی محتاجی معلوم کی جائے لہذا ان چیزوں میں حکم کی بنیاد اسی اجتہاد اور ظن غالب پر ہوگی جو اس کے نزدیک واقع ہو گا حتی کہ اگر اس کے نزدیک یہ اجتہاد واقع ہوا کہ یہ شخص فقیر ہے تو اس کو زکوۃ دینے سے خدا کے حکم کی اطاعت ہو گئی اور زکوۃ ادا ہو گئی اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے نماز پڑھنے والے پر جہت قبلہ مشتبہ ہو جائے پھر اس نے تحری کر کے نماز ادا کی تو اس کی نماز ادا ہوگئی اگر چہ بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ اس نے صحیح سمت کی طرف منہ کر کے نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے کیونکہ بنائے کار اس میں اجتہاد پر ہے نہ کہ یقین پر لہذا جس طرف تحری واقع ہوگئی اس طرف نماز ادا ہو جائے گی، اسی طرح زکوۃ ادا ہوگئی اگر چہ بعد میں ظاہر ہوا کہ جس کو زکوۃ دی گئی ہے وہ زکوۃ کا مصرف نہیں تھا۔

حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ دینے کے بعد اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ جس کو زکوۃ دی گئی ہے وہ مالدار ہے تو زکوۃ ادا ہوگئی اعادہ کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ جس کو زکوۃ دی ہے وہ ہاشمی ہے یا کافر ہے یا اس کا باپ ہے یا اس کا بیٹا ہے تو زکوۃ ادا نہیں ہوئی بلکہ اس کا اعادہ ضروری ہے۔ اس رائے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غنی فی الجملہ زکوۃ کا مصرف ہے جیسے عامل اور سائی کہ مالدار ہونے کے باوجود اس کو زکوۃ کے مال سے دینا جائز ہے لیکن ہاشمی کا [؟] زکوۃ پینا [؟] حرام [؟] اور اس کا بیٹا اس کی زکوۃ کا قطعا مصرف نہیں ہے اس لئے مالدار کو فقیر سمجھ کر اگر زکوۃ دیدی تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی کیونکہ مالدار فی الجملہ زکوۃ کا مصرف ہوتا ہے اور باقی صورتوں میں زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی کیونکہ ہاشمی اور کافر وغیرہ کسی حال میں بھی زکوۃ کا مصرف نہیں ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ظاہر الروایۃ قول اول ہی ہے یعنی تمام صورتوں میں زکوۃ ادا ہو گئی جبکہ اس نے مصرف سمجھ کر زکوۃ دی ہو۔

صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ غیر مصرف میں زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کا ادا ہونا اس وقت ہے جبکہ زکوۃ دینے والے نے تحری کر کے زکوۃ دی اور اس کا غالب گمان یہ ہو کہ یہ شخص زکوۃ کا مصرف ہے اور اگر مزکی کو شک ہوا کہ وہ مصرف زکوۃ ہے یا نہیں لیکن اس کے باوجود تحری نہیں کی بلکہ بغیر تحری کے اس کو زکوۃ دیدی یا تحری کر کے زکوۃ دی اور ظن غالب یہ تھا کہ یہ زکوۃ کا مصرف نہیں ہے تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی ہاں اگر بعد میں ظاہر ہوا کہ جس کو زکوۃ دی ہے وہ فقیر ہے تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی اور یہی صحیح قول ہے۔ فوائد صاحب عنایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ کی چار صورتیں ہیں کیونکہ زکوۃ دینے والے نے اپنے مال کی زکوۃ بغیر شک اور بغیر تحری کے دی ہے یا اس نے زکوۃ لینے والے کے حال میں شک کیا ہے پہلی صورت میں زکوۃ ادا ہو گئی الا یہ کہ زکوۃ لینے والے کا غنی ہونا ظاہر ہو جائے کیونکہ اصل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ کے مال پر قبضہ کرنے والا فقیر ہو۔ اور دوسری صورت میں پھر دو صورتیں ہیں کیونکہ مزکی نے تحری کی ہوگی یا تحری نہیں کی ہوگی اگر تحری نہیں کی تو زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی۔ ہاں اگر یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ جس کو بغیر تحری کے زکوۃ دی ہے وہ فقیر ہے تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی کیونکہ جب مزکی کو زکوۃ لینے والے کے معاملہ میں شک ہوا تو اس پر تحری کرنا واجب ہو گیا پس جب اس نے واجب ہونے کے بعد تحری ترک کر دی تو فریضہ زکوۃ جو ادا کیا گیا ہے وہ ادا نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے اگر مصلی کو جہت قبلہ میں شک ہو گیا تو مصلی پر تحری واجب ہے پس اگر بغیر تحری کے نماز ادا کی تو نماز ادا نہ ہوگی ہاں اگر یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ وہ فقیر ہے تو زکوۃ ادا ہو گئی کیونکہ زکوۃ ادا کرنے میں فقر ہی مقصود ہے اور وہ بغیر تحری کے حاصل ہو گیا جیسے سعی الی الجمعہ فرض ہے لیکن اگر بغیر سعی کے نماز جمعہ ادا کی گئی تو نماز جمعہ ادا ہو جائے گی جیسے جامع مسجد میں اعتکاف کرنے والا بغیر سعی الی الجمعہ کے جمعہ پڑھتا ہے کیونکہ مقصود تو نماز جمعہ ہے نہ کہ سعی الی الجمعۃ اور اگر تحری کر کے زکوۃ دی تو
The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that the giver of zakat has become certain that he made a mistake in paying zakat and gave it to a non-deserving recipient, and it was possible for him to become acquainted with those matters: whether the one to whom he gave zakat is rich or not, Hashimi or non-Hashimi, disbeliever or Muslim, his father or son or not. So when it was possible to become acquainted with these things and the giver became certain of his mistake, it will be said that due to the recipient not being deserving, his zakat was not paid, and when zakat was not paid, its repetition becomes obligatory. And it is exactly like when pure vessels get mixed with impure ones; someone performed ijtihad and performed wudu with water from one vessel, then it became clear that the water in that vessel was impure. In such a case, repeating wudu is necessary. Similarly, if pure clothes get mixed with impure ones and there is no sign to distinguish them, then someone performed ijtihad and wore some of them to pray, and later it became clear that the clothes he wore for prayer were impure, then repeating the prayer is obligatory upon that person. Imam Abu Yusuf says: Just as in these two cases repeating wudu and prayer is necessary, similarly in the issue of zakat, repeating zakat will be necessary. And the wealth given to a non-deserving recipient is not taken back because the invalidity of the direction of zakat does not destroy the payment, so the previous payment remains as it was, but due to the invalidity of the method of payment, it becomes obligatory to give zakat again.

The proof for both sides is the hadith of Ma'n ibn Yazid according to Bukhari's narration. Allamah Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir and Mulla Ali Qari in Sharh al-Niqayah mentioned this hadith with these words: From Ma'n ibn Yazid who said: I pledged allegiance to the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him), I, my father, and my grandfather; he proposed for me and married me, and I pleaded a case to him. My father Yazid took out some dinars to give in charity and placed them with a man in the mosque. I came and took them and brought them to him. He said: By Allah, I did not intend you. So I pleaded my case to the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him), and he said: For you is what you intended, O Yazid, and for you is what you took, O Ma'n. (Bukhari) Ma'n ibn Yazid says: I, my father, and my grandfather pledged allegiance to the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him), and he proposed for me and married me, and I pleaded a case to him. After this introduction, Ma'n ibn Yazid said: My father Yazid took out some dinars to give in charity, so he placed them with a man in the mosque. Then I took those dinars and brought them to him. My father Yazid said: By Allah, I did not intend you. So I presented this matter to the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him), and he said: O Yazid, for you is the reward that you intended, and O Ma'n, for you are these dinars that you took. In this hadith, Yazid was not ordered to repeat, nor Ma'n to return, even though Ma'n was given his father's charity by his father's agent. From this hadith it is understood that if later it becomes known that zakat was given to a non-deserving recipient, repeating zakat is not obligatory upon the giver; rather, the previous zakat is valid. If someone says: It is possible that Yazid gave these dinars as nafl sadaqah, and nafl sadaqah is permissible for one's son, so how can this hadith be proof for both sides? The answer is: Without a doubt this possibility exists, but in the Prophet's statement "For you is what you intended" the word "what" (ma) is a relative pronoun indicating generality, meaning that for every intention of sadaqah there is permissibility; if he intended nafl sadaqah, he gets its reward, and if he intended zakat (obligatory sadaqah), he gets its reward. The second proof for both sides and the answer to Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that it is granted that acquiring knowledge of these matters is possible, but knowledge of these things will be by way of predominant suspicion (ghalabah al-zann), not certainty, because it is very difficult to know someone's need definitively. Therefore, the basis of the ruling in these matters is ijtihad and predominant suspicion that occurs to him. So much so that if ijtihad occurs to him that this person is poor, then by giving him zakat, obedience to Allah's command is achieved and zakat is paid. And this is like when the direction of the qibla becomes ambiguous for a person praying, then he performs ijtihad and prays; his prayer is valid even if he later finds out that he did not pray facing the correct direction, because the basis in this is ijtihad, not certainty. Therefore, he prayed in the direction his ijtihad led him, and similarly zakat is paid even if it later becomes apparent that the one to whom zakat was given was not deserving of zakat.

There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that if after giving zakat it becomes apparent that the recipient was rich, then the zakat is valid and no repetition is needed. But if it becomes apparent that the recipient was a Hashimi, a disbeliever, or his father or his son, then the zakat is not valid and repetition is necessary. The proof for this view is that a rich person is in some respects a recipient of zakat, like the 'amil (tax collector) and the sa'i (agent) who, despite being rich, it is permissible to give them from zakat funds. But a Hashimi [?] taking zakat is [?] forbidden, and one's son is absolutely not a recipient of his zakat. Therefore, if he gave zakat to a rich person thinking him poor, the zakat is valid, because a rich person is in some respects a recipient of zakat. In other cases, zakat will not be valid, because a Hashimi, a disbeliever, etc., are in no case recipients of zakat. Sahib al-Hidayah says: The apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) is the first opinion, i.e., in all cases zakat is valid when he gave it considering the recipient deserving.

Sahib al-Hidayah says: The validity of zakat when given to a non-deserving recipient is when the giver gave zakat after performing ijtihad and his predominant suspicion was that this person is deserving of zakat. If the giver doubted whether he is deserving of zakat but still gave it without ijtihad, or he performed ijtihad but his predominant suspicion was that he is not deserving, then in both these cases zakat is not valid. However, if it later becomes apparent that the one to whom he gave zakat is poor, then the zakat is valid. And this is the correct statement. Fawa'id: Sahib al-'Inayah says: There are four scenarios in this issue: either the giver gave zakat of his wealth without doubt and without ijtihad, or he doubted the condition of the recipient. In the first case, the zakat is valid unless it becomes apparent that the recipient is rich, because the default is that the one who takes possession of zakat wealth is poor. In the second case, there are two further scenarios: either the giver performed ijtihad or he did not. If he did not perform ijtihad, then zakat is not valid. However, if it becomes known that the one to whom he gave zakat without ijtihad is poor, then zakat is valid, because when the giver doubted the condition of the recipient, performing ijtihad became obligatory upon him. So when he abandoned ijtihad after it became obligatory, the zakat obligation that he performed is not valid. This is like when the direction of the qibla is doubtful for the worshiper, ijtihad is obligatory upon him; if he prays without ijtihad, the prayer is not valid. However, if it becomes apparent that he is poor, then zakat is valid because the purpose in paying zakat is poverty, and that has been achieved without ijtihad, just as going for Friday prayer (sa'y ila al-jumu'ah) is obligatory, but if one performs Friday prayer without going (e.g., if he was already in the mosque due to i'tikaf), the Friday prayer is valid because the purpose is Friday prayer, not the going itself. And if he gave zakat after performing ijtihad, then...

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of zakat given to a recipient who later turns out to be non-deserving. The text begins by presenting Imam Abu Yusuf's argument that such zakat is invalid and must be repeated. He argues that the giver now has certain knowledge of his mistake and could have verified the recipient's eligibility, drawing analogies to cases of wudu and prayer where impure items were used after ijtihad. He further states that the invalid method of payment does not undo the original payment but still requires repetition. 

Then, the text presents the hadith of Ma'n ibn Yazid as a proof for both sides. The hadith shows that the Prophet did not order the father (Yazid) to repeat his sadaqah nor the son (Ma'n) to return it, indicating that the charity was valid despite being given to a non-deserving person (the son). The text addresses a possible objection that the hadith may refer to nafl sadaqah, not zakat, by explaining that the Prophet's statement 'For you is what you intended' includes all intentions, so the same principle applies to zakat. 

Next, the text provides the answer to Imam Abu Yusuf's proof: while verification is possible, it is only by way of predominant suspicion (ghalabah al-zann), not certainty. The basis of action in such matters is ijtihad, analogous to determining the qibla direction. If one prays with ijtihad and later discovers error, the prayer is valid; the same applies to zakat. 

Following this, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa is mentioned, distinguishing between a rich recipient (zakat valid because rich can sometimes be eligible) and a Hashimi, kafir, father, or son (zakat invalid because they are never eligible). However, Sahib al-Hidayah declares that the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is the first opinion: zakat is valid in all cases when given with ijtihad. 

Finally, the text details the conditions for validity: ijtihad must be performed and must result in predominant suspicion that the recipient is deserving. If the giver had doubt but did not perform ijtihad, or performed ijtihad but suspected non-deservingness, the zakat is invalid unless it later becomes known that the recipient was actually poor. Sahib al-'Inayah outlines four scenarios, emphasizing the obligation of ijtihad when doubt exists and the default assumption that the recipient is poor.

Key Terms
تحری (taharrī): Ijtihad or effort to determine the correct ruling or recipient, often by seeking signs or using judgment.
ظن غالب (ghalabah al-zann): Predominant suspicion or strong probability that is sufficient for action in matters where certainty is unattainable.
مصرف (masraf): The legitimate recipient or category of recipients of zakat, as defined in the Quran (Surah al-Tawbah, 9:60).
مزکی (muzakki): The person who is obligated to pay zakat and actually gives it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) in this passage, what is the ruling if someone gives zakat to a person he believes is poor, but later discovers the person was actually a rich Hashimi?
A) The zakat is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The zakat is valid and no repetition is required.
C) The zakat is valid only if the giver had performed ijtihad.
D) The zakat is invalid unless the recipient was his father or son.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi relied-upon position is that zakat given with ijtihad and predominant suspicion of deservingness is valid and does not require repetition, even if the recipient is later found non-deserving.

Zakat — Almsgiving
advanced
12 min
Zakat Validity After Discovery: Ijtihad and Predominant Conjecture
Ruling on zakat payment with ijtihad and later discovery of ineligibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat validity when the recipient is later discovered ineligible, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute and the conditions for validity.

Core Idea
Zakat is valid if the payer made ijtihad and had predominant conjecture, even if the recipient was ineligible.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a practical dilemma: what happens when you pay zakat to someone you believe is eligible, but later find out they were not? The Hanafi school builds the ruling on the principle that obligations are based on predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) when certainty is impossible. We will explore the analogy to qibla ijtihad, the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa's narrations, and the detailed conditions for validity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of predominant conjecture
Recognize that the ruling in zakat distribution is built on ghalabat al-zann (predominant conjecture), not certainty, because determining poverty definitively is impractical.
2
Trace the analogy to qibla ijtihad
See how the author draws a parallel between zakat payment and prayer direction: if a worshipper prays after tahrri (estimation) and later realizes he faced the wrong direction, the prayer is valid. Similarly, zakat is valid if given after ijtihad.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) where the illa (effective cause) is reliance on predominant conjecture.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Distinguish between the two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: (1) all cases valid if ijtihad, (2) valid for wealthy but not for Hashimi, kafir, father, son. Then note the relied-upon position from Zahir al-Riwaya.
Sahib al-Hidayah declares the first narration as Zahir al-Riwaya and the mufta bihi.
4
Apply the conditions for validity
Review the four scenarios from al-Inayah: with/without doubt, with/without tahrri, and the effect of predominant conjecture. Understand when zakat is valid or must be repeated.
Tahrri is wajib when doubt arises about eligibility. If tahrri was omitted and the recipient is later proven poor, the zakat becomes valid because the goal (poverty) is achieved.

ان چیزوں کا علم ظن غالب کے طور پر ہوگا نہ کہ یقین کے طور پر کیونکہ یہ بات بہت دشوار ہے کہ قطعی طور پر کسی کی محتاجی معلوم کی جائے لہذا ان چیزوں میں حکم کی بنیاد اسی اجتہاد اور ظن غالب پر ہوگی جو اس کے نزدیک واقع ہو گا حتی کہ اگر اس کے نزدیک یہ اجتہاد واقع ہوا کہ یہ شخص فقیر ہے تو اس کو زکوۃ دینے سے خدا کے حکم کی اطاعت ہو گئی اور زکوۃ ادا ہو گئی اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے نماز پڑھنے والے پر جہت قبلہ مشتبہ ہو جائے پھر اس نے تحری کر کے نماز ادا کی تو اس کی نماز ادا ہوگئی اگر چہ بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ اس نے صحیح سمت کی طرف منہ کر کے نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے کیونکہ بنائے کا ر اس میں اجتہاد پر ہے نہ کہ یقین پر لہذا جس طرف تحری واقع ہوگئی اس طرف نماز ادا ہو جائے گی ، اسی طرح زکوۃ ادا ہوگئی اگر چہ بعد میں ظاہر ہوا کہ جس کو ز کو دی گئی ہے وہ زکوۃ کا مصرف نہیں تھا
حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ دینے کے بعد اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ جس کو ز کو ۃ دی گئی ہے وہ مالدار ہے تو زکوۃ ادا ہوگئی اعادہ کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر ظاہر ہوا کہ جس کو زکوۃ دی ہے وہ ہاشمی ہے یا کافر ہے یا اس کا باپ ہے یا اس کا بیٹا ہے تو زکوۃ ادا نہیں ہوئی بلکہ اس کا اعادہ ضروری ہے۔ اس رائے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غنی فی الجملہ زکوۃ کا مصرف ہے جیسے عامل اور سائی کہ مالدار ہونے کے باوجود اس کو زکوۃ کے مال سے دینا جائز ہے لیکن ہاشمی کا فرمز کی زکو پینے وال کلاب اور اس کا بیٹا اس کی زکوۃ کا قطعا مصرف نہیں ہے اس لئے مالدار کو فقیر سمجھ کر اگر زکوۃ دیدی تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی کیونکہ مالدار فی الجملہ زکوۃ کا مصرف ہوتا ہے اور باقی صورتوں میں زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی کیونکہ ہاشمی اور کافر وغیرہ کسی حال میں بھی زکوۃ کا مصرف نہیں ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ظاہر الروایۃ قول اول ہی ہے یعنی تمام صورتوں میں زکوۃ ادا ہو گئی جبکہ اس نے مصرف سمجھ کر ز کوۃ دی ہو۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ غیر مصرف میں زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کا ادا ہونا اس وقت ہے جبکہ زکوۃ دینے والے نے تحری کر کے زکوۃ دی اور اس کا غالب گمان یہ ہو کہ یہ شخص زکوۃ کا مصرف ہے اور اگر مز کی کو شک ہوا کہ وہ مصرف زکوۃ ہے یا نہیں لیکن اس کے باوجود تحری نہیں کی بلکہ بغیر تحری کے اس کو زکوۃ دیدی یا تحری کر کے زکوۃ دی اور ظن غالب یہ تھا کہ یہ زکوۃ کا مصرف نہیں ہے تو ان دونوں
صورتوں میں زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی ہاں اگر بعد میں ظاہر ہوا کہ جس کوز کو قوی ہے وہ فقیر ہے تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی اور یہی صحیح قول ہے۔ فوائد صاحب عنایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ کی چار صورتیں ہیں کیونکہ زکوۃ دینے والے نے اپنے مال کی زکوۃ بغیر شک اور بغیر تحری کے دی ہے یا اس نے زکوۃ لینے والے کے حال میں شک کیا ہے پہلی صورت میں زکوۃ ادا ہو گئی الا یہ کہ زکوۃ لینے والے کا غنی ہونا ظاہر ہو جائے کیونکہ اصل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ کے مال پر قبضہ کرنے والا فقیر ہو۔ اور دوسری صورت میں پھر دوصورتیں ہیں کیونکہ مزکی نے تحری کی ہوگی یا تحری نہیں کی ہوگی اگر تحری نہیں کی تو زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی۔
ہاں اگر یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ جس کو بغیر تحری کے زکوۃ دی ہے وہ فقیر ہے تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی کیونکہ جب مزکی کو زکوۃ لینے والے کے معاملہ میں شک ہوا تو اس پر تحری کرنا واجب ہو گیا پس جب اس نے واجب ہونے کے بعد تحری ترک کر دی تو فریضہ زکوۃ جو ادا کیا گیا ہے وہ ادا نہ ہوگا ۔ جیسے اگر مصلی کو جہت قبلہ میں شک ہو گیا تو مصلی پر تحری واجب ہے پس اگر بغیر تحری کے نماز ادا کی تو نماز ادا نہ ہوگی ہاں اگر یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ وہ فقیر ہے تو زکوۃ ادا ہو گئی کیونکہ زکوۃ ادا کرنے میں فقر ہی مقصود ہے اور وہ بغیر تحری کے حاصل ہو گیا جیسے سعی الی الجمعہ فرض ہے لیکن اگر بغیر سعی کے نماز جمعہ ادا کی گئی تو نماز جمعہ ادا ہو جائے گی جیسے جامع مسجد میں اعتکاف کرنے والا بغیر سعی الی الجمعہ کے جمعہ پڑھتا ہے کیونکہ مقصود تو نماز جمعہ ہے نہ کہ سعی الی الجمعۃ اور اگر تحری کر کے زکوۃ دی تو
اس کی بھی دوصورتیں ہیں یا تو ظن غالب یہ ہوگا کہ جس کو زکوۃ دی گئی ہے وہ زکوۃ کا مصرف ہے یا مصرف نہ ہونے کا ظن غالب ہوگا اگر دوسری صورت ہے تو زکوۃ ادا نہ ہوگی مگر یہ کہ بعد میں ظاہر ہوا کہ وہ جس کو غیر مصرف سمجھ کر ز کوۃ دی گئی ہے وہ فقیر ہے تو ادا ہو جائے گی اور اگر پہلی صورت ہے یعنی مصرف سمجھ کر زکوۃ دی ہے اور بعد میں ظاہر ہوا کہ وہ شخص واقعتا مصرف ہے یا کچھ ظاہر نہیں ہوا تو بالا تفاق جائز ہے اور اگر بعد میں غنی ہونا یعنی غیر مصرف ہونا ظاہر ہوا تو طرفین کے نزدیک جائز ہے اور یہی ابو یوسف کا پہلا قول ہے اور امام ابو یوسف کا دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ ادا نہیں ہوئی اس پر اعادہ لازم ہے۔
Knowledge of these things will be based on predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann), not certainty, because it is very difficult to know someone's need definitively. Therefore, rulings in these matters are based on ijtihad and predominant conjecture that occurs to him. Even if his ijtihad is that this person is poor, then giving him zakat fulfills God's command and the zakat is discharged. This is like the case of a person praying who becomes uncertain about the direction of the qibla, then he makes tahrri (estimation) and prays; his prayer is valid even if later it becomes known that he did not face the correct direction, because the foundation is on ijtihad, not certainty. So whichever direction his tahrri leads, his prayer is valid. Similarly, zakat is valid even if later it appears that the person given zakat was not a valid recipient. From Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration: If after giving zakat it appears that the recipient was wealthy, the zakat is valid and no repetition is needed. But if it appears he was a Hashimi, a disbeliever, his father, or his son, then zakat is not valid and repetition is necessary. The proof for this view is that a wealthy person is, in some respects, a valid recipient of zakat, like the collector (aamil) and the one who works (sa'i) — despite being wealthy, it is permissible to give them zakat funds. But a Hashimi, a disbeliever, and his son are absolutely not valid recipients. Therefore, if one gives zakat to a wealthy person thinking he is poor, the zakat is valid because the wealthy are valid recipients in some respects. In the other cases, zakat is not valid because Hashimi, disbeliever, etc., are not valid recipients under any circumstance. Sahib al-Hidayah says that the view of Zahir al-Riwaya is the first saying, i.e., in all cases zakat is valid if the giver considered him a valid recipient. Sahib al-Hidayah says: The validity of zakat when given to an invalid recipient is only when the giver made tahrri and his predominant conjecture was that this person is a valid recipient. And if the giver had doubt whether the recipient is valid or not, but did not make tahrri and gave zakat without tahrri, or made tahrri and gave zakat while his predominant conjecture was that he is not a valid recipient, then in these two cases zakat is not valid. Yes, if later it appears that the recipient (who had doubt about) is poor, then zakat is valid. That is the correct saying. The author of al-Inayah says: This issue has four scenarios: either the giver gives zakat from his wealth without doubt and without tahrri, or he has doubt about the recipient's condition. In the first scenario, zakat is valid unless it becomes apparent that the recipient is wealthy, because the default is that the one who takes possession of zakat wealth is poor. In the second scenario, there are two sub-scenarios: the giver either performed tahrri or not. If he did not perform tahrri, zakat is not valid. However, if it becomes known that the person he gave zakat to without tahrri is poor, then zakat is valid. Because when the giver had doubt about the recipient's matter, tahrri became obligatory upon him. When he abandoned tahrri after it became obligatory, the obligatory zakat he gave is not valid. Just as if the worshipper has doubt about the direction of the qibla, then tahrri is obligatory on him; if he prays without tahrri, the prayer is not valid. But if it becomes known that he is poor, zakat is valid because the goal in paying zakat is poverty itself, and it was achieved without tahrri. Like the obligation to go to Friday prayer: if one prays Jumu'ah without going, the prayer is valid, like the one in i'tikaf in the congregational mosque who prays Jumu'ah without going, because the goal is the Friday prayer, not the going. And if he gives zakat after tahrri, then there are two possibilities: either his predominant conjecture is that the recipient is a valid recipient or that he is not. If the latter, zakat is not valid unless it becomes known that the person he considered invalid is actually poor. If the former (i.e., he considered him a valid recipient and gave zakat), and later it appears that the person was indeed a valid recipient or nothing appears, then it is valid by agreement. And if later it appears that he is wealthy (i.e., an invalid recipient), then it is valid according to both (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's first view). This is Abu Yusuf's first view. And Imam Abu Yusuf's second view is that zakat is not valid and repetition is necessary.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah, discusses the validity of zakat when the payer exercises ijtihad (independent reasoning) to determine eligibility, and later discovers the recipient was actually ineligible. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute, expanding on a ruling with comparative analysis. The author begins by establishing the principle: in matters of zakat distribution, the obligation is based on predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann), not certainty, because it is nearly impossible to know definitively whether someone is poor. This is analogous to ijtihad for the qibla direction in prayer: if a worshipper makes tahrri (estimation of the qibla direction) and prays, the prayer is valid even if later proven wrong, because the basis is ijtihad, not certainty. Similarly, if the zakat payer makes ijtihad and gives zakat to someone he believes is a valid recipient, the zakat is valid even if later it becomes clear the recipient was not eligible. However, there is a difference of narration from Imam Abu Hanifa. In one narration, he distinguishes between types of ineligibility: if the recipient turns out to be wealthy (ghani), the zakat is valid because a wealthy person can sometimes be a zakat recipient (e.g., the 'aamil or collector). But if the recipient turns out to be a Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet), a disbeliever, the payer's father, or his son, then zakat is not valid and must be repeated, because these individuals are never eligible to receive zakat under any circumstances. The proof (dalil) for this distinction is that while wealth does not absolutely prevent zakat eligibility (as in the case of the 'aamil), Hashimi, kafir, and direct ascendants/descendants are permanently excluded. But Sahib al-Hidayah (the author of the original Hidayah) states that the relied-upon position in Zahir al-Riwaya is the first view: in all cases, zakat is valid if the payer considered the recipient eligible at the time of payment. The commentary then elaborates on the conditions for validity. The payer must have performed tahrri (investigation) and must have predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) that the recipient is eligible. If the payer had doubt but gave without tahrri, or if he performed tahrri but his predominant conjecture was that the recipient was ineligible, then zakat is not valid—unless it later becomes known that the recipient was indeed poor, in which case the zakat is valid because the goal (poverty) was achieved. The commentator (likely from al-Inayah) breaks the issue into four scenarios: 1) Payer gives without doubt and without tahrri: zakat valid unless recipient is wealthy (default assumption is poverty). 2) Payer doubts and does not perform tahrri: zakat invalid unless recipient is later found poor. 3) Payer doubts, performs tahrri, and his predominant conjecture is eligibility: zakat valid even if recipient is wealthy later. 4) Payer doubts, performs tahrri, and predominant conjecture is ineligibility: zakat invalid, but if later recipient is found poor, zakat becomes valid. This detailed taxonomy shows the Hanafi school's nuanced approach to balancing practical necessity (the difficulty of certainty) with legal requirements. The passage notes that the first view (all cases valid with ijtihad) is the mufta bihi (the position for fatwa).

Key Terms
تحری (tahrri): Effort or investigation to determine the correct ruling or status through ijtihad when there is doubt
ظن غالب (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant conjecture or strong probability that indicates the likely truth, less than certainty but more than doubt
مصرف (masrif): Category of people eligible to receive zakat (e.g., poor, destitute, collectors, etc.)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwaya), if a person gives zakat after ijtihad and later discovers the recipient was his son, what is the ruling?
A) Zakat is invalid and must be repeated
B) Zakat is valid and no repetition is needed
C) Zakat is valid only if the son was poor
D) Zakat is invalid but no repetition is needed

Key Takeaway
Zakat is valid if the payer made ijtihad and had predominant conjecture of eligibility, even if later proven wrong; the relied Hanafi position does not distinguish between types of ineligibility.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate

Paying Zakat to One's Own Slave or Mukatab
Ruling on giving zakat to one's own slave or mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on giving zakat to one's own slave or mukatab and explain why it is invalid using the concept of tamlik and ownership capacity.

Core Idea
Zakat requires complete transfer of ownership; giving to one's own slave or mukatab fails this pillar.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario from al-Hidayah: a person gives zakat to someone, only to discover later that the recipient was his own slave or mukatab. The ruling may seem counterintuitive, but the legal reasoning rooted in the pillar of tamlik (transfer of ownership) clarifies why the payment is invalid and must be repeated. Understanding this case reinforces the fundamental condition that zakat recipients must have full capacity to own property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Giving zakat to one's own slave or mukatab. The ruling is that it is invalid (la yujzihi).
This applies regardless of the giver's knowledge at the time of payment.
2
Locate the dalil and the 'illa
The proof is qiyas (rational analogy) based on the capacity to own. The 'illa is the absence or deficiency of complete tamlik due to the recipient's lack of full ownership capacity.
Tamlik is the rukn (pillar) of zakat payment.
3
Understand the distinction between slave and mukatab
A slave has no capacity to own anything, so tamlik is completely absent. A mukatab can own property, but his person (raqabah) is still owned by the master, resulting in deficient tamlik.
Complete tamlik is required; deficient tamlik does not suffice.
4
Note the consequence
The zakat payment is batil (invalid) and must be repeated with an eligible recipient.
Ignorance of the recipient's status does not excuse the invalidity.

Source Text

وَلَوْ دَفَعَ إِلى شَخْصٍ ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ عَبْدُهُ أَو مُكَاتِبُهُ لَا يُجْزِيْهِ لِانْعِدَامِ التَّمْلِيْكَ لِعَدَمِ أَهْلِيَّةِ المُلْكِ وَهُوَ الرُّكُنُ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ
translation and explanation: ایک شخص کو ز کوۃ دی پھر وہ اسکا غلام یا مکاتب نکلا تو زکوۃ دوبارہ دے
translation urdu: ترجمہ اور اگر کسی کو زکوۃ دیدی پھر معلوم ہوا کہ وہ اس کا غلام ہے یا اس کا مکاتب ہے تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ ملک کی لیاقت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تملیک معدوم ہوگئی حالانکہ تملیک رکن ہے چنانچہ گذرا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہی کہ کسی آدمی نے بغیر شناخت کے ایک شخص کو زکوۃ دی پھر معلوم ہوا کہ جس کو زکوۃ دی ہے وہ اس کا غلام ہے یا اس کا مکاتب ہے تو اس کی بیہز کو ۃ ادا نہ ہوگی کیونکہ غلام کے اندر ملک ہونے کی اہلیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تملیک بالکل نہیں پائی گئی حالانکہ ادائے زکوۃ کارکن ہی تملیک (مالک کرنا ہے۔ اور مکاتب چونکہ رقبہ مملوک ہے اگر چہ پدا آزاد ہے پس ایک اعتبار سے مکاتب اور اس کے مال کا مولیٰ ہی مالک ہے اس لئے اپنے مکاتب کو زکوۃ دینے میں تملیک تو پائی گئی مگر ناقص تملیک پائی گئی حالانکہ ادائے زکوۃار کن کامل تملیک ہے نہ کہ ناقص تملیک ۔
And if he paid to a person, then later knew that he was his slave or his mukatab, it is not sufficient (la yujzihi) because tamlik (transfer of ownership) is absent due to the lack of capacity for ownership (ahliyyat al-milk), and tamlik is the pillar (rukn) as previously mentioned. [Then the Urdu translation]: If he gave zakat to someone, then it turned out that person is his slave or his mukatab, then zakat must be given again. The translation: And if he gave zakat to someone, then later knew that he was his slave or his mukatab, then this is not valid because due to the lack of capacity for ownership, tamlik is absent, whereas tamlik is the pillar (rukn), as has passed. Explanation: The issue is that a person gave zakat to someone without knowing, then it became known that the recipient was his slave or his mukatab; his zakat is not valid because for a slave, due to lack of capacity for ownership, tamlik is completely absent, whereas the pillar of zakat payment is tamlik (making someone owner). And as for the mukatab, although his earnings are for himself, his person (raqabah) is owned; thus, in one respect, the master is the owner of the mukatab and his wealth. Therefore, giving zakat to one's own mukatab involves tamlik, but it is deficient tamlik, whereas the pillar of zakat payment is complete tamlik, not deficient tamlik.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling with its legal reasoning. The type is a ruling with proof (proof by rational argument). The matn from al-Hidayah states: If a person gives zakat to someone and later discovers that recipient is his own slave or mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom), the zakat is not valid (la yujzihi). The reason ('illa) given is that tamlik (transfer of ownership) is absent because the slave lacks the legal capacity to own property (ahliyyat al-milk) — the slave himself is owned, so he cannot own property independently. Tamlik is the essential pillar (rukn) of zakat payment, as established earlier in the book. The commentary expands: For a slave, there is no valid tamlik at all because he cannot own property; therefore, the intended transfer of ownership fails completely. For a mukatab, the situation is nuanced. The mukatab is a slave who has a contract to earn and purchase his freedom. While his earnings are for himself (he can own property to pay his kitabah), his physical person (raqabah) remains owned by the master. So from one perspective, the master is the owner of the mukatab and his wealth. Therefore, giving zakat to one's own mukatab does involve tamlik, but it is deficient (naqis) tamlik. The pillar of zakat requires complete (kamil) tamlik, not deficient, so it is not valid. This ruling applies even if the giver did not know the recipient was his slave or mukatab at the time of payment; the discovery after the fact invalidates the payment. The key takeaway is that zakat must transfer ownership to a free, eligible recipient. A slave is completely ineligible, and a mukatab is ineligible because the master retains ownership over his person, making the transfer incomplete.

Key Terms
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership to the recipient; the essential pillar of zakat payment
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract (kitabah) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments; he can earn and own property but his person is still owned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is zakat invalid when given to one's own mukatab?
A) The mukatab is not Muslim
B) The mukatab is considered wealthy
C) The tamlik is deficient because the master retains ownership of the mukatab's person
D) The mukatab is a direct descendant

Key Takeaway
Zakat must involve complete transfer of ownership to a free eligible recipient; giving to one's own slave or mukatab is invalid because tamlik is absent or deficient.

Giving Zakat to a Nisab Owner: The Ruling and Its Exception
Ruling with explanatory commentary on giving zakat to nisab owners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to a nisab owner, distinguishing between surplus wealth and basic needs assets.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot be given to a nisab owner unless the nisab is not surplus to basic needs.

This lesson examines the Hanafi prohibition on giving zakat to someone who owns a nisab (minimum threshold of wealth). The key is understanding that being 'wealthy' in Islamic law means having surplus assets beyond essential needs. Even if a person's total assets reach the nisab, if those assets are necessary for daily life or profession (like a scholar's books), they are not counted as surplus, and zakat may be given. This nuance prevents injustice and ensures zakat reaches the truly needy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
Read the first sentence: 'And it is not permissible to give zakat to someone who owns a nisab...' Determine the hukm (ruling) for giving zakat to a nisab owner. It is haram if done intentionally and the payment is invalid.
The ruling applies to any type of wealth: gold, silver, livestock, trade goods, etc.
2
Understand the Legal Basis
The text states 'because legal wealth (ghina al-shar'i) is measured by it.' Analyze why nisab is used as the benchmark for being wealthy. This is a form of ta'lil (reasoning).
The underlying principle is that zakat is for the poor; the nisab defines the poverty line.
3
Apply the Condition of Surplus
Identify the condition mentioned: 'the condition is that it (the wealth) be surplus to basic needs (hajat asliyya).' Understand that the nisab must be from wealth not needed for essential living.
Basic needs include food, clothing, shelter, tools of trade, books for scholars, debts, etc.
4
Recognize the Exception
Read the example of a scholar with books worth a nisab. The commentary explains that because the books are necessary for teaching, they are not surplus, so the scholar can receive zakat. Generalize: any essential asset does not count toward the nisab for eligibility.
This is an important practical exception: not every nisab owner is automatically prohibited from receiving zakat.
5
Distinguish from Payer's Obligation
Notice the final part: 'And growth (nama') is only a condition for the obligation (of zakat upon the payer).' Understand that the conditions for paying zakat (like nisab being productive) are separate from conditions for receiving zakat.
For the receiver, the key is lack of surplus nisab, not whether the payer's wealth grows.

And it is not permissible to give zakat to someone who owns a nisab (a minimum amount of wealth) from any type of property, because legal wealth (ghina al-shar'i) is measured by it. And the condition is that it (the wealth) be surplus to basic needs (hajat asliyya). And growth (nama') is only a condition for the obligation (of zakat upon the payer). [Urdu translation and explanation]: And it is not permissible to give zakat to that person who owns a nisab, be it from gold, silver, animals, or other goods — whether the wealth is productive or not, provided it is surplus to basic needs. Basic needs include debts due on him or necessary items for use. For example, if a scholar owns books worth a nisab but he needs them for teaching and studying, then it is permissible for him to receive zakat because although he owns a nisab, it is not surplus to basic needs. Therefore, it is correct for him to take zakat. And as for giving zakat to a nisab-owner...
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Hidayah with commentary. It establishes the prohibition of giving zakat to a person who owns a nisab (the minimum amount of wealth that makes one subject to zakat as a payer). The ruling is explicit: it is not permissible (la yajuz) to give zakat to such a person. The reasoning (ta'lil) provided: legal wealth (ghina al-shar'i) is determined by the nisab threshold. The condition for zakat eligibility (being a recipient) is that the recipient's wealth, after deducting basic needs (hajat asliyya), is less than a nisab. In other words, a person who owns a nisab's worth of surplus wealth is considered wealthy and cannot receive zakat. The commentary clarifies that the nisab can be of any type of property: gold, silver, livestock, trade goods, etc. The wealth may be productive (nami) or non-productive; it's still considered wealth. However, an important exception is mentioned: if the wealth is needed for basic needs (hajat asliyya), such as books for a scholar or a house for residence, then even if its value reaches a nisab, it does not make the person wealthy, because it is not surplus. Therefore, such a person may receive zakat. The passage ends abruptly but covers the core ruling. The key principle: assets that are essential for one's livelihood or profession are not counted as wealth for the purpose of zakat eligibility.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat on the owner; also the threshold above which a person is considered wealthy and cannot receive zakat.
حاجت اصلیہ (hajat asliyya): Basic or essential needs: items necessary for daily living and profession, such as food, clothing, shelter, tools of trade, books for scholars, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The wealth must be surplus to basic needs
C) The recipient must be a scholar or student
D) The nisab must be from gold or silver

Key Takeaway
A nisab-owner may receive zakat only if the assets are essential for basic needs (hajat asliyya), thus not surplus wealth.

Giving Zakat to an Owner of Nisab: The Hanafi Rule
Ruling that a nisab-owner cannot receive zakat, with reasoning and exception for basic needs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to a person who owns nisab and explain the distinction between conditions for receiving and conditions for paying zakat.

Core Idea
A person who owns nisab, even if non-productive, cannot receive zakat because legal wealth is defined by nisab, not by zakat obligation.

This lesson examines the ruling that a person who owns a nisab (minimum zakatable threshold) cannot receive zakat, even if that wealth is not growing (ghayr nami). The source explains the reasoning based on the Shari’i definition of wealth and the condition of surplus to basic needs. It also clarifies a common confusion: that growth (nama’) is a condition for the obligation of zakat, not for the prohibition of receiving it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the hukm: is it permissible to give zakat to a person who owns nisab?
The text says 'لا يجوز' — it is not permissible.
2
Determine the Legal Basis
Why is it impermissible? Because legal wealth (ghina shar‘i) is tied to ownership of nisab, not to productivity.
The condition for receiving is that one's surplus wealth be below nisab.
3
Distinguish Between Conditions
Separate the condition for receiving (not owning nisab surplus to basic needs) from the condition for paying (growth and havlan al-hawl). Growth is relevant only for the obligation to pay, not for eligibility to receive.
Thus a non-productive nisab owner is still considered wealthy.
4
Apply the Exception: Basic Needs
If the nisab is absorbed by basic needs (e.g., a scholar's essential books, debt), the person is not considered 'wealthy' and may receive zakat.
Basic needs (hajat asliyyah) include necessary tools, debts, and essential items.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is not permissible to pay zakat to one who owns a nisab of any property whatsoever, because legal wealth is determined by it, and the condition [for being a recipient] is that [the property] be surplus to basic needs, and growth is only a condition for obligation [of zakat]. Translation: And it is not permissible to give zakat to a person who owns a nisab, of any kind of property, because legal wealth is measured by it, and the condition is that it be surplus to basic needs, and growth is a condition for obligation. Explanation: The issue is that if a person owns the amount of nisab, whether it be the nisab of gold and silver, or of animals, or of other goods, whether this wealth is productive or non-productive, provided it is surplus to basic needs, then giving zakat to him is not permissible. Basic needs include, for example, if he owes a debt to someone, or if he needs it for use—for instance, if a scholar owns books whose value amounts to nisab, but he needs these books and they are used for teaching and learning, then it is permissible for that scholar to take zakat, because although he owns nisab, this nisab is not surplus to basic needs; therefore taking zakat for him is correct. As for why the condition of nisab being productive is not stipulated for the impermissibility of giving zakat to a nisab-owner, the answer is that the growth of wealth is a condition for zakat being obligatory, not for the impermissibility of receiving zakat. So if a person owns a non-productive nisab, zakat is not obligatory upon him, but since in the view of Shariah he is wealthy, it is not permissible for him to take zakat.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that a person who owns a nisab (the minimum threshold of wealth subject to zakat) cannot receive zakat, even if the wealth is not growing (ghayr nami). The reasoning is based on the Shariah's definition of wealth (ghina). The condition for being a zakat recipient is that the person's surplus wealth (above basic needs) falls short of nisab. Basic needs (hajat asliyyah) include debts and essential items like books for a scholar. Even if a person owns nisab, if it is absorbed by basic needs, he is still eligible. The passage then addresses a potential question: why is the condition of growth (nama') not required to deem a nisab-owner ineligible? The answer clarifies that growth is a condition for the obligation of zakat (wujub), not for the prohibition of receiving zakat. Therefore, a person with a non-growing nisab is not required to pay zakat, but he is still considered wealthy in the Shariah's estimation, so he cannot receive zakat. This is a crucial distinction: the criteria for giving zakat are different from the criteria for receiving zakat.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory on its owner and also defines legal wealth; generally 85g of gold or 595g of silver or equivalent.
نامی (nami): Wealth that grows or yields profit (e.g., business assets, livestock); opposite of ghayr nami (non-productive).
حاجت اصلیہ (hajat asliyyah): Basic essential needs of a person, such as debt payment, food, clothing, and tools of trade/learning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because the nisab is non-productive so he is not considered wealthy.
B) Yes, because zakat is not obligatory on him.
C) No, because ownership of nisab defines legal wealth regardless of productivity.
D) No, because only the poor can receive zakat.

Key Takeaway
Ownership of nisab, regardless of productivity, prohibits receiving zakat unless the nisab is absorbed by basic needs.

Giving Zakat to a Healthy Earner with Less than Nisab is Permissible; Dispute with Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on zakat eligibility of healthy earner with less than nisab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to a healthy earner with less than nisab, explain the Hanafi proof involving the principle of amr khafi, and evaluate the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
Zakat is given based on visible poverty (lack of nisab), not hidden need.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can a healthy, able-bodied person who owns less than nisab receive zakat? The Hanafi position permits it, using a fundamental usul principle: when the underlying cause (need) is hidden, the ruling is attached to its manifest evidence (lack of nisab). We will unpack the Hanafi argument, the Shafi'i objection, and the Hanafi rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the specific ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz) to give zakat to a healthy earner who has less than nisab. The key condition is that the recipient must be faqir in the Shari'ah sense (i.e., does not own nisab).
Hanafis define faqir solely based on nisab ownership, not earning ability.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it is not permissible to give zakat to a healthy earner, even if he has less than nisab, because he can work to earn his livelihood.
The Shafi'i position is based on the hadith prohibiting charity for the strong and capable.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school relies on the hadith: 'La tahillu al-sadaqatu li-ghaniyyin wa la li-dhi marrah sawiyyah' (Charity is not permissible for the wealthy nor for the strong and capable). The key phrase is 'dhi marrah sawiyyah', referring to a person with strength and capability.
This hadith is the primary textual evidence for the Shafi'i view.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: first, they re-interpret the hadith to refer to the prohibition of asking (su'al), not giving. This is supported by another hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) refused to give to strong men but offered to give if they insisted. Second, they invoke the usul principle that a hidden cause (need) is substituted by its manifest evidence (lack of nisab).
The Hanafi response shows careful textual analysis and application of usul principles.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis allow giving zakat to a healthy but asset-poor earner; Shafi'is do not, requiring such a person to work for their living. This affects real-world zakat distribution, especially among able-bodied poor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ يَجُوزُ دَفَعُهَا إِلى مَنْ يَّمْلِكُ أَقَلَّ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَإِنْ كَانَ صَحِيحًا مُكْتَسِبًا لأنَّهُ فَقِيرُ وَالْفُقَرَاءُ هُمُ الْمَصَارِفُ وَلأنَّ حَقِيقَة الْحَاجَةِ لَا يُوقَفُ عَلَيْهَا فَأدِيرَ الْحُكْمُ عَلَى دَلِيلِهَا وَهُوَ فَقَدُ النِّصَابِ ترجمہ اور ایسے شخص کوزکوۃ دینا جائز ہے جو اس سے کم کا مالک ہوا اگر چہ وہ شخص تندرست کمانے والا ہوں۔ کیونکہ وہ فقیر ہے اور فقراء ہی زکوۃ کے مصارف ہیں اور اس لئے کہ حقیقی محتاجی پر تو مطلع ہو نہیں سکتا اس وجہ سے حکم اس کی دلیل پر دائر کیا گیا ہے اور وہ نصاب کا مفقود ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک جو شخص نصاب سے کم کا مالک ہو اگر سوى يعنى صدقہ مالدار اور توانا جسم والے کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو شخص نصاب کا مالک نہ ہو شریعت کی نظر میں وہ فقیر شمار ہے ہفنی شمار نہیں ہوتا۔ اور زکوۃ کے مصرف فقراء ہی ہوتے ہیں پس جب یہ شخص شرعا فقیر ہے تو اس کو زکوۃ دینا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حقیقت فقر اور احتیاج پر واقف ہونا تو انتہائی دشوار کام ہے کیونکہ فقر اور احتیاج امرخفی ہیں۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی امر مخفی ہو تو اس کی دلیل کو اس کے قائم مقام قرار دیکر حکم اس کی دلیل پر لگا دیا جاتا ہے جیسے انزال موجب غسل ہے لیکن اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی کی ساتھ جماع کیا حتی کہ دخول بھی پایا گیا مگر انزال نہیں ہوا تو اس صورت میں بھی التقاء ختانین کو انزال کے قائم مقام قرار یکر اس پر وجوب غسل کا حکم لگا دیا جائے گا اور جیسے کسی نے اپنی دلہن سے کہا ان کنتن تحبینی فانت طالق اس نے جواب میں کہا حبک یعنی اگر تو مجھ سے محبت کرے گی تو تجھ کو طلاق ہے اس نے کہا کہ میں آپ سے محبت کرتی ہوں تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی کیونکہ نبت ایک مخفی چیز ہے لہذا اس کے قول احبک کو قائم مقام قرار دیکر اس پر حکم لگا دیا گیا اسی طرح فقر ام مخفی ہے لیکن اس کی دلیل یعنی ساب کا ہونا امرظاہر ہے اس لئے اس کو فقر کے قائم مقام قرار دیکر کہا جائے گا کہ جو شخص نصاب کا مالک نہ ہو وہ فقیر ہے اور فقیر کوز کو دینا ائز ہے لہذا اس کو بھی زکوۃ دینا جائز ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث میں حرمت سوال مراد ہے یعنی جو شخص تو انا تندرست قادر ما الکتب ہو اس کے لئے سوال کرنا اور مانگنا حلال نہیں ہے اور اس کی تائید اس حدیث سے ہوتی ہے کہ اُنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ لَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يُقَسِمُ الصَّدَقَاتِ فَقَامَ إِلَيْهِ رَجُلَانِ يَسْأَلَائِهِ فَنَظَرَ إِلَيْهِمَا وَرَآهُمَا جَلْدَيْنِ فَقَالَ إِنَّهُ لَاحَقِّ لَكُمَا فِيهِ ن شِئْتُمَا أعطيتُكُمَا یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم صدقات تقسیم فرما رہے تھے کہ دو آدمی کھڑے ہو کر مانگنے لگے آپ نے ان دونوں پر نظر ڈالی تو یکھا کہ دونوں طاقتور اور بے کئے ہیں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تم دونوں کا اس میں کوئی حق نہیں ہے اور اگر تم چاہو تو میں تم کو دیدوں گا۔ اس
And it is permissible to give it to one who owns less than that, even if he is healthy and earning, because he is poor, and the poor are the recipients [of zakat], and because the reality of need cannot be known, so the ruling is attached to its evidence, which is the lack of nisab. Translation: And it is permissible to give zakat to a person who owns less than that (i.e., less than nisab), even if he is a healthy earner, because he is poor, and the poor are the recipients of zakat, and because the true state of need cannot be known, thus the ruling is based on its evidence, which is the absence of nisab. Explanation: According to us, a person who owns less than nisab, even if he is healthy and earning, may receive zakat. Imam Shafi'i holds it is not permissible. Shafi'i's proof: The Prophet (PBUH) said, 'Sadaqah is not permissible for the wealthy nor for the one who is strong and capable.' Our proof: A person who does not own nisab is considered poor by Shariah, not wealthy. And the recipients of zakat are the poor. So when this person is poor by Shariah, giving zakat to him is permissible. Second proof: The reality of poverty and need is difficult to ascertain, as poverty and need are hidden matters. The legal principle is that if a matter is hidden, its evidence is substituted for it, and the ruling is attached to that evidence. For example, ejaculation necessitates ghusl, but if a man has intercourse with his wife and penetrates but no ejaculation occurs, the meeting of the circumcised parts is substituted for ejaculation and ghusl becomes obligatory. Similarly, if a man says to his wife, 'If you love me, you are divorced,' and she replies 'I love you,' divorce occurs because love is hidden; her statement is substituted. Similarly, poverty is hidden, but its evidence—lack of nisab—is apparent; so it is substituted, and one who lacks nisab is considered poor, and giving zakat to a poor person is permissible. The response to the hadith presented by Shafi'i is that it refers to the prohibition of asking (su'al), i.e., a person who is healthy and capable should not ask for charity. This is supported by the hadith that the Prophet (PBUH) was distributing sadaqat when two men stood asking; he looked at them and saw they were strong, so he said, 'You have no right to it; if you wish, I will give you [something]...'
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage presents a significant inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the eligibility of a healthy earner with less than nisab to receive zakat. The Hanafi position, as stated, is clear: it is permissible to give zakat to such a person. The reasoning is twofold. First, in Shariah, the criterion for being poor (faqir) is not having nisab, not the ability to earn. A healthy earner who currently has less than nisab is legally poor, and the Quranic recipients of zakat are the poor (fuqara'). Second, since actual need (haqiqah al-hajat) is hidden and difficult to ascertain, Shariah uses a visible evidence (dalil) for it, which is the lack of nisab. This is a well-established legal principle (qa'idah) in Hanafi usul: when the underlying cause is hidden, the ruling is tied to its manifest evidence. The passage provides two illustrative analogies: (1) ghusl being obligatory due to meeting of circumcised parts even without ejaculation, because ejaculation (the hidden cause) is replaced by its evidence; (2) divorce being triggered by a statement of love when the condition is love, because love is hidden and the statement stands in its place. The Shafi'i school relies on the hadith 'La tahillu al-sadaqatu li-ghaniyyin wa la li-dhi marrah sawiyyah' (Charity is not permissible for the wealthy nor for the one with strength). The Hanafi response is that this hadith refers to the prohibition of asking (su'al), not the prohibition of giving. The supporting hadith about the two strong men asking and being told they have no right (to ask) confirms this interpretation. Thus, the Hanafi school maintains that the zakat is permissible, and the Shafi'i argument is refuted by redirecting the hadith to the act of asking rather than receiving in general.

Key Terms
فقیر (faqir): A person who does not own nisab (the minimum threshold of wealth) after deducting basic needs; considered legally poor.
امر مخفی (amr khafi): A hidden matter whose true nature cannot be easily known (e.g., actual need or love); Shariah attaches ruling to its apparent evidence.
سوال (su'al): Asking for charity; the Hanafi interpretation restricts the hadith's prohibition to the act of asking, not receiving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it permissible to give zakat to a healthy earner who has less than nisab?
A) Because such a person is unable to work.
B) Because the Shariah defines poverty by lack of nisab, not earning ability.
C) Because the hadith on prohibition is weak.
D) Because the person must be supported by the state.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits giving zakat to a healthy earner with less than nisab, relying on the Shari'ah definition of poverty (lack of nisab) and the principle that hidden need is substituted by its manifest evidence.

Giving Zakat of Nisaab to One Person: Hanafi Ruling and Dispute
Ruling on giving zakat amount of nisaab to one person with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat of nisaab amount to one person and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
Giving zakat equal to nisaab to one person is valid but disliked because wealth follows payment.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in zakat distribution: the permissibility of giving a full nisaab (200 dirhams or more) to a single recipient. While the act is valid, it carries a degree of dislike (karahah) due to the immediate consequence of the recipient becoming wealthy. The Hanafi school features an internal disagreement: Imam Zufar argues the payment becomes invalid, while the majority view, supported by a key analogy, upholds validity with dislike.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the ruling as stated in the matn: it is disliked (makruh) to give 200 dirhams or more to one person, but if done, it is valid.
This is the position of Imam Muhammad and the majority of the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar holds it is invalid (la yajuz). Understand his reasoning: because the recipient becomes wealthy at the very moment of payment.
Imam Zufar is a Hanafi scholar known for strict analogy (qiyas).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Zufar argues that ghina (wealth) accompanies (qarana) the payment, making the payment go to a wealthy person, which is impermissible for zakat.
The key concept is 'qarana' – simultaneity.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority counters that ghina is the effect (hukm) of the payment, so it follows after the payment; the recipient is poor at the time of payment. They support this with an analogy to praying near filth.
The analogy: prayer near filth is valid but disliked – similarly, zakat near immediate wealth is valid but disliked.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: if Zufar's view were followed, the zakat would have to be given again. The majority view is that it is valid but makruh, and this is the mufta bihi (operative ruling).
Conditions such as the recipient having dependents or debt can remove the dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَكْرَهُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلى وَاحِدٍ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَمٍ فَصَاعِدًا وَإِنْ دَفَعَ جَازَ وَ قَالَ زُفَرُ لَا يَجُوزُ لأَنَّ الْغِنَى قَارَنَ الْأَدَاءَ فَحَصَلَ الْأَدَاءُ إِلَى الْغَنِي وَلَنَا إِنَّ الْغِنَى حُكْمُ الْآدَاءِ فَيَتَعَقَّبُهُ لَكِنَّهُ يُكْرَهُ لِقُرُبِ الْغِنَى مِنْهُ كَمَنْ صَلَّى وَ بِقُرْبِهِ نَجَاسَةٌ
And it is disliked to give to one person two hundred dirhams or more, but if he gives it is permissible. Zufar said: It is not permissible, because richness (becoming wealthy) accompanies the payment, so the payment is made to a rich person. Our proof is: Richness is a result of the payment, so it follows it, but it is disliked due to the closeness of richness (to the act), like someone who prays while near him is filth.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on giving zakat in an amount equal to or exceeding the nisaab (200 dirhams) to a single recipient. The Hanafi position, attributed to Imam Muhammad and mentioned in the text, is that it is makruh (disliked) but valid if done. Imam Zufar, a Hanafi scholar known for his strict analogies, holds it invalid because he argues that the recipient becomes wealthy at the very moment of payment, making the payment go to a wealthy person, which is impermissible. The Hanafi response is based on the principle that richness (ghina) is the hukm (result) of the payment, not concomitant; it occurs after the payment is complete. Therefore, the payment itself is directed to a poor person, and the zakat is valid. However, because richness follows immediately, the act is considered makruh tanzihan (disliked, not prohibited), analogous to praying near filth—the prayer is valid but disliked. The text also clarifies conditions: the ruling applies only if the recipient has no dependents and no debt. If the recipient has dependents, and dividing the amount among them would bring each to less than 200 dirhams, or if the recipient is indebted and paying the debt leaves him with less than 200 dirhams, then the dislike is removed.

Key Terms
الغنى (al-ghina): Richness, i.e., becoming the owner of nisaab (200 dirhams or equivalent) after receiving zakat.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; the act is valid but entails sin if done without necessity, and is closer to prohibition (makruh tahrimi) but here it is tanzihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving 200 dirhams of zakat to a single poor person?
A) It is invalid (batil)
B) It is valid but disliked (makruh)
C) It is obligatory to give more than 200 dirhams
D) It is only valid if the recipient has dependents

Key Takeaway
Giving zakat equal to nisaab to one person is valid but disliked because the recipient becomes wealthy immediately after payment; the majority Hanafi view holds, differing from Imam Zufar who considers it invalid.
