Obligation to Pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for Oneself
Stating the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr for oneself with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Sadaqat al-Fitr for oneself, identify its proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar, and explain why the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib rather than fard.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib upon every sahib-e-nisab for oneself, proven by the Prophet's explicit command.

The obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr is a key duty at the end of Ramadan. In this passage, al-Quduri states the ruling clearly, and the commentary provides the hadith proof. You will learn the legal ruling, its evidence, and the Hanafi classification.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its ruling
Identify that the act is paying Sadaqat al-Fitr for oneself. The ruling is wajib (obligatory).
The text says 'يَخْرُجُ لِكَ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ' – one pays for oneself.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar (radiyallahu anhuma) which mentions that the Prophet prescribed Zakat al-Fitr.
The full hadith is quoted in the commentary.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'فَرَضَ' (prescribed) is an explicit command indicating obligation. The list of categories (male, female, free, slave) shows universality.
In Hanafi usul, commands indicate obligation unless there is a contrary indicator.
4
Note the Hanafi classification
Despite the strong command, the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib, not fard, because the hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
Shafi'is classify it as fard due to the same hadith, showing the role of usul in deriving rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ يَخْرُجُ لِكَ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ لِحَدِيثِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فَرَضَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ زَكَوةَ الْفِطْرِ عَلَى الذَّكَرِ وَالانْتَى الْحَدِيثَ ترجمہ شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری نے کہا کہ اس صدقہ کو اپنی طرف سے نکالے کیونکہ ابن عمر کی حدیث ہے کہ فرمایا رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے مرد و عورت پر زکوۃ الفطر فرض کیا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ صاحب نصاب پر واجب ہے کہ وہ اپنی جان کا صدقہ ادا کرے دلیل ابن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما کی حدیث ہے پوری حدیث یہ ہے فَرَضَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ زَكوةَ الْفِطْرِ عَلَى الذَّكَرِ و الأنثى وَالْحَرِّ وَالْمَملوك صاعاً مِنْ تَمَر أَوْصَاعاً مِنْ شَعِيرٍ
He said: One pays [the Sadaqah] for oneself, due to the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah prescribed Zakat al-Fitr upon the male and the female' – the hadith. Translation: Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: One should pay this Sadaqah on behalf of oneself because the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar says that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made Zakat al-Fitr obligatory on men and women. Commentary: The issue is that it is obligatory upon a sahib-e-nisab to pay the Sadaqah of his own person. The proof is the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both). The complete hadith is: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prescribed Zakat al-Fitr upon the male and the female, the free and the slave: a sa‘ of dates or a sa‘ of barley.'
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn (al-Quduri's text) states: 'He said: One pays for oneself' – meaning the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr on behalf of one's own person. The commentary provides the hadith from Ibn ‘Umar as the proof. The complete hadith mentions that it is prescribed (farada) upon every male, female, free, and slave. In Hanafi terminology, this obligation is considered wajib (not fard) due to the nature of the evidence, but the hadith uses the word 'farada' which indicates a strong obligation. The Urdu commentary clarifies that it is wajib upon a sahib-e-nisab. The hadith specifically includes both genders and both free and slave, but for slaves, the master pays on their behalf (as explained later in the text).

Key Terms
زَكوةَ الْفِطْرِ (zakāt al-fiṭr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, also called Sadaqat al-Fitr. It is a type of purification.
صاع (ṣā‘): A unit of volume. For Sadaqat al-Fitr, it is usually defined as approximately 2.5 kg of wheat or dates, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar, on whom is Zakat al-Fitr prescribed?
A) Only on free men
B) On male, female, free, and slave
C) Only on those who own nisab
D) Only on those who fasted

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib on every sahib-e-nisab for themselves, proven by the Prophet's command in a sound hadith, and classified as wajib due to the ahad nature of the evidence.

Obligation to Pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for Minor Children
Ruling that the father pays Zakat al-Fitr for his minor children with legal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the cause and reasoning for the father's obligation to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his minor children and apply the same reasoning to analogous dependents.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib per dependent head; the father pays for minor children because he maintains them.

Sadaqat al-Fitr is an obligation tied to every person, but who pays for dependents? The Hanafi school clarifies that the father must pay for his minor children. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this ruling, focusing on the concept of the 'head' (ra's) and the analogy to one's own obligation. Understanding this chain of reasoning will help you see how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from linguistic clues and analogical thinking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the matn: 'And one pays for his minor children.' Identify the act and the ruling level. Note that the father (the one with nisab) is the subject.
2
Pinpoint the Cause (Sabab)
The commentary states the cause is a 'head' (ra's) that the person maintains and over whom he has guardianship. Locate the phrase 'لأن السبب رأس يَمُونُهُ وَيَلِي عَلَيْهِ'.
3
Understand the Linguistic Proof
The text uses the term 'زكوة الرأس' (Zakat of the head) to show that the obligation is attributed to the head. This attribution indicates that the head is the cause of obligation.
The term 'آمَارَة' (sign) in the text is likely a misspelling of 'علامة' (sign) or 'أَمَارَة' (indicator).
4
Trace the Analogy (Qiyas)
The original obligation is for one's own head, because one maintains and has guardianship over oneself. Minor children are analogous: the father maintains them and has guardianship over them, so they are attached to the ruling by qiyas.
'فيلحق به ما هو في معناه' – whatever is in its meaning is attached.
5
Apply the Multiplicity Principle
The obligation multiplies with the number of heads, even though the time is one. So the father pays for each minor child separately.
'فتتعدد بتعدد الرأس مع اتحاد اليوم'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ يَخْرُجُ عَنْ أَوْلَادِهِ الصِّغَارِ لأَنَّ السَّبَبِ رَأْسُ يَمُونُهُ وَيَلِى عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهَا تُضَافُ إِلَيْهِ يُقَالُ زَكَوةُ الرَّأْسِ وَهِيَ آمَارَةٌ السَّبَيَّةِ وَالْإِضَافَةُ إلَى الْفِطْرِ بِاعْتَبَارِ أَنَّهُ وَقْتُهَا وَلِهَذَا تَتَعَدَّدُ بِتَعَدُّدِ الرَّأْسِ مَعَ اتَّحَادِ الْيَوْمِ وَالْأَصْلُ فِي الْوُجُوبِ رَأْسُهُ وَهُوَ يَمُوتُهُ وَيَلِى عَلَيْهِ فَيَلْحَقُ بِه مَا هُوَ فِى مَعَاهُ كَا وَلَادِهِ الصَّغَارِ لِأَنَّهُ يَمُونُهُمْ وَيَلِى عَلَيْهِمْ
And one pays for his minor children, because the cause is a head that he maintains and over whom he has guardianship. Because it is attributed to him; it is said: 'Zakat of the head', and it is a sign of causality. And the attribution to 'Fitr' is because it is its time. Therefore, it multiplies with the multiplicity of heads even though the day is one. And the origin in obligation is his own head, and he maintains it and has guardianship over it. So whatever is in its meaning is attached to it, like his minor children, because he maintains them and has guardianship over them. Translation: The author says: And the one possessed of nisab pays Sadaqat al-Fitr on behalf of his minor children, because the cause of obligation is a head (dependent) whom he supports and over whom he has guardianship. For this reason, Sadaqat al-Fitr is attributed to the head (one says 'Zakat al-Ra's' – the zakat of the head). This attribution indicates that the head is the cause. The attribution to 'Fitr' is because it is the time. Thus, the obligation multiplies with the number of heads, even though the day is the same. The original obligation is for his own head, which he supports and over which he has guardianship. Therefore, everything that is analogous to it, such as his minor children, is attached, because he supports them and has guardianship over them.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr for minor children. The matn (Quduri's text) states 'And one pays for his minor children.' The commentary provides the reasoning: the cause (sabab) of obligation is the 'head' (ra's) – meaning a person whom one maintains and has guardianship over. The term 'zakat al-ra's' is used, where 'head' refers to the dependent person. Since the obligation is attached to each head that one supports, and minor children are dependent on the father for maintenance and guardianship, they are included. The commentary also clarifies that the obligation multiplies with the number of heads, even though the time (Eid al-Fitr) is one. The original obligation is for one's own head (oneself), and by analogy, the same applies to minor children under one's care.

Key Terms
رأس (ra's): Literally 'head', but used here to mean a person (a dependent) for whom Sadaqat al-Fitr is obligatory. The obligation is attached to each 'head' that one maintains.
سبب (sabab): The cause of obligation. Here, the cause is the existence of a 'head' (dependent) whom one maintains and has guardianship over.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the father pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his minor children according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the children are his property
B) Because he is their guardian and maintains them
C) Because the children have their own nisab
D) Because the children fasted

Key Takeaway
The father must pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for his minor children because they are dependent heads under his maintenance and guardianship, in qiyas to his own head.
